[F41A 9/58] Cartridge stops -- F41A 9/58 covers cartridge stops, devices that arrest or control the movement of cartridges during the feeding or loading of ammunition in small-arms and ordnance. It is applied to mechanisms that keep a round in a set position before firing or after extraction.
[F41A 9/59] Ejectors for clips or magazines, e.g. when empty -- F41A 9/59 covers devices that automatically expel empty ammunition clips or magazines from firearms, ensuring a clear chamber for reloading. These ejectors are part of the loading and feeding mechanisms used in small-arms and larger ordnance.
[F41A 9/60] Empty-cartridge-case or belt-link collectors or catchers -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridge stripping means in sprocket transporters -> F41A9/31 - Cartridge stripping means in reciprocating slide transporters -> F41A9/33 - Magazines for belted ammunition having provision for collecting belt links or empty cartridge cases -> F41A9/81
[F41A 9/61] Magazines -- F41A 9/61 relates to magazines, the devices that store, transport and feed ammunition to small arms or ordnance during operation. It covers the mechanical arrangements for holding rounds and supplying them to the weapon's chamber, including detachable, fixed, drum or box types.
[F41A 9/62] having means for indicating the number of cartridges left in the magazine, e.g. last-round indicators -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Charge condition indicator -> F41A9/53 - Last round safeties -> F41A17/40
[F41A 9/63] specially adapted for releasable connection with other magazines -- The F41A 9/63 subclass covers ammunition-feeding mechanisms that are specifically designed to allow a magazine to be detached and reattached to another magazine, enabling quick replacement or linking of magazines for small arms or ordnance. It relates to functional features common to weapons where the loading system includes a releasable connection between magazines.
[F41A 9/64] for unbelted ammunition -- F41A 9/64 covers mechanisms for feeding or loading ammunition that is not carried on a belt, such as magazines, clips, or loose rounds, in small-arms or larger ordnance. It pertains to functional features that enable the introduction of unbelted ammunition into the weapon's firing chamber.
[F41A 9/65] Box magazines having a cartridge follower -- A box magazine equipped with a cartridge follower uses a spring-biased plate to push ammunition upward, ensuring each round is positioned for reliable feeding into the weapon's chamber. This design simplifies loading and provides consistent ammunition pressure, improving the function of small-arms and larger ordnance that rely on magazine-fed operation.
[F41A 9/66] Arrangements thereon for charging, i.e. reloading -- The code F41A 9/66 covers the specific arrangements on firearms or artillery that provide the charging or reloading function, such as mechanisms that deliver ammunition into the chamber, feed devices, or other structural features that enable the weapon to be rapidly reloaded.
[F41A 9/67] having means for depressing the cartridge follower, or for locking it in a depressed position -- The CPC subclass F41A 9/67 falls under mechanical engineering for weapons and covers functional features common to small arms and ordnance that relate to ammunition feeding. It specifically designates mechanisms that depress the cartridge follower or lock it in a lowered position to control the loading sequence. This classification is used for inventions that provide means to lower or secure the follower during the feeding cycle.
[F41A 9/68] Plural magazines, e.g. tandem magazines -- F41A 9/68 classifies mechanisms for feeding ammunition that employ multiple or tandem magazines, such as side-by-side or stacked magazine arrangements, used in small arms and other ordnance. It covers the design and operation of plural magazine systems that enable rapid or sequential loading of rounds.
[F41A 9/69] characterised by multiple-row or zigzag arrangement of cartridges -- F41A 9/69 covers ammunition-feeding or loading devices in small-arms and ordnance that use a multiple-row or zigzag arrangement of cartridges. The classification applies to mechanisms that guide cartridges in staggered or angled rows to improve feeding reliability or rate of fire.
[F41A 9/70] Arrangements thereon for discharging, e.g. cartridge followers or discharge throats -- The CPC subclass F41A 9/70 covers components that form the discharge path for ammunition in weapons, such as cartridge followers, discharge throats and related arrangements that direct or release a round during firing. It falls under Mechanical Engineering → Weapons → Functional features common to small-arms and ordnance → Feeding or loading of ammunition.
[F41A 9/71] Arrangements thereon for varying capacity -- The subclass F41A 9/71 covers arrangements mounted on firearms or artillery that enable the ammunition capacity to be altered, such as interchangeable magazines, adjustable chambers, or variable-size drum mechanisms. It includes any device that lets the user increase or decrease the number of rounds the weapon can hold.
[F41A 9/72] Tubular magazines, i.e. magazines containing the ammunition in lengthwise tandem sequence -- F41A 9/72 covers tubular magazines, which store ammunition in a lengthwise tandem sequence within a tube and are used for feeding or loading rounds in firearms and artillery.
[F41A 9/73] Drum magazines -- Drum magazines are cylindrical ammunition containers that hold multiple rounds and feed them into a firearm's chamber via a spring-driven mechanism, allowing rapid, high-capacity loading for small arms and artillery. This CPC sub-class covers their design, construction, and integration with weapon feeding systems.
[F41A 9/74] with radially disposed cartridges -- The subclass F41A 9/74 covers weapon systems whose ammunition is arranged radially around a central axis, such as firearms or artillery that load cartridges positioned like spokes on a wheel. It pertains to the feeding or loading mechanisms that handle these radially disposed cartridges, enabling rapid or simultaneous chambering of multiple rounds. This feature is applicable to both small-arms and larger ordnance.
[F41A 9/75] having a spiral cartridge channel -- F41A 9/75 covers weapon loading mechanisms that incorporate a spiral cartridge channel, a helical passage within the ammunition or barrel that guides rounds during feeding. The feature applies to both small-arms and ordnance to improve loading efficiency.
[F41A 9/76] Magazines having an endless-chain conveyor -- F41A 9/76 relates to magazine constructions for small-arms or large-calibre weapons in which ammunition is moved by an endless-chain conveyor, providing continuous feeding or loading of rounds within the weapon's ammunition storage system.
[F41A 9/77] Magazines having a screw conveyor -- F41A 9/77 classifies ammunition magazines that incorporate a screw conveyor for moving rounds between storage and the weapon. The code applies to both small-arms and larger ordnance where a helical screw transports ammunition during loading.
[F41A 9/78] Magazines having a reciprocating conveyor -- The F41A 9/78 subclass defines magazines for firearms or artillery that employ a reciprocating conveyor mechanism to transport ammunition within the storage device, enabling continuous feeding or loading. This functional feature applies to both small-arms and larger ordnance systems and falls under the broader categories of mechanical engineering, weapons, and ammunition-handling details.
[F41A 9/79] for belted ammunition -- The CPC subclass F41A 9/79 covers mechanisms that feed or load belted ammunition, which includes cartridges or shells with a circumferential belt for extraction and handling. It pertains to the design of loading devices, magazines, or conveyors that manage such ammunition in firearms or artillery systems. This subclass falls under functional features common to both small arms and ordnance, specifically the feeding or loading of ammunition.
[F41A 9/80] having provision for quick-coupling of the belts of adjacent magazines -- This CPC subclass covers feeding or loading features that provide a means for quickly coupling the belts of adjacent magazines, enabling fast, continuous ammunition feed in small arms or ordnance.
[F41A 9/81] having provision for collecting belt links or empty cartridge cases -- F41A 9/81 designates weapon feed or loading systems that incorporate a means for gathering spent belt links or empty cartridge cases, such as trays, conveyors or chutes, enabling their removal, storage or reuse during operation. This feature appears in small-arms and larger ordnance.
[F41A 9/82] Reloading of magazines -- This classification covers mechanisms and methods for refilling or reloading ammunition magazines in firearms, including designs for automatically or manually replenishing cartridges, applicable to small-arms and larger ordnance.
[F41A 9/83] Apparatus or tools for reloading magazines with unbelted ammunition, e.g. cartridge clips -- F41A 9/83 covers devices used to reload magazines that hold loose, unbelted ammunition, such as cartridge clips or similar tools. The classification applies to mechanisms that facilitate rapid feeding of rounds into firearms, addressing the loading process for small arms and related ordnance.
[F41A 9/84] Clips -- F41A 9/84 covers clips that secure, hold, or organize ammunition for feeding or loading in small-arms and larger ordnance, such as pistol, rifle, or cannon cartridges. The subcategory includes detachable, fixed, spring-loaded or otherwise hinged devices that retain rounds in a stack or bundle and release them for chambering. It pertains to the functional features common to both small-arms and artillery loading mechanisms.
[F41A 9/85] for reloading revolver-type magazines -- F41A 9/85 covers designs and mechanisms for reloading revolver-type magazines, addressing devices that feed or insert cartridges into the rotating cylinder of a revolver. It falls under functional features common to small arms and ordnance, specifically the feeding or loading of ammunition within mechanical engineering of weapons.
[F41A 9/86] Feeding belted ammunition into magazines -- This subclass deals with mechanisms that transfer belt-linked ammunition into a magazine, guiding and advancing the belt so that individual rounds are loaded directly into the magazine chamber. It covers devices for feeding belt-fed cartridges into box, drum or other types of magazines for small arms and larger ordnance.
[F41A 9/87] Ammunition handling dollies or transfer carts -- This subclass covers devices that transport ammunition between storage and loading points, such as dollies or carts equipped with wheels or rollers for moving rounds, shells or cartridges. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, functional features common to small arms and ordnance, focusing on feeding or loading.
[F41A 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups of this subclass -- F41A 99/00 is a residual group in the CPC covering functional features or details common to small-arms and ordnance that are not specifically addressed in any other subgroup of this subclass. It is used for novel or miscellaneous weapon-related inventions-such as unique mechanisms, components or methods-when no more precise classification exists.
[F41B] WEAPONS FOR PROJECTING MISSILES WITHOUT USE OF EXPLOSIVE OR COMBUSTIBLE PROPELLANT CHARGE -- **Definition:** This place covers:  All weapons propelling a missile but not using an explosive or combustible pyrotechnic propellant charge as the energy to launch the missile, i.e. using accumulated potential energy such as:  air or gas pressure  elastic deformation (bow, crossbow, spring, elastic)  kinetic energy (slings, friction wheels)  electromagnetism.  The subclass further includes thrusting, hitting and hand-thrown weapons.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Projectiles for fishing, e.g. fish-spears -> A01K81/00 - Sports implements for throwing -> A63B65/00 , A63B65/08 - Stationary apparatus for projecting sports balls, e.g. tennis balls, A63B69/40 -> A63B69/40 - Throwing or slinging toys -> A63H33/18 - Knives, axes -> B26B - Projectiles or missiles specially adapted for projection without use of explosive or combustible propellant charge, e.g. for blow guns, bows or crossbows, hand-held spring or air guns -> F42B6/00
[F41B 1/00] Blow guns, i.e. tubes for impelling projectiles, e.g. peas or darts, by the force of the breath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Guns for launching the missile with the force of the breath only. The configuration ranges from a simple tube with a mouthpiece at the end, a tube with an appendix offset from the tube's axis carrying the mouthpiece or a tube with a mouthpiece attached at the end of a flexible tube.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Toys, including pop guns -> A63H - Actuating the trigger of a firearm with the help of breath -> F41A19/08
[F41B 11/00] Compressed-gas guns, e.g. air guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Guns or devices for discharging projectiles through a barrel by conversion of the potential energy stored in a compressed gas into kinetic energy for the propulsion of the projectile. The compressed gas is either available in a pre-compressed form or compressed with mechanical means, i.e. without use of explosive or combustible propellant charge, immediately before or during the launching of each projectile.  **Glossary:** - Airgun: generic term for compressed gas guns, sometimes used for guns using compressed gas other than air, most commonly CO2. Classical airguns project so-called airgun pellets, wasted projectile hollowed at the base and available in a variety of head styles
[F41B 11/50] Magazines for compressed-gas guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Containers for holding a plurality of missiles to be projected by a compressed gas gun, i.e. magazines.  Devices or mechanisms for sequentially bringing such missiles from an external magazine into the gun frame/casing/housing/receiver, i.e. feeding arrangements.  Devices or mechanisms for sequentially bringing such missiles into the position inside the compressed gas gun ready to be projected ("firing" chamber), i.e. loading arrangements.
[F41B 11/51] the magazine being an integral, internal part of the gun housing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Magazines integrally formed with the gun, i.e. the magazine is not removable.  The missiles to be projected by the compressed gas gun are inserted and stored directly in a space/cavity formed in the gun.
[F41B 11/52] the projectiles being loosely held in a magazine above the gun housing, e.g. in a hopper -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Magazines holding projectiles in a removable magazine above the gun housing which implies the following:
[F41B 11/53] the magazine having motorised feed-assisting means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The hopper contains secondary means to assist the gravity powered feeding of the projectiles, such as:
[F41B 11/54] the projectiles being stored in a rotating drum magazine -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The projectiles are stored in an ordered fashion, i.e. the order in which the projectiles will be discharged is pre-defined. Drum magazines can be in any of the known types, for example:
[F41B 11/55] the projectiles being stored in stacked order in a removable box magazine, rack or tubular magazine -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The projectiles are stored in an ordered fashion, i.e. the order in which the projectiles will be discharged is pre-defined, the arrangement of projectile is substantially linear inside the magazine. This arrangement implies a so-called follower, i. e. a spring biased element pushing the stack of projectiles out the magazine. The magazine is removable from the gun, often as a look alike to a firearm magazine.
[F41B 11/56] the magazine also housing a gas cartridge -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The removable magazine carrying the projectiles also carries an exchangeable or refillable pressurised cartridge such as a CO 2 cartridge, usually for soft-air guns.
[F41B 11/57] Electronic or electric systems for feeding or loading -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Electric systems for powering of motors for the active force feeding or loading of the projectiles, except for the hoppers having motorised agitation and/or feed assisting means (precedence of F41B11/53 ).  Electronic systems for the control of active force feeding or loading systems, except for the hoppers having motorised agitation and/or feed assisting means (precedence of F41B11/53 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - for controlling motorised feed assisting means associated with the projectile magazine -> F41B11/53
[F41B 11/60] characterised by the supply of compressed gas -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Residual group including compressed-gas guns with particular means for supplying compressed gas which are not covered in any of the groups F41B11/62 – F41B11/684 .
[F41B 11/62] with pressure supplied by a gas cartridge -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Compressed gas guns, wherein the pre-compressed gas is stored in an exchangeable/refillable gas cartridge, which can be housed either:
[F41B 11/64] having a piston effecting a compressor stroke during the firing of each shot -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Airguns with a piston to compress the air for propelling the projectile at the moment of the firing, i.e. the triggering action of the gun activates the compression means and the resulting compressed air is used directly for launching the projectile. This implies that no intermediate compressed air storage chamber (pressure accumulation tank) is present (an expansion or equalisation chamber in the sense of transit chambers might be present). The piston is either:
[F41B 11/641] the piston being hand operated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Airguns with manually operated pistons, the piston directly delivering the compressed air to the "firing chamber", i.e. hand-pumps directly feeding compressed air to the "firing chamber".  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Pumping or compressor arrangements for pre-compressed air -> F41B11/681
[F41B 11/642] the piston being spring operated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements wherein the energy for moving the piston in the cylinder is delivered by a spring under tension.
[F41B 11/643] the piston being arranged concentrically with the barrel -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements wherein the longitudinal axis of the spring coincides with the longitudinal axis of the barrel. The spring may be arranged around or behind the barrel.
[F41B 11/644] having an additional slidable mass moving in the opposite direction to the piston, e.g. for recoil reduction -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Airguns with spring operated pistons compressing the air during the launch of the projectile will inherently create considerable recoil deteriorating precision. This group covers countermass-type recoil reduction mechanism, wherein, synchronised with the movement the piston, a countermass will be accelerated in the opposite direction to neutralise the reaction force caused by the movement of the piston.
[F41B 11/645] the slidable mass being a compressor piston -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Systems with two spring operated pistons with the same mass acting in opposite direction so as to eliminate the recoil force induced by the reaction to the piston acceleration.
[F41B 11/646] Arrangements for putting the spring under tension -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for pre-tensioning the spring and holding the piston in the fully spring-loaded position, i.e. cocking. The arrangements do not compress any air, they only accumulate energy in the spring that will, upon trigger actuation, compress air in the cylinder.
[F41B 11/647] by a rocker lever -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A rocking lever being mechanically linked to the spring-piston arrangement, so as to put the spring under tension and hold the piston in the fully spring-loaded position, i.e. cocking by rocking lever.
[F41B 11/648] in breakdown air guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The breaking of the airgun, i.e. the relative movement of two hinged parts of the airgun, usually the barrel and the receiver, actuates the piston so as to compress the air inside the compressed air storage tank, i.e. the piston itself is the pressure accumulation tank. The two hinged parts of the airgun take over the function of a dedicated rocking lever for actuating the piston.
[F41B 11/66] having deformable bellows or chambers pressed during firing, e.g. by deformation of the body of the gun -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Airguns with a deformable container, e.g. bellows, a bulb or other substantially air-tight part of the airgun, holding a quantity of air, which is pressurised by the squeezing or deformation of the container, so as to decrease the internal volume of the container and urge the air into the "firing chamber" in order to directly launch the projectile.  Illustrative examples of subject matter classified in this place:  1.  2.
[F41B 11/68] the gas being pre-compressed before firing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Airguns comprising a compressed air storage chamber (pressure accumulation tank), filled with compressed air before the firing, i.e. the triggering action of the gun activates a valve or other mechanism to fluidly connect the air storage chamber (pressure accumulation tank) with the "firing chamber", thereby allowing the compressed air to launch the projectile. The exclusion of the group F41B11/62 implies that some means to pre-compress the air, e.g. pump or compressor, must be an integral part of the gun.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Compressed gas guns characterised by the supply of compressed gas with pressure supplied by a gas cartridge -> F41B11/62
[F41B 11/681] Pumping or compressor arrangements therefor -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for compressing the air in the air storage chamber (pressure accumulation tank), i.e. hand-pumps or electrically powered pumps integrated into the gun or permanently attached thereto for compressing atmospheric air into the pressure accumulation tank.  This group further includes airguns with integral or permanently attached pressure accumulation tanks for storing the atmospheric air compressed by a pump or compressor, in particular documents wherein the teaching is specifically aimed at the particular shape/arrangement/configuration/material of the pressure accumulation tank per se.
[F41B 11/682] Pressure accumulation tanks -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Air guns with integral or permanently attached pressure accumulation tanks for storing the atmospheric air compressed by a pump or compressor. This group contains documents wherein the teaching is specifically aimed at the particular shape/arrangement/configuration/material of the pressure accumulation tank per se.
[F41B 11/683] operated by a rocker-lever system -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A rocking lever being directly mechanically linked to a piston arrangement, so as to compress the air inside the compressed air storage tank, i.e. the piston itselfis one of the boundaries of the pressure accumulation tank.
[F41B 11/684] in breakdown air guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The breaking of the airgun, i.e. the relative movement of two hinged parts of the airgun, usually the barrel and the receiver, actuates the spring-piston arrangement so as to put the spring under tension and hold the piston in the fully spring-loaded position, i.e. cocking by breakdown mechanism.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Breakdown activated pumping arrangements for pre-compressing air for storing it into a pressurised air storage tank -> F41B11/648

[F41B 11/71] Electric or electronic control systems, e.g. for safety purposes -- F41B 11/71 covers electric or electronic control systems for compressed-gas guns such as air guns, including safety mechanisms and electronic firing controls used in weapons that launch projectiles without explosive or combustible propellant.
[F41B 11/72] Valves -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Valve arrangements integrated in compressed gas guns for regulating the various pneumatic functions of an compressed gas gun, such as:
[F41B 11/721] for controlling gas pressure for both firing the projectile and for loading or feeding -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Compressed gas guncomprising a single valve performing the dual function of firing the projectile and feeding or loading the consecutive projectile in a (semi-)automatic compressed gas gun.
[F41B 11/722] for controlling gas pressure for loading or feeding only -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A valve in a compressed gas gun, the valve being a dedicated valve for performing the function of feeding or loading of the consecutive projectile in a (semi-)automatic compressed gas gun.
[F41B 11/723] for controlling gas pressure for firing the projectile only -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A valve in a compressed gas gun, the valve being a valve specifically dedicated for performing the function of firing the projectile.
[F41B 11/724] for gas pressure reduction -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A valve in a compressed air gun situated on the pneumatic path between the over-pressurisedcompressed gas source, i.e. accumulation tank, gas cartridge, piston-cylinder, and the firing chamber reducing the pressure to a predefined pressure. The aim is to achieve pressure regulation for reliably ensuring constant fire power, to reduce the firing power to levels accepted under national laws or to levels corresponding to competition regulations.
[F41B 11/73] Sealing arrangements -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements of seals in a compressed air gun sealing off any pneumatic component of the compressed gas gun, including in particular the interface between an external gas cartridge or pressure accumulation tank with the internal pneumatic components of the gun. This group contains documents wherein the teaching is specifically aimed at the particular shape, arrangement, configuration or material of the sealing arrangement.  This group contains documents wherein the teaching is specifically aimedat the particular shape, arrangement, configuration or material of the sealing arrangement.
[F41B 11/80] specially adapted for particular purposes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Residual group including compressed-gas guns for particular purposes not covered by F41B11/81 – F41B11/89 .
[F41B 11/81] for ejecting powder, e.g. pepper -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices for pneumatic ejection or marking/irritating powders, either by:
[F41B 11/83] for launching harpoons -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices for propelling harpoons or fishing spears with pneumatic pressure, wherein at least part of the shaft of the harpoon is held in the barrel of the compressed gas gun and guided inside the barrel when discharged by the expanding compressed gas.  The group includes both, devices for use by divers in submerged condition or by fishers standing on land/ship and propelling the harpoon/spear into the water.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Trigger mechanisms for harpoon guns -> F41B7/046  **Glossary:** - Wet firing: discharge of the harpoon wherein the barrel holding the shaft of the harpoon is partially filled with water - Dry firing: discharge of the harpoon with a sealed off dry (air filled) barrel, either for one time use or else with means for keeping the barrel sealed under water (sealed piston pusher or draining means)

[F41B 11/87] for industrial purposes, e.g. for surface treatment -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Compressed gas guns specifically designed for the intended use in industry, e.g. for cleaning/descaling of ovens, furnaces, kilns or pipes where burning residues or slag is removed by impacting it with projectiles propelled by pneumatic launchers.
[F41B 11/89] for toys -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices for launching a projectile by air or gas pressure, typically with low energy, with the main purpose of amusement, suitable for use by children without any particular safety precautions. The term "toy gun" is often erroneously used in order to differentiate the air gun from a firearm, see also special rule of classification below.  **Glossary:** - Toy gun: is often erroneously used in order to differentiate the air gun from a firearm, see also special rules of classification above
[F41B 13/00] Thrusting-weapons -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Hand held thrusting and cutting weapons, to be kept in hand during the use, i.e. not intended to be thown.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Throwing knives -> F41B15/00 - Bolas -> F41B15/10 - Fencing equipment -> A63B69/02 - Sheaths for hand cutting tools -> B26B29/00 - Firearms combined with thrusting or cutting weapons -> F41C27/16 - Bayonets -> F41C27/18
[F41B 13/02] Sabres
[F41B 13/04] Sheaths or scabbards therefor -- F41B 13/04 covers sheaths or scabbards specifically designed for thrusting weapons that launch missiles without using explosive or combustible propellant, such as spears, darts or similar projectiles. The entry falls under mechanical engineering weapons for projecting missiles by thrust rather than combustion.
[F41B 13/06] for concealment, e.g. swordsticks -- F41B 13/06 covers thrusting weapons that are designed to be concealed within ordinary objects, such as walking sticks, umbrellas or jewelry, allowing a blade or similar projectile to be hidden from view while maintaining the appearance of a non-weapon item.
[F41B 13/08] Daggers -- F41B 13/08 covers daggers, a type of hand-held thrusting weapon that projects a blade as a missile without the use of an explosive or combustible propellant charge. The subclass is nested under mechanical engineering, weapons, and thrusting-weapons in the CPC system.
[F41B 13/10] Lances -- Lances are long pole weapons ending in a sharp point, designed for thrusting attacks, especially from horseback. They function as thrusting-weapons that project a missile without any explosive or combustible propellant, relying solely on the kinetic force generated by the user's motion. This category includes various lance types used historically and in modern ceremonial or sporting contexts.
[F41B 15/00] Weapons not otherwise provided for -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Residual group for weapons which do not use pyrotechnic charges to propell a missile, it includes in particular blunt hitting weapons such as batons or sticks and hand thrown weapons such as bolas and throwing knives or shuriken  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Electric shock devices, e.g. cattle prods -> A01K15/02 - Electric stunning means -> F41H13/0012 - Darts -> F42B6/003
[F41B 15/02] Batons -- The CPC code F41B 15/02 classifies batons as a type of weapon that does not launch missiles with explosive or combustible propellant, falling under the broader categories of mechanical engineering and weapons. It groups these handheld, non-lethal implements with other weapons not otherwise specified in the classification hierarchy.
[F41B 15/022] of telescopic type -- F41B 15/022 pertains to telescopic-type weapons that launch missiles or projectiles without employing explosive or combustible propellant, such as mechanically driven launchers or catapults that use a telescoping barrel to accelerate the munition.
[F41B 15/025] the telescoping sections being locked by coacting conical end surfaces, i.e. by friction -- This CPC subclass covers weapons whose launch tube or barrel consists of telescoping sections that are locked together by coacting conical end surfaces which rely on friction. It applies to non-explosive projectile launchers such as pneumatic or electromagnetic devices where the locking mechanism does not use separate fasteners.
[F41B 15/027] the telescoping sections being locked by an additional mechanical locking element -- F41B 15/027 covers weapons that launch missiles without an explosive or combustible propellant where the barrel or launch tube consists of telescoping sections secured by an additional mechanical locking element, ensuring the sections remain fixed during operation. This falls under the mechanical-engineering weapons category for non-explosive missile projectors.
[F41B 15/04] with electric stunning-means -- F41B 15/04 covers weapons that launch missiles or projectiles without an explosive or combustible propellant, using electric stunning means to power or activate the projectile. The classification includes devices where an electric discharge or electromagnetic force provides the launching energy or delivers a non-lethal stun effect to the target.
[F41B 15/06] with inserted knives or spikes -- This subclass covers non-explosive projectile weapons that incorporate knives or spikes as the payload, intended to be projected without a combustible propellant. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, and specifically weapons for launching missiles without explosive charge that are not otherwise specified.
[F41B 15/08] Knuckledusters -- F41B 15/08 covers knuckledusters, handheld striking implements designed to enhance the impact of a punch. Classified under mechanical engineering, weapons, and the subcategory for weapons projecting missiles without explosive or combustible propellant, they are listed as weapons not otherwise provided for.
[F41B 15/10] Bolas -- Bolas are a type of non-explosive projectile weapon consisting of two or more weighted spheres linked by cords, thrown to entangle the legs of target animals or people. The device is categorized under mechanical engineering weapons that launch missiles without explosive or combustible propellant, and falls within the broader class of weapons not otherwise provided for.
[F41B 3/00] Sling weapons -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Bows, crossbows -> F41B5/00 - Spring guns -> F41B7/00 - Traps or throwing-apparatus for throwing clay target discs -> F41J9/18  **Glossary:** - Trebuchet:: a type of catapult that works by using the energy of a raised counterweight to throw the projectile - Sling: a projectile receiving patch with two non-elastic ropes, bands or cords attached, the projectile being launched by centrifugal force - Catapult: a projectile receiving patch with two elastic bands attached, said elastic bands at the other end being attached to a fork shape handle - Catapult (siege engine): device with a rotary arm carrying a projectile receiving element at one end, the other end either being attached to a heavy weight, the arm having an intermediate turning axle or being fixedly held, the arm being flexible.
[F41B 3/005] Catapults in pistol or rifle form having a cocking device, i.e. a mechanical device for holding the elastic band -- This subclass covers handheld catapults shaped like pistols or rifles that include a cocking mechanism-a mechanical device for holding and tensioning an elastic band used to launch a projectile, and it belongs to weapons for projecting missiles without explosive or combustible propellant.

It covers the structure, operation and accessories of these sling-type weapons.
[F41B 3/03] Catapults having a pivotable launcher arm -- F41B 3/03 classifies catapults whose launcher arm pivots to hurl a projectile, using a swinging motion rather than an explosive or combustible charge. These devices belong to the sling-weapon sub-category of weapons for projecting missiles without propellant.
[F41B 3/04] Centrifugal sling apparatus -- A centrifugal sling apparatus is a weapon that launches missiles or other projectiles by converting rotational energy into linear motion, using a rapidly rotating arm or disc to fling the payload outward. It falls under the category of non-explosive, non-combustible missile-projecting weapons and is classified within the mechanical engineering weapons hierarchy.

[F41B 9/00] Liquid ejecting guns, e.g. water pistols -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Guns for expelling liquid at high pressure and high velocity, i.e. the liquid is the missile in this main group.
[F41B 9/0003] characterised by the pressurisation of the liquid  for launching torpedoes or stores from submarines  F41F3/10 -- This classification covers devices that launch torpedoes or stores from submarines by pressurising a liquid, falling under liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols and belonging to weapons that project missiles without explosive or combustible propellant.
[F41B 9/0006] the liquid being pressurised prior to ejection -- The entry concerns liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols, focusing on the step where the liquid is pressurised before it is expelled. [F41B 9/0009] the pressurised liquid being contained in an expandable chamber, e.g. a bladder or a chamber with a spring-loaded slidable wall -- F41B 9/0009 covers liquid-ejecting guns where the propelling fluid is stored in an expandable chamber such as a bladder or a spring-loaded sliding wall. The pressurised liquid is released to fire a projectile without using explosive or combustible propellant. It applies to devices like water pistols and other non-explosive missile-projection weapons.
[F41B 9/0012] the gun having an unpressurised liquid reservoir -- The subclass F41B 9/0012 covers guns that project missiles using a liquid drawn from an unpressurised reservoir, where the liquid is expelled by the operator's action rather than by a compressed-gas or combustible charge. It includes devices such as water pistols that rely on simple liquid ejection without a pressurised or explosive propellant.
[F41B 9/0015] the liquid being pressurised by compressed gas, e.g. air  pressurisation by explosion gases  F41B9/0043 -- This CPC subclass covers liquid ejecting guns such as water pistols where the propelling liquid is pressurised by a compressed gas, for example air, or by gases generated in an explosion. It pertains to weapons that launch missiles without using an explosive or combustible propellant charge.
[F41B 9/0018] the gas being compressed utilising a manual piston pump -- F41B 9/0018 covers liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols that use a manually operated piston pump to compress gas, which then provides the propulsive force for the projectile. The entry falls under mechanical engineering, specifically weapons that project missiles without explosive or combustible propellant.
[F41B 9/0021] the gas being compressed by non-manual pumping means, e.g. an electric pump -- This subclass addresses liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols in which the propelling gas is compressed by a non-manual pumping means, for example an electric pump, rather than by hand operation. It covers the gas-generation system that provides the compressed gas for missile projection without the use of explosive or combustible propellant.
[F41B 9/0025] the pressurised liquid and the compressed gas being physically separated from each other, e.g. by a movable wall -- This subclass covers devices in which the liquid propellant and gas are kept separate within the barrel, using a movable partition to allow pressure to act on the liquid without mixing, typical of non-explosive projectile launchers such as water pistols.
[F41B 9/0028] the gun having an unpressurised liquid reservoir -- F41B 9/0028 covers guns that employ an unpressurised liquid reservoir to eject a stream, such as water pistols and similar liquid-ejecting weapons that project missiles without using explosive or combustible propellant.
[F41B 9/0031] the liquid being pressurised at the moment of ejection -- The CPC subclass F41B 9/0031 covers liquid-ejecting guns in which the liquid is pressurised at the moment of ejection, such as water pistols that generate pressure only during the discharge. This falls under weapons for projecting missiles without explosive or combustible propellant, within the mechanical engineering hierarchy.
[F41B 9/0034] Pressurisation by deformation of the gun body -- The CPC subclass F41B 9/0034 covers liquid-ejecting guns, such as water pistols, that generate pressure by flexing or deforming the barrel or chamber rather than using an explosive charge. This method creates the propulsive force needed to expel the liquid projectile.
[F41B 9/0037] Pressurisation by a piston -- F41B 9/0037 covers mechanisms that use a piston to increase pressure in a reservoir, forcing liquid out of a gun-type device such as a water pistol. The piston moves within a cylinder, compressing the liquid or gas to generate a jet for non-explosive projectile launch.
[F41B 9/004] the piston movement being mechanically coupled to the trigger movement, e.g. the piston being part of the trigger -- F41B 9/004 covers designs in which the piston that propels a liquid projectile is directly linked to the trigger mechanism, so that moving the trigger also moves the piston, for example by integrating the piston into the trigger assembly of water-pistol type guns.
[F41B 9/0043] Pressurisation by explosive pressure -- Pressurisation by explosive pressure describes a method of generating the driving force in liquid-ejecting guns, such as water pistols, by using a small explosive charge rather than springs or compressed gas. The technique is applied to weapons that launch missiles without an explosive or combustible propellant, providing a rapid pressure rise to propel the projectile.
[F41B 9/0046] Disruptors, i.e. for neutralising explosive devices -- The CPC code F41B 9/0046 covers disruptors designed to neutralise explosive devices, typically using a high-velocity liquid or gas jet to disable detonators or warheads. These devices fall under the mechanical-engineering weapons category for non-explosive projectile weapons such as water pistols.
[F41B 9/005] the gun being connected to an external source of pressurised liquid during use of the gun, i.e. at least during ejection of the liquid -- This subclass covers liquid-ejecting guns that are linked to an external source of pressurised liquid while firing, using a hose or conduit to supply the propellant fluid during each discharge. It applies to designs where the gun remains connected to the external liquid supply at least for the ejection phase.
[F41B 9/0053] the external source being a pressurised water supply system, e.g. the municipal water supply system or a water supply system onboard a ship -- This CPC subgroup pertains to liquid-ejecting guns that obtain the propelling water from an external pressurised supply such as a municipal mains or a ship's water system, rather than from a self-contained reservoir. It includes water pistols and similar weapons that rely on a continuous external water source for projectile discharge.
[F41B 9/0056] the external source being open water and the pressure being generated by an intake travelling at high speed through the water -- F41B 9/0056 covers liquid-ejecting devices that draw water directly from an open source and create ejection pressure by moving an intake rapidly through the water, using the resulting water flow to power the projectile without a separate propellant.
[F41B 9/0059] characterised by the number or kind of pressure or storage chambers -- This subclass covers liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols whose design is defined by the number or type of pressure or storage chambers employed. It belongs to the mechanical-engineering weapons group for non-explosive missile projection.
[F41B 9/0062] the liquid being stored in the handle, grip or stock of the gun -- This CPC subclass covers weapons that store the liquid propellant inside the handle, grip or stock of the gun, such as water pistols where the reservoir is integral to those parts. It relates to non-explosive, liquid-ejecting firearms in the group for projecting missiles without use of an explosive or combustible propellant charge.
[F41B 9/0065] with removable storage tanks -- F41B 9/0065 covers liquid-ejecting weapons such as water pistols that incorporate removable storage tanks for the projectile medium. This subclass falls within the broader group of non-explosive missile-projecting weapons in mechanical engineering.
[F41B 9/0068] with more than one storage tank -- The F41B 9/0068 class covers liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols that use more than one storage tank to hold the propellant fluid.
