[F41B 9/0075] characterised by special nozzle arrangements, e.g. for a swirling effect or a directional effect -- This classification covers liquid-ejecting guns that use special nozzle designs to create a swirling or directional flow effect. It applies to devices such as water pistols where the nozzle geometry shapes the stream without any explosive propellant, falling under weapons that project missiles without an explosive charge.
[F41B 9/0078] characterised by the gun housing, e.g. its shape or concealment -- F41B 9/0078 concerns liquid-ejecting guns in which the distinguishing element is the design of the gun housing, including its shape, dimensions or means of concealment, independent of the projectile or propellant system.
[F41B 9/0081] Special gun housing shapes, e.g. in the form of animals, airplanes, toys or figurines -- The F41B 9/0081 class covers liquid-ejecting guns whose housings are formed into novelty shapes such as animals, airplanes, toys or figurines, rather than conventional cylindrical barrels. It applies to designs that integrate the decorative form with the functional gun body for recreational water-pistols.
[F41B 9/0084] Concealed gun housings, e.g. concealed nozzles in a garment -- The F41B 9/0084 classification covers concealed housings for weapons that eject liquids or similar projectiles without explosive or combustible propellants, such as hidden nozzles integrated into garments. It applies to designs where the firing element is embedded in clothing or other apparel to disguise the weapon's presence, typically used in water-pistols or similar non-lethal devices.
[F41B 9/0087] characterised by the intended use, e.g. for self-defence, law-enforcement, industrial use, military purposes  F41B9/0046  takes precedence -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Liquid ejecting guns or devices for serious purposes, i.e. NOT for leisure, games, toys, play or fun  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Adaptations for feeding or loading missiles from magazines into spring guns -> F41B9/0046
[F41B 9/009] for ejecting electrically charged jets -- A subclass of weapons that project missiles without explosives, covering liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols that use an electrically charged jet to propel the fluid. It describes devices that eject electrically charged streams of liquid for projectile purposes.
[F41B 9/0093] for riot control, e.g. water cannons therefor -- This subclass covers non-explosive liquid-ejecting weapons used for crowd dispersal, specifically water-cannon systems and similar devices employed in riot control. It pertains to mechanical engineering of weapons that project missiles without explosive or combustible propellant, such as water pistols and related ejectors.
[F41B 9/0096] having means for mixing other agents with the liquid -- F41B 9/0096 pertains to liquid-ejecting guns such as water pistols that include a device for blending additional substances-like dyes, chemicals or fragrances-into the expelled liquid, allowing the projectile to carry a mixed payload. It falls under the weapons category for non-explosive missile projection.
[F41C] SMALLARMS, e.g. PISTOLS, RIFLES -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Small arms means a firearm which is generally held with one or both hands for firing. Small arms in the sense of man-portable firearms, i.e. a weapon capable of launching a projectile by confined deflagration of a pyrotechnic propellant, such as pistols, rifles, shotguns or the like, and details and accessories that are unique to small arms  Pistols:  Shoulder-fired small arms:  Parts of small arms:  Miscellaneous attachments for small arms; accessories:  Means for wearing or carrying small arms  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Pistols or machine guns operated without detonators -> A63H5/04 - Pistols for shooting bolts into concrete constructions, metal walls or the like -> B25C - Hand-held nailing tools operated by combustion pressure generated by detonation of a cartridge -> B25C1/10 - Arrangement of guns on vessels -> B63G1/00 - Arrangement of military equipment in aircraft -> B64D7/00 - Functional features or details common to both small arms and ordnance, mountings therefor -> F41A - Weapons for projecting missiles without use of explosive or combustible propellant charge -> F41B  **Glossary:** - Under-barrel grenade launcher: firearm for launching grenades, can be an auxiliary firearm attach to a primary firearm, usually single shot - Machine gun: firearm with a long rifled barrel capable of sustained firing in full automatic mode, the projectiles are fed from a belt or a high capacity magazine that can be fitted or portable - Carbine: short shoulder-fired firearm, originally for cavalry use - Submachine gun: short, light weight machine gun, designed to fire pistol cartridges - Rifle: shoulder-fired firearm with a long rifled barrel. Rifles can be capable for firing with magazine fed projectiles in single shot mode (repeater rifle) or in semi automatic and full automatic mode (assault rifle) - Shotgun: smooth booth bore shoulder-fired firearm for firing shot at a relatively short distance
[F41C 23/00] Details -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes handgrips for handguns and handgrips/pistol grip for shoulder-fired small arms, i.e. the grip associated with the trigger system.  Includes stocks for shoulder-fired small arms, in particular: forestocks, i.e. the part which is held by the forward hand (not the shooting hand) for support during shooting and buttstocks, i.e. the part held against the shoulder during shooting.  Includes butts, i.e. the proximal ends of the buttstocks, the part actually contacting the shoulder.
[F41C 23/02] Attachment of slings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The attachement for attaching the sling, integral or fixed to the stock, forestock of handgrip.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Slings for carrying long guns -> F41C33/002
[F41C 23/04] Folding or telescopic stocks or stock parts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Only the stock is folding, telescopic or collapsible, no functional parts of the firarm is folding or articulated.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Hinge frame revolvers -> F41C3/16 - Breakdown guns -> F41C7/00 - Articulated or collapsible guns -> F41A11/04
[F41C 23/06] Stocks specially adapted for recoil reduction -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Stocks with integrated recoil buffers only in the stock.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Bolt buffers or recuperators acting on the bolt but partially entering the stock -> F41A3/78
[F41C 23/08] Recoil absorbing pads -- F41C 23/08 covers recoil-absorbing pads that are attached to small-arms such as pistols or rifles to reduce the impact of firing on the shooter. The pads may be made of rubber, polymer or other dampening materials and are positioned on the stock, grip or muzzle area to mitigate felt recoil and improve handling.
[F41C 23/10] Stocks or grips for pistols, e.g. revolvers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also includes pistolgrips associated with the trigger group of a shoulder-fired small arm  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Auxiliary stocks for stabilising, or for transforming pistols, e.g. revolvers, into shoulder-fired guns -> F41C23/12
[F41C 23/12] Auxiliary stocks for stabilising, or for transforming pistols, e.g. revolvers, into shoulder-fired guns -- F41C 23/12 covers auxiliary stocks and similar attachments that can be fitted to pistols or revolvers to provide shoulder support and increase stability, effectively converting the hand-held firearm into a shoulder-fired weapon. The subclass includes removable, foldable or detachable stocks designed for this purpose.
[F41C 23/14] Adjustable stock or stock parts, i.e. adaptable to personal requirements, e.g. length, pitch, cast or drop -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Adaptations of guns to both right and left hand use -> F41A35/06
[F41C 23/16] Forestocks -- F41C 23/16 covers forestocks, a type of device attached to a rifle or small-arms barrel that permits firing of shotgun shells or other low-pressure ammunition, often used for hunting or close-range defense. The classification groups such conversion or multi-caliber accessories within the weapons sub-section of mechanical engineering.
[F41C 23/18] characterised by the material used -- F41C 23/18 covers small-arms inventions whose defining feature is the material used in the weapon's construction, such as polymer, alloy or composite components for the barrel, receiver or other structural parts. The classification applies when the material choice itself determines the functional or performance characteristics of the pistol or rifle.
[F41C 23/20] Butts -- F41C 23/20 pertains to the butt of small-arms, the rear section of a pistol, rifle or similar firearm that is placed against the shooter's shoulder. The class includes design variations, materials, ergonomic shaping, recoil-absorbing pads and adjustable or foldable features that affect handling and stability.
[F41C 23/22] Stocks having space for the storage of objects -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also pistol grips or magazine extensions having space for the storage of objects.
[F41C 27/00] Accessories -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Residual group for attachments, accessories and details especially adapted for small arms, but not covered in F41C3/00 - F41C23/22 .
[F41C 27/04] Arrangements for mounting spades or shields -- Arrangements for mounting spades or shields involve the design of brackets, hinges, clamps or other fixtures that attach protective or stabilizing devices to small-arms such as pistols or rifles. These configurations enable rapid deployment and secure fixing of shield or spade-type attachments used for recoil control, tactical shielding or weapon handling enhancement.
[F41C 27/06] Adaptations of smallarms for firing grenades, e.g. rifle grenades, or for firing riot-control ammunition -- The F41C 27/06 entry covers adaptations that enable pistols, rifles or similar smallarms to launch grenades or riot-control ammunition, including launchers, adapters and conversion kits that modify the weapon to fire explosive or less-lethal projectiles.
[F41C 27/16] Smallarms combined with thrusting or cutting weapons -- The F41C 27/16 class deals with smallarms that incorporate a thrusting or cutting element, such as firearms equipped with knives, bayonets, or other bladed accessories. It covers designs where the cutting weapon is integrated with or attached to pistols, rifles, or similar small firearms for combined use.
[F41C 27/18] Bayonets -- F41C 27/18 covers bayonets, the detachable blade-like or spike accessories designed to be mounted on the muzzle of rifles or similar small-arms for close-quarters combat. The subclass falls under small-arms accessories within the mechanical engineering weapons hierarchy and defines designs, attachment methods, and functional features of bayonet devices.
[F41C 27/20] Attachments for wire cutting -- This subclass covers devices that can be mounted on small-arms such as pistols or rifles to cut wire, cord, or similar materials. It includes line-cutting attachments, grappling-hook cutters and other accessories designed for cutting or severing fine tensile elements while the firearm is carried or fired.
[F41C 27/22] Balancing or stabilising arrangements -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Stabilising devices worn on the body -> F41C33/001
[F41C 3/00] Pistols, e.g. revolvers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes both general types of handheld (as opposed to shoulder-fired) firearms, pistols, i.e. handgun with a chamber that is integral with the barrel, and revolvers, i.e. handgun that has a cylinder containing multiple chambers and at least one barrel for firing. Further includes toy, signal and cap-firing pistols.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Small arms specially adapted for underwater use -> F41C9/06 - Muzzle-loading small arms -> F41C9/08 - Devices for slaughtering or stunning animals -> A22B - Devices for shooting bolts into concrete constructions, metal walls or the like -> B25C
[F41C 3/005] Toy guns, e.g. cannons, firing a projectile by means of the combustion of a propellant charge, e.g. a cap -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cap firing toy pistols -> F41C3/06
[F41C 3/02] Signal pistols, e.g. Very pistols -- F41C 3/02 covers signal pistols, such as very pistols, which are designed to launch flares, smoke or other signaling projectiles rather than to serve as combat weapons. The category is part of the small-arms pistol subgroup within the weapons section of mechanical engineering.
[F41C 3/04] Starting pistols -- F41C 3/04 designates starting pistols, small firearms used to emit a signal at the beginning of races or competitions. They are typically single-shot, low-power weapons intended solely for starting purposes rather than combat.
[F41C 3/06] Cap-firing pistols, e.g. toy pistols -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A cap gun is a toy gun that creates a loud sound simulating a gunshot and a puff of smoke when the trigger is pulled.
[F41C 3/08] with band supply -- F41C 3/08 classifies pistols, such as revolvers, that incorporate a band-type feeding mechanism for delivering cartridges to the chamber. The band typically moves around the cylinder or barrel to guide ammunition into position during firing. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, smallarms, and pistols in the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[F41C 3/10] with rotatable cap carrier, e.g. drum -- F41C 3/10 classifies pistols, especially revolvers, that employ a rotatable cap carrier such as a drum to hold the ammunition caps, distinguishing them from firearms with fixed magazines.
[F41C 3/12] with slidable cap carrier, e.g. clip -- The CPC subclass F41C 3/12 relates to pistols, such as revolvers, that feature a slidable cap carrier, often referred to as a clip, for feeding ammunition. It falls under mechanical engineering → weapons → small arms → pistols and specifies designs where the ammunition-feeding component can move longitudinally along the weapon.
[F41C 3/14] Revolvers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Handgun that has a cylinder containing multiple chambers and at least one barrel for firing.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cap firing pistol with rotatable cap carrier, e.g. drum -> F41C3/10 - Obturating or packing devices for gas leak prevention in breech mechanisms specially adapted for sealing the gap between the forward end of the cartridge chamber and the rearward end of the barrel, e.g. sealing devices for revolvers or revolver-type guns -> F41A3/76 - Feeding of unbelted ammunition using a revolving drum magazine in revolver-type guns other than revolvers -> F41A9/27 - Extractors or ejectors for revolver-type guns -> F41A15/02
[F41C 3/16] Hinge-frame revolvers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group.
[F41C 33/00] Means for wearing or carrying smallarms -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes shooting harnesses for supporting the gun during shooting.  Includes slings, holsters and other means for wearing or carrying small arms on the body of the shooter when not in use.  Includes stationary, closed containers for transport or storage of small arms.
[F41C 33/001] Shooting harnesses; Stabilising devices, e.g. straps on the body  balancing arrangements on the gun itself  F41C27/22 -- A shooting harness or stabilising device is a wearable or body-attached system, such as straps, belts or balancing mechanisms, that secures a small-arms weapon and helps the shooter control recoil and aim. It includes harnesses fitted to the user and built-in stabilisers on the gun itself.
[F41C 33/002] Slings for carrying longguns, e.g. straps  attachment of slings  F41C23/02 ; shooting harnesses  F41C33/001 -- F41C 33/002 covers slings and harnesses designed to carry long guns, including straps that attach to the weapon and shooting harnesses that distribute weight for the user. It falls under the mechanical-engineering subgroup for weapons, specifically small-arms accessories used for wearing or carrying pistols, rifles and similar firearms.
[F41C 33/003] Buttstock supports, i.e. devices for carrying the weight of long firearms in a substantially vertical orientation by supporting the buttstock  holsters  F41C33/02 -- F41C 33/003 covers buttstock supports - devices that carry the weight of long firearms in a substantially vertical orientation by supporting the buttstock, such as specialised holsters. The subclass falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, smallarms and means for wearing or carrying smallarms.
[F41C 33/005] combined with a second point of support remote from the buttstock, enabling hands-free carrying -- This subclass covers smallarms equipped with an additional support point located away from the buttstock, such as a sling or harness, that allows the weapon to be carried without the shooter holding it. It includes designs where the secondary support provides hands-free operation.
[F41C 33/006] Clips, hooks or the like, for carrying the weight of smallarms  holsters  F41C33/02 -- Clips, hooks or similar fittings used to bear the weight of small-arms in a holster, enabling secure and comfortable carriage of pistols, rifles or other portable firearms. This element belongs to the small-arms carrying accessories group within mechanical engineering weapon classifications.
[F41C 33/007] for long firearms, e.g. rifles -- The CPC subclass F41C 33/007 covers features or devices for carrying or wearing long firearms such as rifles. It sits within the hierarchy mechanical engineering - weapons - smallarms, pistols and rifles - means for wearing or carrying smallarms.
[F41C 33/008] for handguns, i.e. pistols or revolvers -- The F41C 33/008 subgroup pertains to devices for wearing or carrying handguns, specifically pistols or revolvers, and includes items such as holsters, belt clips, shoulder straps and other retaining or transport accessories.
[F41C 33/02] Holsters, i.e. cases for pistols having means for being carried or worn, e.g. at the belt or under the arm -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes carrying means for firearms including long guns or parts thereof (e.g. mortar parts) worn on the human or animal body in a non-shooting position in so far as not covered by F41C33/003 - F41C33/008  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Magazine holstes, magazine pouches -> F42B39/02
[F41C 33/0209] Pouch or pocket like containers for small arms covering all or most of the small arm -- A pouch or pocket-type container designed to hold a small-arm, such as a pistol or rifle, and to cover all or most of the weapon for transport, protection, or concealment. It functions as a means of wearing or carrying the firearm while providing a surrounding envelope that shields the barrel, stock and other components.
[F41C 33/0218] having a flap substantially covering the opening of the pouch or pocket -- The CPC entry F41C 33/0218 covers small-arms carrying devices whose pouch or pocket is closed by a flap that substantially covers the opening, enhancing protection, concealment or retention of the weapon. It applies to holsters, belts, slings and similar accessories designed for pistols, rifles or other firearms.
[F41C 33/0227] having a strap or other restraining element only covering the hammer or a part of the upper part of the small arm -- The subclass covers devices for attaching a strap or other restraining element to a small-arm that protects only the hammer or a portion of the upper receiver. Such arrangements are intended to secure the weapon without enclosing the entire firearm.
[F41C 33/0236] Half-holsters covering by encircling only a part of the small arm, e.g. ghost-holsters -- F41C 33/0236 covers half-holsters that encircle only part of a small arm, such as ghost-holsters that wrap around the barrel or grip while leaving the remainder exposed. These accessories are intended for wearing or carrying pistols, rifles and similar firearms.
[F41C 33/0245] Skeleton-holsters, e.g. contacting only a minimal part of the small arm, e.g. contacting the muzzle, ejection port, chamber, trigger guard or hammer -- F41C 33/0245 covers skeleton holsters that support a firearm while contacting only a minimal part such as the muzzle, ejection port, chamber, trigger guard or hammer. These lightweight carriers are intended for small arms like pistols and rifles and provide limited contact for quick draw and reduced bulk.
[F41C 33/0254] with accommodation for auxiliary devices mounted on the small arm, e.g. telescopic sights, flashlights or laser-devices -- This CPC subclass covers small-arms that are designed with built-in features to attach auxiliary devices such as telescopic sights, flashlights or laser aimers. It applies to pistols, rifles and similar firearms where the weapon itself includes mounting provisions for these accessories.
[F41C 33/0263] having a locking system for preventing unauthorized or accidental removal of the small arm from the holster  F41C33/0227  takes precedence
[F41C 33/0272] having means for facilitating or accelerating the drawing of the small arm from the holster -- A device or mechanism incorporated into a holster that speeds up or eases the removal of a pistol or rifle, enabling the shooter to draw the weapon more quickly and smoothly. It is classified under mechanical engineering for weapons, specifically small-arms accessories that aid rapid deployment.
[F41C 33/0281] with means for assisting in cocking or loading the small arm -- This class includes small-arms equipped with devices that aid the user in cocking or loading the weapon, such as spring-loaded helpers, loading levers or other assistive mechanisms. It falls under mechanical engineering → weapons → smallarms → means for wearing or carrying smallarms.
[F41C 33/029] combined with electronic devices, e.g. GPS -- F41C 33/029 covers accessories for wearing or carrying small-arms that incorporate electronic components such as GPS or other navigation devices. It lies within the mechanical-engineering weapons subclass for small-arms, focusing on integrated technology that enhances location tracking or smart functionality.
[F41C 33/04] Special attachments therefor -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means for attaching holsters to a belt or webbing, i.e. intermediate parts between actual holster and belt/webbing
[F41C 33/041] for connecting a holster to a belt, webbing or other object -- F41C 33/041 covers devices that attach a holster to a belt, webbing, or similar supporting structure, enabling secure carriage of pistols or rifles. It falls under the weapons sub-category of small-arms accessories within mechanical engineering.
[F41C 33/043] for connection in more than one transversal position -- The CPC subclass F41C 33/043 refers to accessories for wearing or carrying smallarms that permit the weapon to be attached in more than one transversal position, such as modular straps, belts or mounts that allow the firearm to be positioned across the body in various orientations.
[F41C 33/045] for connection in more than one rotational position around an axle, e.g. by using a rotatable connection -- F41C 33/045 designates attachments for small-arms carrying or wearing devices that can be secured to an axle in more than one rotational setting, typically by means of a rotatable or pivoting connection. Such mechanisms let the user adjust orientation while keeping a secure fit.
[F41C 33/046] Webbing, harnesses, belts or straps for wearing holsters -- F41C 33/046 covers the design and manufacture of webbing, harnesses, belts or straps that attach holsters to a person's body, enabling secure carrying of pistols, rifles or other small firearms. The classification addresses the means of wearing or transporting small arms through textile or synthetic support structures.
[F41C 33/048] for concealed carrying of a small arm -- F41C 33/048 covers devices or accessories designed for the concealed carrying of a small arm, such as pistols or rifles. It pertains to means that enable a user to hide or transport a firearm in a discreet manner, typically integrated into clothing or personal gear.
[F41C 33/06] Containers for carrying smallarms, e.g. safety boxes, gun cases -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Holsters -> F41C33/02 - Rests for supporting small arms in non-shooting position -> F41A23/18
[F41C 33/08] Handles for carrying smallarms -- F41C 33/08 relates to handles specifically designed to enable the wearing or carrying of small arms such as pistols and rifles. It falls within the mechanical engineering branch, under weapons and the smallarms subgroup, covering accessories that facilitate easy transport and retention of the firearm.
[F41C 7/00] Shoulder-fired smallarms, e.g. rifles, carbines, shotguns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Long guns, normally supported against the shoulder for recoil absorbsion during the firing.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Small arms specially adapted for underwater use -> F41C9/06 - Muzzle-loading small arms -> F41C9/08
[F41C 7/02] Pump-action guns, i.e. guns having a reciprocating handgrip beneath the barrel for loading or cocking -- F41C 7/02 covers pump-action firearms, a type of shoulder-fired smallarm in which a moving handgrip beneath the barrel is used to load or cock the weapon. These mechanisms are typical of rifles, carbines and shotguns that employ a reciprocating fore-arm to advance ammunition.
[F41C 7/025] having hand-operated sliding barrels -- F41C 7/025 covers shoulder-fired smallarms that incorporate a hand-operated sliding barrel mechanism, allowing the barrel to be manually moved for loading, unloading, or firing operations. This feature is typical of certain rifles, carbines and shotguns where the operator slides the barrel by hand to cycle the weapon.
[F41C 7/04] with reciprocating handgrip under the buttstock for loading or cocking -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The primary handgrip under the receiver, including the trigger arrangement is used for the reciprocation (pumping).  Illustrative example of subject matter classified in this group.
[F41C 7/06] Lever-action guns, i.e. guns having a rocking lever for loading or cocking -- F41C 7/06 designates lever-action guns, a subgroup of shoulder-fired smallarms such as rifles and carbines that employ a rocking lever to load cartridges and cock the mechanism. These firearms are classified under Mechanical Engineering → Weapons → Smallarms → Shoulder-fired smallarms. The entry covers lever-action designs used in pistols, rifles and shotguns.
[F41C 7/11] Breakdown shotguns or rifles -- F41C 7/11 covers shoulder-fired weapons such as break-action shotguns and rifles where the barrel or breech block separates from the receiver for loading, typically by a hinged or removable action.
[F41C 7/12] Gallery rifles; Parlour rifles -- F41C 7/12 refers to gallery and parlour rifles, a subset of shoulder-fired smallarms designed for low-power indoor or limited-range shooting such as target practice in shooting galleries or private parlours. These rifles use reduced-energy cartridges to minimise recoil and hazard while maintaining basic rifle functionality.
[F41C 9/00] Other smallarms, e.g. hidden smallarms or smallarms specially adapted for underwater use -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This is a residual group for specific or exotic small arms, not particularly covered in F41C3/00 and F41C7/00
[F41C 9/02] Concealed pistols, e.g. in pencils -- This CPC subclass covers pistols that are designed to be hidden, often incorporated into ordinary objects such as pencils, pens or other personal items, allowing the firearm to be concealed from view. It falls under smallarms and specifically addresses compact, covert designs.
[F41C 9/04] Walking-stick guns -- Walking-stick guns are firearms integrated into the shaft of a walking stick, allowing a concealed weapon that can be discharged like a regular gun while appearing as a harmless aid. Classified under F41C 9/04 they fall within smallarms adapted for covert or specialized use, including hidden or underwater weapons.
[F41C 9/06] Smallarms specially adapted for underwater use -- The CPC subclass F41C 9/06 covers small arms that have been modified or designed for operation underwater, such as pistols or rifles with sealed mechanisms, waterproof ammunition, or special propulsion. These weapons are intended for use by divers and underwater forces, featuring adaptations to prevent water ingress and maintain functionality at depth.
[F41C 9/08] Muzzle-loading smallarms -- The F41C 9/08 class covers small arms that are loaded through the muzzle, including pistols, rifles and other firearms where the projectile and propellant are inserted at the front of the barrel. It also encompasses specially adapted versions such as concealed or underwater-use weapons, focusing on their design, loading mechanisms and related operational features.
[F41C 9/085] Accessories for loading muzzle loading guns, e.g. magazines or tools for loading -- F41C 9/085 covers devices that aid the loading of muzzle-loading firearms, including detachable magazines, loading levers, loaders or other tools that simplify inserting powder, projectile or both into the barrel. These accessories are intended for smallarms such as pistols and rifles, including concealed or underwater-adapted weapons.
[F41F] APPARATUS FOR LAUNCHING PROJECTILES OR MISSILES FROM BARRELS, e.g. CANNONS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Projectile launchers per se, except for smallarms which are covered in F41C , i.e. cannons, mortars, medium/large calibre guns, artillery guns, ordnance.  Launchers for self propelled missiles, i.e. rockets and torpedos.  Gravity propelled missile launchers and missile launching apparatuses without barrels.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Mounting of armament on ships -> B63G - Mounting of armament on aircraft -> B64D - Functional features common to both smallarms and ordnance -> F41A - Projecting missiles without use of explosive or combustible propellant charge -> F41B - Smallarms -> F41C - Self-propelled missiles -> F42B15/00 - Torpedoes -> F42B19/00
[F41F 1/00] Launching apparatus for projecting projectiles or missiles from barrels, e.g. cannons -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes the projectile launching apparatuses with a barrel which is larger than smallarms. A barrel being defined as a gun tube with a closable breech at the proximal end.  Includes mortars.  Includes harpoon guns projecting harpoons with a pyrotechnic charge.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Rocket or torpedo launchers -> F41F3/00 - Spring guns adapted to discharge harpoons -> F41B7/04 - Compressed gas guns adapted to discharge harpoons -> F41B11/83
[F41F 1/06] Mortars -- F41F 1/06 (Mortars) classifies mortars, short-barrelled artillery that launch shells or missiles at high trajectories from a barrel. The entry covers the design, construction and mounting of these firing devices, including breech mechanisms, recoil systems and related accessories used in military applications.
[F41F 1/08] Multibarrel guns, e.g. twin guns -- F41F 1/08 covers multibarrel guns, such as twin-barrel weapons, where two or more barrels are mounted on a single firing assembly to fire projectiles either simultaneously or in rapid succession. These systems are designed for increased fire rate, redundancy, or specific tactical effects and include configurations like side-by-side or stacked barrels.
[F41F 1/085] with oscillating barrels; with barrels having variable relative orientation  scatter-fire arrangements  F41A27/04 -- F41F 1/085 covers launchers whose barrels can oscillate or change relative orientation to produce scatter-fire patterns, such as cannons that fire multiple projectiles with varying aim. The subclass falls within the weapons group for barrel-based projectile launchers.
[F41F 1/10] Revolving-cannon guns, i.e. multibarrel guns with the barrels and their respective breeches mounted on a rotor -- F41F 1/10 covers rotating-cannon weapons in which several barrels and their breeches are mounted on a common rotor, so that the assembly turns to bring each barrel into firing position. This multibarrel arrangement is used to raise the rate of fire or to provide a sequence of firing angles for projectiles or missiles.
[F41F 3/00] Rocket or torpedo launchers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Launchers for rockets, including portable rocket tubes and vehicle/infrastructure mounted rocket pods or silos.  Torpedo launchers from above (ship, land and air) and below the water surface.
[F41F 3/04] for rockets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Launchers for rockets, i.e. missiles including a warhead and a rocket propulsion system or self propelled missiles.
[F41F 3/0406] Rail launchers -- Rail launchers are devices that propel rockets, missiles or torpedoes along a fixed guide rail, using electromagnetic, pneumatic or other thrust methods instead of a conventional barrel. They belong to the category of apparatus for launching projectiles or missiles from barrels and are classified under mechanical engineering weapons. The CPC entry F41F 3/0406 specifically covers these rail-based launch systems.
[F41F 3/0413] Means for exhaust gas disposal, e.g. exhaust deflectors, gas evacuation systems -- F41F 3/0413 covers devices that manage the gases produced when a projectile or missile is launched, such as exhaust deflectors, vents, ducts or evacuation systems that direct or disperse the blast plume. These means are used in rocket or torpedo launchers to reduce recoil, protect nearby equipment and improve launch safety.
[F41F 3/042] the launching apparatus being used also as a transport container for the rocket -- F41F 3/042 covers launch devices that double as transport containers for rockets or torpedoes, integrating storage and handling functions with the firing mechanism. The classification applies to apparatus where the launch tube or barrel also serves as the means of moving the munition to the firing site.
[F41F 3/045] adapted to be carried and used by a person, e.g. bazookas -- F41F 3/045 refers to rocket or torpedo launchers that are adapted to be carried and operated by a single person, such as shoulder-fired bazookas. The classification falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, and apparatus for launching projectiles from barrels.
[F41F 3/0455] Bazookas -- F41F 3/0455 covers bazookas, which are man-portable rocket launchers designed to fire anti-armor projectiles from a tube. The class is part of mechanical-engineering weapons, specifically apparatus for launching projectiles or missiles from barrels such as cannons.
[F41F 3/048] Means for imparting spin to the rocket before launching -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Stabilising arrangements using spin for missiles (after launch) -> F42B10/26
[F41F 3/052] Means for securing the rocket in the launching apparatus -- F41F 3/052 covers devices that lock or hold a rocket in a launch tube or barrel, ensuring proper alignment, retention and safety before ignition. The means may include clamps, latches, brackets or other securing mechanisms integrated into rocket or torpedo launchers. It pertains to mechanical engineering of weapon launch apparatus.
[F41F 3/055] Umbilical connecting means -- The entry covers umbilical connecting means, which are the cables or flexible lines that link a launch platform to a rocket or torpedo launcher to provide power, control signals, or fluid supply during preparation and launch. These devices are designed to detach safely at launch, ensuring reliable connection while the projectile remains in the barrel.
[F41F 3/058] Means for removing duds or misfires -- F41F 3/058 covers devices that extract unfired or stuck projectiles from rocket or torpedo launch tubes, allowing safe removal of duds or misfires and rapid restoration of the launcher for subsequent firing.
[F41F 3/06] from aircraft -- F41F 3/06 covers launch devices mounted on aircraft that fire rockets or torpedoes, including the mounting, aiming and firing mechanisms for airborne projectile launchers. It falls under the mechanical engineering weapons hierarchy for barrel-type launchers.
[F41F 3/065] Rocket pods, i.e. detachable containers for launching a plurality of rockets -- F41F 3/065 designates rocket pods, which are detachable containers that hold and launch multiple rockets as a single unit. These devices are mounted on weapons platforms and enable rapid, simultaneous firing of several rockets from a barrel-type launcher.
[F41F 3/07] Underwater launching-apparatus -- F41F 3/07 covers apparatus designed to launch rockets, torpedoes or other projectiles from underwater platforms. It includes launch tubes, ejection mechanisms and supporting systems used on submarines, torpedo boats or other submerged vessels to fire missiles or torpedoes while submerged.
[F41F 3/073] Silos for rockets, e.g. mounting or sealing rockets therein -- The CPC subclass F41F 3/073 defines silos designed to mount, seal or store rockets within a launch barrel system, providing protective housing and launch preparation for missile or projectile firing. It falls under mechanical-engineered weapons apparatus for rocket or torpedo launchers.
[F41F 3/077] Doors or covers for launching tubes -- F41F 3/077 covers protective doors, hatches or cover assemblies that seal and protect rocket or torpedo launch tubes when not in use, enabling safe storage and quick opening for firing. The devices are designed to withstand pressure, environmental exposure and handling while integrating with the launcher's structural and control systems.
[F41F 3/08] for marine torpedoes -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Disposition of guns on vehicles, gun mountings for disappearing guns on board of submarines -> F41A23/22
[F41F 3/10] from below the surface of the water -- This CPC group covers launch devices that fire rockets, missiles or torpedoes from a position below the water surface, such as submarine-borne launch tubes or underwater launchers. It includes mechanisms for initiating projectile ejection while the launcher remains submerged and related control or ejection systems.
[F41F 5/00] Launching-apparatus for gravity-propelled missiles or projectiles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes devices for dropping warheads from a certain height only propelled by gravity, e.g. from land vehicles or buildings.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Laying of mines and depth charges -> B63G6/00 - Dropping bombs from aircrafts -> B64D1/04
[F41F 5/04] from ships, e.g. for mines, for depth charges -- This CPC subclass covers launching mechanisms mounted on ships for gravity-propelled munitions such as naval mines or depth charges, including devices integrated with a hull or deck that fire these weapons without explosive propulsion.
[F41F 7/00] Launching-apparatus for projecting missiles or projectiles otherwise than from barrels, -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Residual maingroup for projectile or missile launchers not covered by F41B1/00 - F41C9/08 and F41F1/00 - F41F5/04 .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Rocket launchers -> F41F3/04 - Centrifugal sling apparatus -> F41B3/04
[F41G] WEAPON SIGHTS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Sighting devices.  Aiming and Laying means.  Elevating or traversing control systems for weapons.  Direction control systems for missiles or projectiles.  **Glossary:** - Aiming: Bringing a weapon to a direction differing from the sighting direction by corrections in order that the projectile may hit the target - Sighting: Bringing into visual coincidence a direction defined by a so-called "sighting" device with the direction of a target - Laying: Setting a weapon in the correct position for hitting a target
[F41G 1/00] Sighting devices -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Mechanical aspects of sighting devices, which are either fixedly or detachably mounted on weapons, i. e. iron sights, telescopic sights, periscopic sight as well as tube and bar sights. The group further includes means for protecting, adjusting and for testing of such mechanical sighting devices. This group further includes weapon mounted means for illuminating the sights or the the target.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Aiming means; Laying means -> F41G3/00 - Structural association of sighting-devices with laser telemeters -> F41G3/065 - Indirect laying of fire -> F41G3/16 - Bombsights -> F41G3/24 - Means for mounting tubular or beam shaped sighting or aiming devices on firearms -> F41G11/001 - Optical aspects of sighting devices -> G02B23/00 , G02B27/00 - Shooting or aiming glasses -> G02C5/003
[F41G 1/01] characterised by the visual combination effect of the respective geometrical forms of fore and rear sight -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Tube sights; Bar sights -> F41G1/42
[F41G 1/02] Foresights -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Sights mounted at the distal end of the weapon and having a small dimension parallel to the barrel axis.
[F41G 1/027] with lens -- This subclass defines weapon sighting devices that incorporate an optical lens as part of the aiming system. The lens is used to magnify or focus the view of the target, providing enhanced accuracy for firearms or related weapons. It covers optical, telescopic or lens-based sights integrated into the weapon.
[F41G 1/033] adjustable -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Tools for adjustment of sights -> F41G1/545
[F41G 1/04] Protection means therefor -- F41G 1/04 relates to protective means for weapon-sighting devices, such as shields, covers or other structures that guard the sight from impact, weather and tampering. These features are intended to preserve sight functionality while increasing durability.
[F41G 1/06] Rearsights -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Sights mounted at the proximal end of the weapon and having a small dimension parallel to the barrel axis.
[F41G 1/065] Protection means therefor  F41G1/04  takes precedence -- F41G 1/065 covers protective means for weapon sighting devices, including shields, covers, housings or other elements that safeguard the sight from damage, debris, weather or tampering. It falls under the broader F41G 1/04 category for sighting-device structures.
[F41G 1/08] with aperture -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Tube sights; Bar sights -> F41G1/42
[F41G 1/10] with notch -- F41G 1/10 covers weapon sighting devices that use a notch as the aiming element. The classification includes any mechanical sight where a narrow opening or groove provides the reference line for aiming.
[F41G 11/00] Details of sighting or aiming apparatus -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Details and accessories relevant to sighting apparatuses, not covered in F41G1/00 .
[F41G 11/001] Means for mounting tubular or beam shaped sighting or aiming devices on firearms -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The devices being lamps, e.g. flashsights, telescopes or other tubular optical, optronic, electronic or electric devices mounted on smallarms.
[F41G 11/002] Mountings with recoil absorbing means -- F41G 11/002 covers mountings for weapon sights that incorporate recoil-absorbing mechanisms, allowing the sight to stay aligned with the barrel during firing. These devices use springs, dampers or other energy-absorbing elements to reduce movement and maintain aiming accuracy.
[F41G 11/003] Mountings with a dove tail element, e.g. "Picatinny rail systems" -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes picatinny or weaver rails with integrated electric connections.
[F41G 11/004] Mountings with clamping means on the device embracing at least a part of the firearm, e.g. the receiver or a dustcover  F41G11/003  takes precedence -- F41G 11/004 covers mounting arrangements for weapon sights that use clamping mechanisms to attach directly to a part of the firearm, such as the receiver or a dust cover. The clamp embraces the component, providing a secure base for the sighting device.
[F41G 11/005] Mountings using a pivot point and an anchoring point -- F41G 11/005 covers mountings for weapon sighting devices that employ a pivot point together with an anchoring point, enabling the sight to be swung or tilted while remaining secured to the weapon. The classification includes mechanisms that allow precise adjustment of the line of sight without compromising stability.
[F41G 11/006] the device being rotated in a horizontal plane -- F41G 11/006 covers mechanisms that rotate a weapon sight in the horizontal plane, such as swivels, rotating mounts or gears that allow the aiming device to be turned left-right for aiming adjustments. It is a subcategory of details of sighting or aiming apparatus within weapon sights.
[F41G 11/007] the device being tilted in a vertical plane -- The entry covers mechanisms that enable a weapon sight to be inclined up or down relative to the barrel, providing vertical elevation adjustment for aiming. It includes tilting devices, hinges, actuators or other arrangements that change the sight's angle in the vertical plane.
[F41G 11/008] the device being pivotable about an axis coaxial with the axis of the barrel, e.g. for loading -- F41G 11/008 pertains to weapon sighting or aiming devices that can pivot around an axis coaxial with the barrel, allowing the sight to be swung out of line-often to facilitate loading or other handling operations.
[F41G 1/12] with line or mark other than notch -- F41G 1/12 designates weapon sighting devices that employ a line, dot, bar or other marking rather than a traditional notch to provide the aiming reference. It covers sights where the visual cue is a continuous or discrete mark used for alignment of the target and barrel. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering - weapons - weapon sights - sighting devices.
[F41G 1/14] with lens -- F41G 1/14 covers weapon sighting devices that incorporate a lens, such as optical or telescopic sights using glass or other transparent material to focus the image. The classification applies to any sight where a lens is a principal component for magnifying or clarifying the target view, including riflescopes, combat optics, and other lens-based aiming aids.
[F41G 1/16] Adjusting mechanisms therefor -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Tools for adjustment of sights -> F41G1/545
[F41G 1/17] Convertible sights, i.e. sets of two or more sights brought into the sight line optionally -- F41G 1/17 in the CPC refers to convertible sights for weapons, meaning a set of two or more sighting elements that can be placed in the line of fire as needed. The classification covers mechanisms that allow the shooter to switch between different sight types, such as iron, optical or night-vision devices, within the same mount.
[F41G 1/18] Clicking-indicators with spring detents -- Clicking-indicators with spring detents are sight-adjustment components that produce a tactile or audible click as the sight is turned, using a spring-biased detent to lock each step. They enable precise, repeatable positioning of weapon sights.
[F41G 1/20] coarse and fine -- F41G 1/20 covers mechanisms that provide coarse and fine adjustments in weapon sighting devices, allowing the user to shift the aim rapidly for large corrections and then fine-tune for precise targeting. The classification applies to any system that integrates both adjustment scales into a sight or optical accessory for firearms.
[F41G 1/22] Friction clamps -- F41G 1/22 covers friction clamps, which are devices that secure sighting components of weapons by applying pressure to grip them without screws or adhesives. These clamps enable quick adjustment and stable mounting of optics or aiming devices on firearms.
[F41G 1/24] rack-and-pinion -- The F41G 1/24 subclass covers rack-and-pinion mechanisms used in weapon sighting devices. It includes arrangements where linear motion of a rack is converted to angular movement of a pinion to adjust the sight's aim point, enabling precise and rapid elevation or windage changes. Such systems are employed in rifles, artillery and other firearms for accurate targeting.
[F41G 1/26] screw -- F41G 1/26 designates screws employed in weapon sighting devices, covering fastening elements that secure or adjust optical or mechanical sights on firearms. The classification includes all forms of mounting, locking or aligning screws specifically used in the construction or adjustment of weapon sight assemblies.
[F41G 1/28] wedge -- A wedge is a sighting-device component that forms a sloping surface to align a projectile's trajectory with the shooter's line of sight, often used to adjust elevation or windage in weapon sights. It is classified under mechanical engineering, weapons, and weapon sights in the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[F41G 1/30] Reflecting-sights specially adapted for smallarms or ordnance -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Sights with light source projecting the image of an aiming point or a reticle into the eye of the shooter either via a half-mirror or direct. [F41G 1/32] Night sights, e.g. luminescent -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also includes daylight sights with active illumination of target or sights.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Mounting of nightsights -> F41G11/001 - Night vision devices -> G02B23/12
[F41G 1/34] combined with light source, e.g. spot light -- F41G 1/34 covers weapon sighting devices that incorporate an illumination element such as a spot light to provide a lit aiming point. The integration of the light source directly with the sight improves visibility of the target in low-light conditions without requiring a separate lamp.
[F41G 1/345] for illuminating the sights -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes active illumination of the sights by a powered light source.  Includes passive illumination of the sights by gathering and guiding ambient light to the sights.  Includes fluorescent and chemoluminescent markers on iron sights.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Virtual image of a reticle or an aiming point projected in the eye of the shooter -> F41G1/30

[F41G 1/36] with infrared light source -- F41G 1/36 designates weapon sighting devices that employ an infrared light source to illuminate the target area, enabling visibility in low-light or night conditions. It falls under the broader categories of mechanical engineering, weapons, and weapon sights, specifically within the subgroup of sighting devices.
[F41G 1/38] Telescopic sights specially adapted for smallarms or ordnance -- F41G 1/38 covers telescopic sights that are specifically designed for use on small arms or ordnance. These devices incorporate optical magnification to improve target acquisition and aiming accuracy for firearms and artillery.
[F41G 1/383] Protection means therefor -- This subclass defines protective elements incorporated with weapon sighting devices, such as covers, shields, housings or other means that guard the sight against impact, debris, weather or tampering while preserving its aiming function.
[F41G 1/387] Mounting telescopic sights on smallarms -- F41G 1/387 covers the mounting of telescopic sights on smallarms, detailing the mechanical arrangements and attachment mechanisms that secure the sight to the weapon while preserving alignment and durability. It belongs to the hierarchy Mechanical Engineering → Weapons → Weapon Sights → Sighting Devices.
[F41G 1/393] Mounting telescopic sights on ordnance -- F41G 1/393 relates to methods and structures for attaching telescopic sighting devices to firearms, artillery or other ordnance, including brackets, rails, clamps and other mounting assemblies that secure the optics and permit adjustment while withstanding operational stresses.
[F41G 1/3935] Transmission of sight movements to the associated gun -- The entry covers devices or mechanisms that link a firearm's sighting apparatus to the gun so that adjustments or movements of the sight are directly transferred to the weapon, enabling coordinated alignment or automatic compensation of the barrel position when the sight is moved.
[F41G 1/40] Periscopic sights specially adapted for smallarms or ordnance -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes sights enabling shooting around the corner.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Sighting devices adapted for indirect laying of fire using a TV-monitor -> F41G3/165
[F41G 1/41] Mounting periscopic sights on smallarms -- This subclass covers the attachment of periscopic optical sights to hand-held firearms such as rifles and pistols, including mounting brackets, rail systems and integration methods. It falls under the CPC hierarchy for mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights and sighting devices.
[F41G 1/42] Tube sights -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Tubular sights or cylindrical sights, the cross-section not being necessarily circular, functionning by the tunnel effect, void of any optical components.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Telescopic sights -> F41G1/38
[F41G 1/425] Bar sights -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Open sights (as opposed to the tubular sights) with a substantial longitudinal dimension with respect to the barrel length. Either single sight so as to aim along its lenght or combination of fore and rear sight.
[F41G 1/44] Spirit-level adjusting means, e.g. for correcting tilt; -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means for indicating the spacial orientation of the firearm, the adjusting is done by the shooter himself.
[F41G 1/46] for particular applications -- F41G 1/46 covers weapon sighting devices that are adapted for specific uses, such as sights designed for particular firearm types, calibers, or tactical applications. It includes specialized configurations intended for unique operational requirements rather than general-purpose sights.
[F41G 1/467] for bows -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Telescope sights for bows -> F41G1/38 - Accessories for bows (other than sights) -> F41B5/14
[F41G 1/473] for lead-indicating or range-finding, e.g. for use with rifles or shotguns -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Arrangements for maintaining the aiming of a weapon with respect to a moving target -> F41G5/00 - Adaptations of rangefinders for combination with telescopes or binoculars -> G01C3/04
[F41G 1/48] for firing grenades from rifles -- F41G 1/48 relates to rifle-mounted sighting devices specifically designed to allow the firing of grenades, providing a combined aiming and safety mechanism that aligns the weapon and facilitates accurate grenade launch from the firearm.
[F41G 1/50] for trench mortars -- F41G 1/50 pertains to sighting devices specifically designed for trench mortars, covering mechanisms that allow operators to aim and align these short-range, high-angle weapons accurately from confined positions. It includes mounted, handheld, or integrated sights adapted to the unique geometry and firing conditions of trench mortar systems.
[F41G 1/52] for rifles or shotguns having two or more barrels, or adapted to fire different kinds of ammunition, e.g. ball or shot
[F41G 1/54] Devices for testing or checking -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices and tools to test the function of the sights and/or the parallelity of sight and barrel.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Arrangements for checking the straighness of gun barrels -> F41A31/02
[F41G 1/545] Tools for adjustment of sights -- This subclass covers devices used to adjust or calibrate weapon sighting mechanisms, such as collimators, windage and elevation knobs, or specialized tools that enable precise alignment of optical or iron sights. It is part of the mechanical engineering group for weapons, under weapon sights and sighting devices.
[F41G 3/00] Aiming or laying means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for the aiming of weapons.  Arrangements for teaching or practicing the aiming of weapons.  Arrangements for testing or checking weapon aiming means.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Structural details of sighting devices -> F41G1/00 - Sighting devices combined with light source for illuminating a target -> F41G1/35 - Sighting devices for range-finding or lead indicating -> F41G1/473
[F41G 3/005] with means for correcting the parallax between the sighting means and the muzzle axis -- This subclass covers weapon sight systems that incorporate a mechanism to eliminate or reduce parallax error by aligning the optical axis of the sight with the barrel's muzzle axis. The correction means may be adjustable or fixed, allowing the shooter to maintain accurate aim regardless of eye position.
[F41G 3/02] using an independent line of sight -- F41G 3/02 relates to weapon sight arrangements in which the line of sight is provided by an element separate from the barrel or projectile path, allowing the shooter to aim without relying on the bore axis. This independent line of sight may be fixed or adjustable and is used in firearms, artillery or similar weapons to improve targeting accuracy.
[F41G 3/04] for dispersing fire from a battery -- This CPC subclass covers mechanisms or arrangements that disperse the fire of a weapon battery, enabling multiple barrels or projectiles to be engaged simultaneously. It includes devices that coordinate aiming or firing across a group of weapons to achieve a spread effect.
[F41G 3/06] with rangefinder -- F41G 3/06 pertains to weapon sighting devices that incorporate a rangefinder, enabling the user to determine target distance while aiming. These systems combine distance measurement with aiming optics for firearms, artillery or other weapons.
[F41G 3/065] Structural association of sighting-devices with laser telemeters -- The F41G 3/065 subclass covers designs that physically combine a sighting device, such as a scope or reflex sight, with a laser telemeter (rangefinder), including mounting structures, integral housings, or other means that link the two components so that distance measurement and aiming are jointly provided. It addresses the mechanical integration and alignment of the laser unit with the sight to enable combined functionality.
[F41G 3/08] with means for compensating for speed, direction, temperature, pressure, or humidity of the atmosphere -- This subclass covers weapon sighting devices that include mechanisms to automatically adjust the aim for atmospheric factors such as projectile speed, wind direction, temperature, pressure or humidity, ensuring accurate targeting despite environmental changes. It applies to optical, electronic or hybrid sights that incorporate compensating elements like variable prisms, sensors or computational corrections. This enables shooters to maintain precision without manual recalibration.
[F41G 3/10] with means for compensating for canting of the trunnions -- F41G 3/10 classifies aiming or laying devices for weapon sights that incorporate mechanisms to offset trunnion canting, ensuring the sight remains properly aligned despite angular displacement of the mounting trunnions. This subcategory falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, and weapon-sight categories in the cooperative patent classification used by the EPO and USPTO.
[F41G 3/12] with means for compensating for muzzle velocity or powder temperature -- The F41G 3/12 subclass covers weapon sight devices that incorporate mechanisms to adjust the point of aim in response to changes in muzzle velocity or propellant temperature. Such compensating means allow the shooter to maintain accurate targeting despite ballistic variations caused by temperature or charge fluctuations.
[F41G 3/14] Indirect aiming means -- F41G 3/14 covers indirect aiming means for weapons, i.e. devices that enable the shooter to align the weapon with the target without looking directly through a traditional sight line. Examples include reflex or holographic sights, laser projection systems, or collimated optical devices that present a reticle superimposed on the field of view.
[F41G 3/142] based on observation of a first shoot; using a simulated shoot  training  F41G3/26 -- F41G 3/142 covers weapon sight aiming or laying methods that rely on observing the result of an initial shot and then using a simulated-shoot training system to adjust the aim for subsequent firing. It pertains to training techniques that replicate real-world shooting conditions to improve sight alignment.
[F41G 3/145] using a target illuminator -- F41G 3/145 relates to devices that illuminate a target to improve the aiming of weapon sights, such as lasers, LEDs or infrared emitters that project light onto the intended point of impact. It covers both built-in and attachable illumination systems used in low-light or night conditions.
[F41G 3/147] based on detection of a firing weapon -- F41G 3/147 concerns weapon sight systems that determine aim by detecting the discharge of the firearm, such as electronic or optical devices that sense muzzle blast or flash to provide aiming information. It falls under the mechanical engineering class for weapons, specifically the subgroup for aiming or laying means.
[F41G 3/16] Sighting devices adapted for indirect laying of fire -- F41G 3/16 pertains to sighting devices designed for indirect fire, enabling a weapon to be aimed without a direct line of sight to the target. The entry includes indirect fire sights, panoramic or elevation-azimuth scopes, and related mechanisms that calculate firing angles for mortars, artillery or similar weapons.
[F41G 3/165] using a TV-monitor -- The code F41G 3/165 covers weapon sight systems that incorporate a television monitor for aiming or laying purposes. It applies to mechanical engineering designs of sights that display a video image to assist the shooter in targeting.
[F41G 3/18] Auxiliary target devices adapted for indirect laying of fire -- F41G 3/18 pertains to auxiliary target devices that aid indirect fire, including laser rangefinders, ballistic computers, and sighting add-ons used to determine elevation and bearing without a direct line-of-sight.
[F41G 3/20] specially adapted for mountain artillery -- The entry F41G 3/20 covers sighting and laying devices that are specially adapted for mountain artillery, providing means to adjust for steep terrain, high elevation angles and limited mobility so that guns can be accurately aimed in rugged, mountainous environments.
[F41G 3/22] for vehicle-borne armament, e.g. on aircraft -- F41G 3/22 designates aiming or laying devices that are integrated with armament mounted on vehicles, including aircraft. It covers sighting systems, targeting aids and related mechanisms used to direct fire from platform-borne weapons.
[F41G 3/225] Helmet sighting systems -- F41G 3/225 covers sighting devices integrated into or mounted on helmets, providing the shooter with a line of sight aligned with the weapon while maintaining head protection. Such systems may include optical, laser, or electronic components that allow aiming without removing the helmet.
[F41G 3/24] Bombsights -- F41G 3/24 covers bombsights, the aiming or laying devices installed on aircraft to direct bombs toward a target. These systems calculate the bomb's trajectory by accounting for altitude, speed, wind and other variables, allowing the crew to release the payload with greater accuracy. Both mechanical and electronic implementations used in military aviation fall under this classification.
[F41G 3/26] Teaching or practice apparatus for gun-aiming or gun-laying -- F41G 3/26 covers teaching or practice apparatus designed to train users in aiming or laying firearms, such as laser training devices, dummy sight kits, mock target systems and other non-lethal tools that simulate gun sighting and alignment without discharging ammunition.
[F41G 3/2605] using a view recording device cosighted with the gun  F41G3/2616  takes precedence -- The F41G 3/2605 subclass covers weapon sight arrangements that incorporate a view-recording device, such as a camera, positioned coaxially with the gun to capture the line of sight during aiming or firing. It is subordinated to the more specific F41G 3/2616 entry, which takes precedence.
[F41G 3/2611] coacting with a TV-monitor -- F41G 3/2611 covers weapon sight assemblies where a television monitor is integrated with the aiming device, allowing the shooter to view a video image of the target through the sight. The classification includes mechanisms that link the optical or electronic sight to a TV screen for real-time aiming assistance.
[F41G 3/2616] using a light emitting device -- F41G 3/2616 covers the use of light-emitting devices, such as LEDs or lasers, incorporated into weapon sights to provide illumination for aiming. The classification applies to systems that generate, transmit or project light to enable the shooter to acquire a target in low-visibility conditions, including illuminated reticles, glow-in-the-dark markings and active illumination of the sight picture.
[F41G 3/2622] for simulating the firing of a gun or the trajectory of a projectile -- F41G 3/2622 covers weapon sight elements that simulate the firing of a gun or the trajectory of a projectile, providing the shooter with visual cues such as bullet drop, velocity and impact point to improve aiming accuracy.
[F41G 3/2627] Cooperating with a motion picture projector -- F41G 3/2627 pertains to weapon sight arrangements that incorporate a motion picture projector to project visual information onto the aiming device, allowing dynamic targeting cues. The classification covers the mechanical coupling and alignment methods that enable the projector to work in concert with the sight.
[F41G 3/2633] using a TV type screen, e.g. a CRT, displaying a simulated target -- This subclass covers weapon-sight arrangements that use a television-type display, such as a CRT, to show a simulated target image for aiming, replacing or supplementing a conventional optical reticle.
[F41G 3/2638] giving hit coordinates by means of raster control signals, e.g. standard light pen -- The CPC entry F41G 3/2638 falls under Mechanical Engineering → Weapons → Weapon Sights → Aiming or Laying Means. It covers systems that provide hit coordinates to a weapon sight by using raster-controlled signals, such as those generated by a standard light pen, enabling precise target acquisition.
[F41G 3/2644] Displaying the trajectory or the impact point of a simulated projectile in the gunner's sight -- The entry covers mechanisms or software that present the predicted flight path or point of impact of a simulated projectile directly within a gunner's sight, often using computer-generated graphics or integrated targeting displays to aid aiming. It relates to weapon sights that provide real-time trajectory visualization for enhanced targeting accuracy.
[F41G 3/265] with means for selecting or varying the shape or the direction of the emitted beam -- F41G 3/265 refers to weapon sight arrangements that incorporate a mechanism for changing the shape or direction of the emitted beam, such as adjustable optics, movable apertures or steering elements that let the user modify the beam's pattern or aim point while the sight is in use.
[F41G 3/2655] in which the light beam is sent from the weapon to the target -- This subclass covers weapon-mounted sighting devices that emit a light beam from the firearm toward the target, such as laser or LED aiming modules used to assist aiming. It specifically addresses forward-projected illumination rather than reflected or ambient light.
[F41G 3/2661] in which the light beam is sent from the target to the weapon  F41G3/2638  takes precedence -- This subclass covers weapon sighting arrangements in which a light beam is generated at the target and directed back toward the firearm to aid aim, such as retro-reflective or laser-designated target illumination. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights, and aiming or laying means.
[F41G 3/2666] with means for selecting or varying PRF or time coding of the emitted beam -- F41G 3/2666 covers weapon sight or aiming devices that include a mechanism for selecting or varying the pulse-repetition-frequency or applying time-coding to the emitted beam, allowing the user to adjust illumination or signal patterns for better target acquisition.
[F41G 3/2672] using PRF adapted receiver
[F41G 3/2677] with PRF determination -- The CPC entry F41G 3/2677 falls under Mechanical Engineering → Weapons → Weapon Sights → Aiming or laying means and concerns sighting devices that incorporate a pulse-repetition-frequency (PRF) determination capability, enabling the system to measure or calculate the PRF of a target or projectile for improved accuracy.
[F41G 3/2683] with reflection of the beam on the target back to the weapon -- This subclass concerns aiming or laying means for weapons that project a beam toward a target and use the beam's reflection on the target to return to the weapon, providing a visual cue for alignment and accurate aiming.
[F41G 3/2688] using target range measurement, e.g. with a laser rangefinder -- F41G 3/2688 covers weapon sight aiming or laying means that determine the distance to a target, typically by employing a laser rangefinder or similar distance-measuring device. The technology integrates range data into the sighting system to improve accuracy and fire control.
