[F41G 3/28] Small-scale apparatus -- F41G 3/28 designates small-scale apparatus for the aiming or laying of weapons, including portable sights, optical or electronic aiming aids, and related support mechanisms. It falls under the mechanical engineering section for weapon sights, specifically focusing on compact devices that assist users in aligning fire.
[F41G 3/30] Gun-laying apparatus -- F41G 3/30 covers gun-laying apparatus, devices that control the elevation and traverse of firearms to aim them accurately, including mechanical, hydraulic or electronic systems used on artillery, tanks or naval guns.
[F41G 3/32] Devices for testing or checking -- F41G 3/32 relates to devices used to test or check weapon sighting systems, covering apparatus that calibrates, measures accuracy, or verifies alignment of sights, range-finders and related aiming equipment. The subclass includes test rigs, simulation tools and diagnostic instruments that ensure proper performance of aiming or laying means. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights, and aiming or laying means.
[F41G 3/323] for checking the angle between the muzzle axis of the gun and a reference axis, e.g. the axis of the associated sighting device  testing alignment of axes in general  G01B11/27 -- The subclass F41G 3/323 covers methods and devices used to verify the angular relationship between a firearm's muzzle axis and a reference axis such as that of a sighting device, encompassing general testing of axis alignment for weapons. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights, and aiming or laying means, and is linked to the broader measurement group G01B11/27.
[F41G 3/326] for checking the angle between the axis of the gun sighting device and an auxiliary measuring device  F41G3/323  takes precedence -- This CPC subclass F41G 3/326 covers methods or devices for measuring the angular relationship between the line of sight of a gun sight and an auxiliary measuring instrument, enabling verification of alignment. It falls under Mechanical Engineering - Weapons - Weapon Sights - Aiming or Laying Means and is subordinate to the broader subclass F41G 3/323.
[F41G 5/00] Elevating or traversing control systems for guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for setting a weapon in a predetermined firing position.  Arrangements for maintaining the aiming direction of a weapon with respect to a moving target.  Arrangements for maintaining the aiming direction of a weapon mounted on a mobile platform.  Arrangements for testing or checking elevating or traversing control systems for weapons  Though the title of the group refers to elevating or traversing control systems for guns, this group applies to elevating or traversing control systems for weapons in general (e.g. missile/rocket launchers).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Determining the aiming direction of a weapon -> F41G3/00 - Gun mountings permitting traversing or elevating movement, e.g. gun carriages -> F41A27/00 - Details of sensors for the tracking of targets -> G01S
[F41G 5/02] using only mechanical means for remote control -- The CPC entry F41G 5/02 covers elevating or traversing control systems for guns that are operated solely by mechanical means for remote control, such as levers, gears, cams or linkage mechanisms, without electrical, hydraulic or pneumatic assistance. It is classified under weapon sights within mechanical engineering.
[F41G 5/04] using hydraulic means for remote control -- This subclass covers gun elevation or traverse mechanisms that are operated remotely by hydraulic power. It includes hydraulic cylinders or fluid-driven actuators that adjust sight alignment or barrel position from a distance.
[F41G 5/06] using electric means for remote control -- F41G 5/06 relates to weapon sight assemblies whose elevation or traversal is achieved through electric actuators, allowing the sight to be aimed or moved remotely via electronic control rather than manual adjustment.
[F41G 5/08] Ground-based tracking-systems for aerial targets -- The CPC subclass F41G 5/08 covers ground-based systems that track aerial targets and provide elevation or traversing control for gun-mounted weapons. It falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights, and elevating or traversing control systems for guns, addressing technologies such as radar, optical, or electro-optical trackers that enable guns to follow and engage aircraft or drones from a fixed position.
[F41G 5/12] acoustically influenced -- F41G 5/12 covers gun sight elevation or traversing mechanisms that respond to acoustic inputs. The technology uses sound signals, such as Doppler or microphone detection, to automatically adjust the sight for target tracking or vibration reduction. It applies to active or passive acoustic control of sight movement.
[F41G 5/14] for vehicle-borne guns -- F41G 5/14 covers mechanisms that raise or swing the aim of firearms installed on vehicles, such as tanks or naval guns, enabling vertical or horizontal adjustment of the weapon's line of fire. These systems are part of weapon sight and mounting technology in mechanical engineering.
[F41G 5/16] gyroscopically influenced -- F41G 5/16 covers elevating or traversing control systems for guns that employ a gyroscope to influence the movement of the weapon's sight. The gyroscopic action stabilises or adjusts the sight's elevation and traverse, improving accuracy during rapid motion or recoil. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, and weapon sights.
[F41G 5/18] Tracking systems for guns on aircraft -- F41G 5/18 covers systems that automatically follow or maintain aim on airborne guns, enabling the weapon to stay on target while the aircraft maneuvers. These tracking mechanisms integrate sensors, actuators and control logic to adjust elevation and traverse in real time, ensuring accurate fire against moving targets.
[F41G 5/20] for guns on ships -- The code F41G 5/20 designates elevating or traversing control systems for guns mounted on ships, covering mechanisms that adjust the vertical or horizontal aim of naval artillery. It is part of the hierarchy mechanical engineering → weapons → weapon sights.
[F41G 5/22] to compensate for rolling or pitching -- The F41G 5/22 subclass covers devices that counteract the rolling or pitching motion of a firearm to keep its sight aligned, typically using stabilizing or corrective mechanisms integrated into elevation-or-traversing control systems.
[F41G 5/24] for guns on tanks -- F41G 5/24 covers mechanisms that adjust the elevation or traverse of tank-mounted guns, enabling the weapon to be aimed up or down and left or right while in the vehicle. The classification includes hydraulic, pneumatic, electric or manual control systems designed specifically for armored fighting vehicle cannons.
[F41G 5/26] Apparatus for testing or checking -- This subclass covers devices that test or verify the operation of gun-sight elevation or traversing mechanisms, such as calibrators, test rigs and diagnostic equipment used to assess aiming accuracy and control-system performance.
[F41G 7/00] Direction control systems for self-propelled missiles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for the determination of the relative position between a guided missile and a target.  Preparatory measures taken before the launching of the guided missiles.  Guided missiles training or simulation devices.  Devices or systems for testing or checking arrangements for the determination of the relative position between a self-propelled missile and a target.  Though the title of the group refers to self-propelled missiles, the group also relates to un-propelled guided projectiles such as guided artillery shells and glide-bombs.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Flight control of aircrafts -> B64C - Steering arrangements for missiles -> F42B10/60 - The physical integration of arrangements for guidance or control in missiles -> F42B15/01 - Proximity fuzes -> F42C13/00 - Control of position, course, altitude or attitude of land, water, air or space vehicles -> G05D1/00  **Glossary:** - Homing systems: Systems wherein the target tracker and the guidance computers are situated in the missile. - Command-link systems: System wherein the target tracker and/or the guidance computers are remotely situated from the missile (e.g. command to line-of-sight systems) - Beam-riding systems: Systems wherein a missile is guided in relation to reference direction defined by a beam projected from a remotely situated transmitter.
[F41G 7/001] Devices or systems for testing or checking -- F41G 7/001 refers to equipment or methods employed to test, calibrate, diagnose or verify the operation of direction-control systems in self-propelled missiles, including test benches, simulators, measurement devices and other checking apparatuses used to ensure proper aiming and guidance performance.
[F41G 7/002] target simulators -- F41G 7/002 designates target simulators, devices that produce artificial targets for testing, calibrating and training weapon sighting and missile guidance systems, enabling verification of performance without live ammunition.
[F41G 7/003] for seekers using radio waves -- F41G 7/003 covers direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that employ radio-wave (radar) seekers. The subclass falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights, focusing on guidance methods using radio frequency signals to locate and track targets.
[F41G 7/004] for infrared seekers -- F41G 7/004 relates to direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that use infrared seekers, covering the design and integration of IR-guided guidance components. It is situated in the weapon-sight subclass of mechanical engineering.
[F41G 7/005] for testing benches or sets -- F41G 7/005 covers testing benches and sets used to evaluate direction-control systems of self-propelled missiles, including guidance, steering and related components, by simulating flight conditions to verify performance.
[F41G 7/006] Guided missiles training or simulation devices -- The F41G 7/006 entry covers devices that provide training or simulation of guided missiles, focusing on the control of missile direction within weapon-sight systems. It falls under mechanical engineering, specifically the weapons branch, and pertains to direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles.
[F41G 7/007] Preparatory measures taken before the launching of the guided missiles -- This subclass covers procedures and actions performed before a guided missile is fired, such as loading target data, running system diagnostics, aligning guidance sensors and setting flight parameters to ensure the correct trajectory. It is part of the direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles within the weapon-sights group.
[F41G 7/008] Combinations of different guidance systems -- The F41G 7/008 class covers self-propelled missiles that use more than one type of guidance method in combination, such as pairing inertial navigation with laser, radar, or GPS inputs to steer the weapon. It addresses the integration and interaction of multiple guidance subsystems for improved targeting accuracy.
[F41G 7/20] based on continuous observation of target position -- The class includes direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that rely on continuous observation of the target, using sensors or cameras to track the target's position and adjust the missile's trajectory in real time.
[F41G 7/22] Homing guidance systems -- F41G 7/22 covers homing guidance systems, which are direction-control mechanisms that enable self-propelled missiles to automatically track and steer toward a target. The class falls under weapon sights within the mechanical engineering field, focusing on autonomous targeting technology.
[F41G 7/2206] using a remote control station -- The F41G 7/2206 subclass covers direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that are operated from a remote control station, allowing an operator separate from the missile to steer, adjust trajectory or engage targets via wired or wireless links.
[F41G 7/2213] maintaining the axis of an orientable seeking head pointed at the target, e.g. target seeking gyro -- The entry details a system for keeping the axis of a movable seeking head aligned with a target, typically employing a target-seeking gyro. It falls under direction-control methods for self-propelled missile weapon sights, ensuring continuous orientation of the sighting element during flight.
[F41G 7/222] for spin-stabilized missiles -- F41G 7/222 covers direction control mechanisms specifically designed for spin-stabilized missiles, detailing features that guide the missile's trajectory while maintaining spin stability. It falls under the weapon sights subclass of mechanical engineering.
[F41G 7/2226] comparing the observed data with stored target data, e.g. target configuration data -- This subclass covers the process of matching real-time sensor measurements of a missile's target with pre-stored target configuration data, enabling verification of target identity or adjustment of the missile's flight path during guidance.
[F41G 7/2233] Multimissile systems -- F41G 7/2233 covers multimissile systems, i.e., arrangements that launch and guide multiple missiles from a single platform and include the associated direction-control mechanisms. It falls under weapon sights and direction control for self-propelled missiles in the mechanical engineering class of weaponry.
[F41G 7/224] Deceiving or protecting means  jamming or anti-jamming of radio-wave systems in general  G01S7/36 ,  G01S7/38 ; defense installations in general  F41H11/02 ; chaff dispensers  F42B12/70
[F41G 7/2246] Active homing systems, i.e. comprising both a transmitter and a receiver -- F41G 7/2246 covers active homing systems for self-propelled missiles that use both a transmitter and a receiver to guide the weapon. The system emits signals and processes reflected or emitted responses to continuously adjust the missile's flight path, providing autonomous direction control.
[F41G 7/2253] Passive homing systems, i.e. comprising a receiver and do not requiring an active illumination of the target -- F41G 7/2253 relates to passive homing systems for self-propelled missiles, where the weapon uses a receiver to detect signals emitted or reflected by the target without actively illuminating it. The classification includes infrared, acoustic or passive radar receivers that guide the missile based on those detected cues.
[F41G 7/226] Semi-active homing systems, i.e. comprising a receiver and involving auxiliary illuminating means, e.g. using auxiliary guiding missiles -- F41G 7/226 covers semi-active homing guidance for missiles, where the weapon carries a receiver that detects energy reflected from a target illuminated by an auxiliary source such as a separate guiding missile or laser designator. The system relies on external illumination rather than an onboard emitter, enabling the projectile to adjust its flight path toward the target.
[F41G 7/2266] Systems comparing signals received from a base station and reflected from the target -- This classification covers systems that compare a signal transmitted from a base station with the signal reflected off a target to determine direction for a self-propelled missile. The approach is used in weapon sight guidance to adjust the flight path based on the comparative analysis of the two signals.
[F41G 7/2273] characterised by the type of waves -- This subclass covers direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that are defined by the type of waves employed for guidance, such as electromagnetic, acoustic, or other wave-based signals, and relates to weapon sight technologies within mechanical engineering.
[F41G 7/228] using acoustic waves, e.g. for torpedoes -- F41G 7/228 covers direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that use acoustic waves, such as torpedoes. It includes any method or device that generates, transmits, receives or processes sound energy to adjust the missile's course, providing guidance or steering through acoustic signals.
[F41G 7/2286] using radio waves -- F41G 7/2286 covers direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that employ radio-wave techniques. It pertains to weapon sights in the mechanical engineering field, specifically those that guide missiles using radio signals for steering or targeting.
[F41G 7/2293] using electromagnetic waves other than radio waves -- F41G 7/2293 covers the use of electromagnetic waves other than radio waves for direction control of self-propelled missiles, including weapon sight systems. It includes methods and devices that employ infrared, laser or other non-radio-frequency radiation to guide or steer missiles.
[F41G 7/24] Beam riding guidance systems -- Beam riding guidance systems are missile control methods that keep the projectile within a directed electromagnetic or optical beam emitted from the launch platform, using the beam as a reference for navigation toward the target. This technique provides continuous line-of-sight guidance without onboard radar or inertial sensors and is used primarily in short-range anti-aircraft and surface-to-air weapons.
[F41G 7/26] Optical guidance systems -- F41G 7/26 covers optical guidance systems used to steer self-propelled missiles. These systems employ visual sensors or cameras to detect targets and provide directional control, falling under weapon sights within the mechanical engineering domain.
[F41G 7/263] Means for producing guidance beams -- F41G 7/263 refers to inventions that provide means for generating the guidance beams used to steer self-propelled missiles. It falls under mechanical engineering → weapons → weapon sights → direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles, covering beam-producing devices such as lasers, infrared emitters or other energy sources that enable missile guidance.
[F41G 7/266] for spin-stabilized missiles -- F41G 7/266 pertains to direction-control systems specifically designed for spin-stabilized missiles, covering methods such as aerodynamic surfaces, thrust-vector devices or other mechanisms that adjust the flight path of self-propelled weapons while maintaining spin stabilization.
[F41G 7/28] Radio guidance systems -- F41G 7/28 pertains to radio guidance systems that steer self-propelled missiles, a subclass of weapon sight technologies within the mechanical-engineering field.
[F41G 7/30] Command link guidance systems -- F41G 7/30 covers command link guidance systems that provide direction control for self-propelled missiles, where a ground-based or airborne controller transmits commands to the weapon to adjust its flight path. These systems are part of the broader category of weapon sights within mechanical engineering.
[F41G 7/301] Details -- F41G 7/301 covers the detailed components and arrangements of weapon sight or guidance subsystems that control the flight direction of self-propelled missiles, such as the mechanical, optical or electronic elements that adjust aim, target tracking or course correction. It includes specific designs of sighting optics, sensor packages, actuators and associated control electronics that enable precise directional control during missile flight.
[F41G 7/303] Sighting or tracking devices especially provided for simultaneous observation of the target and of the missile -- The classification F41G 7/303 pertains to sighting or tracking devices that enable simultaneous observation of the target and the missile, typically incorporated in weapon sight systems for self-propelled missiles.
[F41G 7/305] for spin-stabilized missiles -- F41G 7/305 relates to direction-control systems used on spin-stabilized missiles, describing mechanisms that adjust or steer the missile's trajectory while it maintains stability through rapid rotation. The class falls within mechanical engineering, weapons, weapon sights.
[F41G 7/306] for transmitting guidance signals;  F41G7/308  takes precedence -- F41G 7/306 covers systems that transmit guidance signals to control the flight path of self-propelled missiles, including radio, laser or infrared links used to steer the weapon. It falls under weapon sights in mechanical engineering. The related subclass F41G 7/308, which deals with receiving or processing those signals, is considered primary.
[F41G 7/308] for guiding a plurality of missiles -- F41G 7/308 covers direction-control systems that guide a plurality of self-propelled missiles, enabling coordinated steering of multiple projectiles toward a target. It pertains to weapon-sight technology that manages simultaneous missile trajectories, ensuring synchronized flight paths for improved accuracy and effectiveness.
[F41G 7/32] for wire-guided missiles -- It covers mechanisms that steer missiles via a physical wire connecting the missile to the launch platform or operator, enabling real-time directional adjustments. The classification includes control unit designs, wire deployment methods, and feedback systems used in wire-guided projectiles. It falls under mechanical engineering weapon sight direction control systems.
[F41G 7/34] based on predetermined target position data -- This subclass concerns direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that navigate using pre-loaded target position data. The guidance logic relies on stored coordinates rather than real-time tracking, enabling the missile to follow a predefined flight path toward the intended impact point.
[F41G 7/343] comparing observed and stored data of target position or of distinctive marks along the path towards the target -- F41G 7/343 covers methods for comparing real-time observations of a missile's target position or distinctive marks along its path with pre-stored reference data, allowing the guidance system to adjust its trajectory.
[F41G 7/346] using global navigation satellite systems, e.g. GPS, GALILEO, GLONASS -- F41G 7/346 covers the use of global navigation satellite systems such as GPS, Galileo or GLONASS to provide direction control for self-propelled missiles and related weapon sighting devices. The classification includes methods of deriving position, velocity or heading from satellite signals to guide missile flight or to adjust aiming mechanisms. It applies to any integration of GNSS data into the missile's guidance or targeting system.
[F41G 7/36] using inertial references -- F41G 7/36 relates to direction-control systems for self-propelled missiles that employ inertial references, such as accelerometers or gyros, to determine orientation and adjust flight trajectory. It falls under weapon sights within mechanical engineering and covers guidance methods that operate without external signals.

[F41H] ARMOUR -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This subclass covers the defensive aspects such as protection gear camouflage and personal, vehicle and stationary armour (passive and active).  It includes armed and armoured vehicles.  It further includes offensive and defensive systems using flames, gas or smoke.  It also includes passive and active tactical defence installations, including laying or removing land mines and other obstacles.  It includes means of attack other than conventional weaponry, e.g. electical stunning means, directed energy weapons, EMP generators.

[F41H 11/00] Defence installations -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Active and passive defensive installations except conventional shields, armours and shelters.  Includes areal barrages, harbour nets, obstacles and minefields.  Includes demining methods and devices.
[F41H 11/02] Anti-aircraft or anti-guided missile defence installations or systems -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Active systems or installation capable of destroying, neutralising or deviating incoming missiles.  Hard-kill methods includes the physical destruction of the incoming missile with perforating, fragmenting or high explosive projectiles.  Soft-kill methods include missile neutralisation by influencing the missile's electronic homing and initiation systems (jamming, blinding, altering) or to mislead the incoming missile's sensory system with decoys so as to avoid it's impact with the object to be protected.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridges for dispensing radar chaff or infrared material -> F42B5/15 - Missiles for producing smoke -> F42B12/48 - Missiles for dispensing radar chaff or infrared material -> F42B12/70

[F41H 11/05] Net barriers for harbour defence -- F41H 11/05 relates to net-type barriers installed in harbours for defence against enemy vessels, submarines, torpedoes or mines. [F41H 11/06] Guntraps -- Guntraps are protective devices installed in defensive structures such as fortifications, bunkers or armored vehicles that enable firing weapons while preventing enemy entry. They consist of hinged or sliding plates, shutters or netting that can be opened for fire and closed to block projectiles and personnel.

[F41H 11/12] Means for clearing land minefields -- F41H 11/12 covers devices, systems and methods used to clear land-minefields, including mechanical flails, rollers, tillage tools, explosive or water-jet neutralisation devices and associated support equipment designed to detect, disarm or destroy buried mines. [F41H 11/13] Systems specially adapted for detection of landmines -- F41H 11/13 covers devices and methods designed to locate buried landmines, including detection sensors, scanning equipment and integrated systems used in demining operations. [F41H 11/132] Biological systems, e.g. with detection by animals or plants -- F41H 11/132 covers defence installations that incorporate biological systems for detection, such as using animals, plants or other living organisms to sense chemical, biological or environmental threats. [F41H 11/134] Chemical systems, e.g. with detection by vapour analysis -- F41H 11/134 pertains to chemical systems used in defence installations, especially armour and weapons, that detect hazards by analysing vapour. [F41H 11/136] Magnetic, electromagnetic, acoustic or radiation systems, e.g. ground penetrating radars or metal-detectors -- This subclass covers devices that use magnetic, electromagnetic, acoustic or radiative methods for detecting objects or probing terrain, such as ground-penetrating radar and metal detectors, typically applied in military or defensive settings for armour or installation surveillance.
[F41H 11/138] Mechanical systems, e.g. prodding sticks for manual detection -- The CPC subclass F41H 11/138 covers mechanical systems used for manual detection, such as prodding sticks employed in the inspection of armour or defensive installations. [F41H 11/14] Explosive line charges, e.g. snakes -- F41H 11/14 covers explosive line charges, commonly called "snakes," designed to create a continuous blast that clears obstacles or breaches fortifications. [F41H 11/16] Self-propelled mine-clearing vehicles -- F41H 11/16 covers self-propelled vehicles designed to detect, neutralise or clear land-mines and other explosive devices while moving autonomously or under operator control, typically incorporating protective armour, propulsion systems and mine-clearing tools such as flails, rollers or explosive charge deployment. The classification applies to military or civilian platforms intended for rapid, safe clearance of mined areas in combat zones or post-conflict environments.
[F41H 11/18] with ground-impacting means for activating mines by the use of mechanical impulses, e.g. flails or stamping elements -- F41H 11/18 covers ground-impacting mechanisms that activate mines by delivering mechanical impulses, such as flails, stamping elements or similar devices that strike the earth to trigger explosive devices. It falls under the weapons-armour section of mechanical engineering, specifically relating to defensive installations that use kinetic energy to set off mines.
[F41H 11/20] with ground-penetrating elements, e.g. with means for removing buried landmines from the soil -- The entry refers to engineering solutions incorporated into armour or defence installations that use ground-penetrating technology to detect and remove buried explosives such as landmines from the soil. It covers devices and methods for locating, extracting or neutralising buried ordnance as part of protective military structures.
[F41H 11/22] the elements being excavation buckets -- F41H 11/22 classifies the individual elements of excavation buckets used in military or defensive earth moving operations, such as the bucket shell, cutting teeth, hinges and attachment hardware. The code applies to components designed for constructing or maintaining fortifications, barriers and other defence installations.
[F41H 11/24] the elements being ploughs -- F41H 11/24 covers the individual components that function as ploughs, i.e., cutting or earth-moving attachments used on defensive fortifications or armoured vehicles for shaping terrain, digging ditches or clearing obstacles.
[F41H 11/26] the elements being rotary ground-penetrating elements -- F41H 11/26 covers rotary ground-penetrating elements, such as rotating probes or sensors that are inserted into soil or other substrates to detect buried objects, voids, or structural features. The classification applies to devices used in armor, weapons or defensive installations for underground surveillance, mapping or mine-detection purposes.
[F41H 11/28] using brushing or sweeping means or dozers to push mines lying on a surface aside -- **Definition:** This place covers:  May include magnets for picking up ferro magnetic items and gripping means for picking up or handling items.
[F41H 11/30] with rollers creating a surface load on the ground, e.g. steadily increasing surface load, for triggering purposes -- The code covers systems that use one or more rollers to apply a controlled surface load to the ground, often increasing steadily, in order to activate or trigger a defensive mechanism such as a mine, barrier or other protective device.
[F41H 11/32] Decoy or sacrificial vehicles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes magnetic means for creating a magnetic field "lure/decoy" for triggering mines or other non-contact devices for remotely exploding mines or unexploded ordnance (UXO).  Includes sound wave devices, IR-lures, water jets or other devices for triggering potential contact or proximity sensors in a mine.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Directed energy weapons -> F41H13/0043 - Disruptors -> F41B9/0046  **Glossary:** - UXO: Unexploded ordnance
[F41H 13/00] Means of attack or defence not otherwise provided for -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes ballistically deployed restraining systems, directed energy weapons and electro-shock weapons.  Includes acoustic weapons.
[F41H 13/0006] Ballistically deployed systems for restraining persons or animals, e.g. ballistically deployed nets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Including ballistically deployed nets for restraining surface vessels.  Including ballistically deployed nets for catching aerial vehicles.
[F41H 13/0012] Electrical discharge weapons, e.g. for stunning -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Including documents concerning remote discharge via ionised beams.
[F41H 13/0018] for nearby electrical discharge, i.e. the electrodes being positioned on the device and the device brought manually or otherwise into contact with a nearby target  batons with electric discharge capability  F41B15/04 ; electric shock devices for animals  A01K15/02 -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Including devices for administering an electrical shock to the wearer of the device.
[F41H 13/0025] for remote electrical discharge via conducting wires, e.g. via wire-tethered electrodes shot at a target
[F41H 13/0031] for remote electrical discharge by means of a wireless projectile -- This subclass covers weapon systems that deliver an electrical discharge at a distance by means of a projectile that carries the charge without a physical connection, such as electrically charged missiles, darts or similar autonomous devices.
[F41H 13/0037] for remote electrical discharge via liquid jets  details of the gun for generating the liquid jets  F41B9/00
[F41H 13/0043] Directed energy weapons, i.e. devices that direct a beam of high energy content toward a target for incapacitating or destroying the target -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Weapons which use an energy beam for achieving an effect on the target, as opposed to physical projectiles impacting the target.
[F41H 13/005] the high-energy beam being a laser beam -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also includes documents concerning laser as enabling technology.
[F41H 13/0056] for blinding or dazzling, i.e. by overstimulating the opponent's eyes or the enemy's sensor equipment -- F41H 13/0056 covers weapons or protective systems that incapacitate a target by blinding or dazzling, using intense light, lasers, infrared or other radiation to overstimulate human eyes or electronic sensors. The classification applies to devices designed to impair visual perception or sensor function for tactical advantage.
[F41H 13/0062] causing structural damage to the target -- The code refers to methods or devices that inflict structural damage on a target, such as explosives, kinetic impactors, or directed-energy tools that breach or destroy armor, walls, or other constructions. It covers techniques whose primary purpose is to compromise the integrity of a structure rather than to deliver a conventional projectile or fire. The classification is used for weapons designed to cause damage by destroying or weakening the target's structural components.
[F41H 13/0068] the high-energy beam being of microwave type, e.g. for causing a heating effect in the target -- F41H 13/0068 covers the use of high-energy microwave beams as weapons that produce a heating effect in a target. It is placed under mechanical engineering, weapons, armour, and means of attack or defence not otherwise provided for, focusing on systems that generate microwave radiation to damage or disable targets through rapid heating.
[F41H 13/0075] the high-energy beam being a radiofrequency beam -- The entry F41H 13/0075 covers weapons that employ a high-energy radiofrequency beam as the means of attack, a type of directed-energy system that uses radiofrequency energy to damage or disable targets. It falls within the broader categories of mechanical engineering, weapons, armour, and means of attack or defence not otherwise provided for.
[F41H 13/0081] the high-energy beam being acoustic, e.g. sonic, infrasonic or ultrasonic -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices and methods for producing focused acoustical beams or fan shaped diverging beams. Not omni-directional sound producing devices.
[F41H 13/0087] the high-energy beam being a bright light, e.g. for dazzling or blinding purposes  F41H13/0056  takes precedence -- F41H 13/0087 covers weapons that employ a high-energy light beam, such as a bright flash or laser, intended to dazzle, blind or otherwise impair the target's vision. It falls under means of attack or defence not otherwise provided for in the armour subclass and refines the broader category F41H13/0056, which deals with active illumination for hostile purposes.
[F41H 13/0093] Devices generating an electromagnetic pulse, e.g. for disrupting or destroying electronic devices -- F41H 13/0093 relates to devices that generate an electromagnetic pulse for the purpose of disrupting or destroying electronic equipment, serving as a means of attack or defence. It is classified under mechanical engineering, weapons, armour, and the category of means of attack or defence not otherwise provided for.
[F41H 3/00] Camouflage, i.e. means or methods for concealment or disguise -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes passive camouflage, i.e. covers, nets, garments , as well as active, electronic camouflage and shielding.  Includes camouflage in the visible and in the infrared spectrum.  Includes camouflage patterns.
[F41H 3/02] covers, e.g. screens, nets -- F41H 3/02 pertains to camouflage coverings, such as screens, nets or similar materials, employed to conceal or disguise military equipment, installations or personnel, falling under mechanical engineering, weapons and armour categories.
[F41H 5/00] Armour -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This main group includes the aspects of composition, configuration and the mounting of the armour elements.  It further includes the aspects of application/use of armours, e.g. as shields, turrets, manhole covers or windows  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Armoured vehicles -> F41H7/00
[F41H 5/007] Reactive armour -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes armour using liquid and the blast or shockwave mitigation effects of a fluid e.g. by rheological properties  Includes armour using electrical fields for the incapacitation of warheads  Includes armour with dilatant, materials or other chemically reactive substances in layers.  Includes pyrotechnically reactive substances.  Includes dynamic armour, i.e. elastically reacting armour.  Includes systems for intercepting incoming projectiles or missiles, i.e. active armour.  **Glossary:** - ERA: often used in the field for explosive reactive armour.
[F41H 5/013] Mounting or securing armour plates -- The F41H 5/013 CPC entry covers methods and devices for attaching armour plates to a vehicle, structure or equipment, including brackets, clamps, bolts, adhesives and other securing mechanisms designed to hold protective metal or composite panels in place.
[F41H 5/02] Plate construction -- F41H 5/02 covers the design and assembly of armor plates, including their geometry, materials, fastening methods and layering techniques used to form protective panels for vehicles, personal gear or structures. The classification addresses both monolithic and composite plate constructions intended to absorb or deflect kinetic energy and ballistic impacts.
[F41H 5/023] Armour plate, or auxiliary armour plate mounted at a distance of the main armour plate, having cavities at its outer impact surface, or holes, for deflecting the projectile -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also includes slat armour and nets for protection against hollow charge projectiles such as rocket propelled grenades (RPG).
[F41H 5/026] Slat armour; Nets -- F41H 5/026 relates to slat armour and net-type protective systems employed on vehicles or personal equipment. It covers armor composed of spaced bars or slats, often combined with netting, that is intended to disrupt or deflect kinetic projectiles, shaped charges and similar threats.
[F41H 5/04] composed of more than one layer -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Layered armour where the armour effect is enhanced by the mechanical impedance discontinuities between the layers.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Outerwear resistant to mechanical aggressions -> A41D31/24
[F41H 5/0407] Transparent bullet-proof laminates informative reference: layered products essentially comprising glass in general  B32B17/06 , e.g.  B32B17/10009 ; manufacture or composition of glass, e.g. joining glass to glass  C03 ; permanent multiple-glazing windows, e.g. with spacing therebetween,  E06B3/66 -- F41H 5/0407 relates to transparent bullet-proof laminates, i.e., layered structures that incorporate glass to provide impact resistance. The classification links to glass manufacturing and joining methods (B32B17/06, B32B17/10009) and to permanent multiple-glazing window technologies (C03, E06B3/66).
[F41H 5/0414] Layered armour containing ceramic material -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The ceramic being the main armour component, meaning the stopping action of the projectile is mainly performed by the ceramic layer(s).  Includes surface mounted interlocking or abutting ceramic tiles.  Also includes glass ceramics.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Ceramic elements embedded in a matrix -> F41H5/0492
[F41H 5/0421] Ceramic layers in combination with metal layers -- F41H 5/0421 covers armour that incorporates ceramic layers together with metal layers, typically in a composite structure where the ceramic provides high hardness and the metal supplies ductility and impact absorption. The classification is used for designs of protective plates, shields or vehicle armor that rely on this hybrid material arrangement.
[F41H 5/0428] Ceramic layers in combination with additional layers made of fibres, fabrics or plastics -- This subclass deals with protective armor that integrates a ceramic plate or coating with one or more backing layers of fibers, fabrics or plastic materials, designed to improve impact resistance and energy absorption in military or law-enforcement applications.
[F41H 5/0435] the additional layers being only fibre- or fabric-reinforced layers -- This CPC subclass relates to armor where the extra protective layers are made exclusively of fiber- or fabric-reinforced materials, adding protection without using metal, ceramic or other dense inserts. It falls under mechanical engineering weapons armor and specifies the construction of supplemental layers using only textile-based reinforcement.
[F41H 5/0442] Layered armour containing metal  in combination with ceramic layers  F41H5/0421 ; heat treatment of armour plate  C21D9/42 -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The metal being the main armour component, meaning the stopping action of the projectile is mainly performed by the metal layer(s)
[F41H 5/045] all the layers being metal layers -- F41H 5/045 relates to armor whose protective structure is formed solely from metal layers, typically achieved by laminating or stacking multiple metal sheets to provide ballistic resistance. The subclass covers designs where no non-metallic materials such as ceramics or polymers are used in the protective layers, and is applied to vehicle armor, personal shields and other mechanical engineering weapon systems.
[F41H 5/0457] Metal layers in combination with additional layers made of fibres, fabrics or plastics -- This subclass covers armor where a metal layer is combined with one or more additional layers of fibers, fabrics or plastics, forming a hybrid structure that improves protection, weight or flexibility. It includes constructions in which metal is bonded, laminated or otherwise integrated with non-metallic layers to achieve enhanced mechanical or ballistic performance.
[F41H 5/0464] the additional layers being only fibre- or fabric-reinforced layers -- F41H 5/0464 designates armor that incorporates additional protective layers made exclusively from fibre- or fabric-reinforced materials, such as woven composites or laminates, to enhance resistance against projectiles or blasts. The entry applies to mechanical-engineering solutions for personal, vehicle or equipment armor where the extra layers rely solely on reinforced textiles rather than metal or ceramic components.
[F41H 5/0471] Layered armour containing fibre- or fabric-reinforced layers  in combination with ceramic layers  F41H5/0428 , with metal layers  F41H5/0457 -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The fibrous layer(s) or tapes being the main armour component, meaning the stopping action of the projectile is mainly performed by the fibrous layer(s) or tapes.
[F41H 5/0478] Fibre- or fabric-reinforced layers in combination with plastics layers -- This subclass defines protective armor constructed from one or more layers of fibre- or fabric-reinforced material that are combined with layers of plastic or polymer resin. It includes multi-layer composites where the fabric reinforcement (e.g., aramid, glass or carbon fibres) is bonded to or interleaved with polymer sheets to achieve impact resistance, ballistic protection or lightweight shielding.
[F41H 5/0485] all the layers being only fibre- or fabric-reinforced layers -- F41H 5/0485 covers armor in which every protective layer is made only of fibre- or fabric-reinforced material, such as textile composites, laminates or similar non-metallic constructions. The classification applies to protective equipment-personal, vehicle or structural-where reinforcement is provided exclusively by woven, non-woven or polymer-impregnated fibres, without metal or ceramic layers.
[F41H 5/0492] Layered armour containing hard elements, e.g. plates, spheres, rods, separated from each other, the elements being connected to a further flexible layer or being embedded in a plastics or an elastomer matrix -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The layer with the plurality of hard elements, possibly within a matrix, being the main projectile stopping layer.  Also includes chain mail type armour with linked or engaging rings or platelets  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Ceramic armour comprising externally mounted, full-body covering ceramic tiles -> F41H5/0414
[F41H 5/06] Shields -- F41H 5/06 relates to shields used as protective equipment for personnel, vehicles or structures, encompassing designs that resist ballistic, chemical or blast effects. The entry covers the construction, materials and functional features of armor plates, panels and other defensive coverings employed in weapon systems.
[F41H 5/08] for personal use
[F41H 5/10] Spade bayonets, i.e. usable as a spade, bayonet or cover against rifle fire -- Spade bayonets are multifunctional rifle accessories that can be employed as a digging spade, a close-combat blade, or a protective cover to shield the muzzle from incoming rifle fire. Mounted on a weapon's barrel, they enable a soldier to excavate defensive positions, engage in hand-to-hand fighting, and safeguard the rifle against damage.
[F41H 5/12] for smallarms -- This CPC subgroup covers protective devices specifically designed to defend against small-arms fire, including personal body armor, vehicle plating, and portable shields. It pertains to materials, construction methods, and performance criteria aimed at stopping or mitigating bullets and fragments from pistols, rifles and similar weapons.
[F41H 5/14] Wheeled armoured shields -- Wheeled armoured shields are mobile protective devices mounted on a frame with wheels, enabling personnel or vehicles to advance under cover while deflecting small-arms fire, shrapnel or melee attacks. Historically they were used in siege warfare and modern equivalents serve convoy protection and crowd-control operations.
[F41H 5/16] for ordnance -- F41H 5/16 relates to armour specifically intended for use with ordnance, such as shells, missiles or bombs, providing protection for the payload or delivery system against impact, blast or penetration. It falls under mechanical engineering, within the weapons-armour hierarchy.
[F41H 5/18] Rotating shields -- Rotating shields are protective devices that turn about a central axis to present a fresh surface to incoming projectiles or threats, often mounted on vehicles, fortifications, or personal armor. Their motion can be driven mechanically, hydraulically, or by reactive forces to enhance survivability against ballistic or explosive attacks.
[F41H 5/20] Turrets -- Turrets are rotating or hinged armored structures mounted on military vehicles or fortifications that house weapons, sensors, and crew compartments, allowing fire coverage over a wide arc while providing protection. They may be fixed, enclosed, or open, and can be integral to tanks, naval vessels, or static defenses, often featuring gun stabilization and remote operation.
[F41H 5/22] Manhole covers, e.g. on tanks; -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes locking systems for doors on armoured vehicles.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Mounting of windows on armoured vehicle doors -> F41H5/26
[F41H 5/223] Manhole covers specially adapted for armoured or fighting vehicles -- F41H 5/223 covers manhole or access covers that are specifically engineered for armored or fighting vehicles, featuring reinforced structures, sealing mechanisms and ballistic protection to maintain hull integrity while allowing crew or equipment access. The design addresses the demanding durability and security needs of combat-grade vehicle armor.
[F41H 5/226] Doors on armoured vehicles or structures  F41H5/263  takes precedence -- The F41H 5/226 subclass covers doors fitted to armored vehicles or structures, including their design, mounting, sealing, locking mechanisms and integration with the surrounding armor. It addresses requirements for ballistic protection, blast resistance and operational reliability. The more specific subclass F41H 5/263 is considered the primary reference and takes precedence over this entry.
[F41H 5/24] for stationary use, e.g. fortifications -- F41H 5/24 refers to stationary armour, including fortifications, bunkers and other fixed protective structures built to shield against weapons fire, and falls under the mechanical-engineering weapons armour hierarchy.
[F41H 5/26] Peepholes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes observation means incl. camera's and periscopes on vehicles  Includes locking systems for AFV doors  mounting armoured transparent panels in vehicle body or doors frames to protect interface gaps  gunports not being/having ball or swivel mounts
[F41H 5/263] Mounting of transparent armoured panels, e.g. bulletproof windows on vehicles -- F41H 5/263 relates to the mounting of transparent armoured panels, such as bullet-proof windows, on vehicles. It covers methods and structures for installing or securing clear protective glazing in military, police or security vehicle applications.
[F41H 5/266] Periscopes for fighting or armoured vehicles -- F41H 5/266 covers periscopic devices incorporated into combat or armored vehicles that enable the crew to view the external environment while remaining protected inside the hull. The classification includes optical or electronic periscopes used for surveillance, targeting or navigation in tanks, infantry fighting vehicles and similar armored platforms.
[F41H 7/00] Armoured or armed vehicles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes in principle all tactical military, para-military or police vehicles, i.e. the ones being armoured against aggression and the ones serving as a mobile weapon platform.
[F41H 7/005] Unmanned ground vehicles, i.e. robotic, remote controlled or autonomous, mobile platforms carrying equipment for performing a military or police role, e.g. weapon systems or reconnaissance sensors  F41H11/16  takes precedence -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Self-propelled mine-clearing vehicles -> F41H11/16  **Glossary:** - UAV: Unmanned arial vehicle - UGV: Unmanned ground vehicle - USV: Unmanned surface vessels - UUV: Unmanned undersea vehicle
[F41H 7/02] Land vehicles with enclosing armour, e.g. tanks -- F41H 7/02 classifies land vehicles that are completely surrounded by protective armor, such as battle tanks and other armored fighting vehicles, emphasizing the enclosing armor structure and its integration with the vehicle's mobility and weapon systems. This subclass falls under the weapons-armour hierarchy of mechanical engineering, covering designs where the armor forms a sealed hull around the vehicle.
[F41H 7/03] Air-pressurised compartments for crew -- The F41H 7/03 subclass deals with air-pressurised crew compartments integrated in armoured or armed vehicles, focusing on sealed cabins that maintain internal pressure and provide breathable air under hostile conditions such as blasts or contaminated environments. It includes systems for pressurisation, sealing, and related control mechanisms.
[F41H 7/035] Gratings for ventilation openings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Gratings or similar covers for air inlet, respectively air outlet, openings on an armoured vehicle, the covers offering protection against ballistic threats while still permitting air to flow into and out of the vehicle.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Slat armour; Nets -> F41H5/026
[F41H 7/04] Armour construction -- F41H 7/04 covers the structural design of armoured or armed vehicles, detailing how protective layers of steel, composites, or ceramics are arranged, joined, and integrated with the vehicle's chassis, hull, and internal compartments to achieve ballistic resistance while maintaining functionality.
[F41H 7/042] Floors or base plates for increased land mine protection -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Specially formed or reinforced outer bottom walls of a vehicle body, e.g. V-shaped for blast deflection;  Special assemblies located on the inside of the outer bottom wall of the vehicle body for mitigating the blast wave, resulting from a mine or IED explosion, e.g. deformable assemblies such as honeycomb structures.  Floor plates for the passenger cell not connected to the outer bottom wall or blast wave mitigating assemblies.
[F41H 7/044] Hull or cab construction other than floors or base plates for increased land mine protection  mounting of armoured plates  F41H5/013 -- The code F41H 7/044 covers design features of a vehicle's hull or cab-excluding floors and base plates-that enhance protection against land mines, typically through the mounting of additional armoured plates. It pertains to mechanical-engineering solutions for armoured or armed vehicles aimed at improving survivability in mine-threat environments.
[F41H 7/046] Shock resilient mounted seats for armoured or fighting vehicles -- F41H 7/046 covers shock-resilient mounted seats designed for armored or fighting vehicles, focusing on seat structures or mounting systems that absorb impact and vibration to protect occupants during combat or rough terrain. The classification includes seats with suspensions, cushions or other energy-absorbing features integrated into the vehicle's interior.
[F41H 7/048] Vehicles having separate armoured compartments, e.g. modular armoured vehicles -- F41H 7/048 designates vehicles that incorporate distinct armored compartments, for example modular armored vehicles, and falls under the mechanical-engineering weapons armor category. This code is used to classify designs where protection is provided by separate, interchangeable sections of armor.
[F41H 7/10] Minelaying land vehicles -- F41H 7/10 covers land vehicles designed to deploy mines, including armored or armed vehicles equipped for laying anti-personnel or anti-tank mines during combat operations. It belongs to the CPC hierarchy for mechanical engineering, weapons and armour, specifically armoured or armed vehicles.
[F41H 9/00] Equipment for attack or defence by spreading flame, gas or smoke -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Offensive and defensive equipment using dispersion of gas, smoke, fog, aerosols including the projection of flames by sustained fuelling of a burning directional flame.
[F41H 9/02] Flame-throwing apparatus -- The CPC subclass F41H 9/02 covers flame-throwing apparatus, i.e., devices designed to project a stream of burning or flammable material for military or defensive use. These systems are classified under mechanical engineering, weapons and armour, specifically equipment that spreads flame, gas or smoke.
[F41H 9/04] Gas-blowing apparatus, e.g. for tear gas -- F41H 9/04 covers devices that generate and discharge gas or aerosol for purposes such as crowd control or combat, including tear-gas launchers and other portable gas-blowing apparatus. The classification applies to equipment designed to spread chemical agents for offensive or defensive use, belonging to the weapons-armour subgroup of mechanical engineering.
[F41H 9/06] Apparatus for generating artificial fog or smoke screens -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Stationary or vehicle borne apparatus generating a sustained flow of fog or smoke, the apparatus containing large quantities of smoke-generating agent, which generally would inhibit it being carried around by an individual.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Smoke pot projectors -> F42B5/155 - Projectiles producing smoke -> F42B12/48
[F41H 9/08] Smoke-pots without propulsive charge, i.e. stationary -- F41H 9/08 covers stationary smoke-pots that emit smoke without a propulsive charge. These devices are intended to create a cloud of smoke for concealment, signaling or area denial in weapons or defensive equipment. They differ from launchable smoke grenades by lacking an explosive or rocket charge.
[F41H 9/10] Hand-held or body-worn self-defence devices using repellant gases or chemicals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Portable device used by an individual for self-defence dispensing an aerosol, or a cloud of repellant gases or chemicals, such as pepper spray (OC), malodorant chemicals, chemicals inducing nausea, colouring agents (markers), diluted acids, etc.  Such a hand-held device may be in the form of a pressurised spraying can or it might be integral or attached to a weapon, an accessory or a personal shield.  A body-worn device may be in the form of an arm band, a bracelet or a ring, or eventually integrated in a back pack, a body armour, a piece of protective clothing or similar.
[F41J] TARGETS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This subclass covers all aspects of targets per se, their holders, mechanisms for target movements, hit-indication systems and target ranges.
[F41J 1/00] Targets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The targets as such characterised by their material, configuration or intended use. Further includes immobile means for holding a target in static position during the shooting.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Reflecting targets, e.g. radar-reflector targets; Active targets transmitting electromagnetic or acoustic waves -> F41J2/00 - Targets for arrows or darts, e.g. for sporting or amusement purposes -> F41J3/00 - Target indicating systems; Target-hit or score detecting systems -> F41J5/00 - Movable targets which are stationary when fired at -> F41J7/00 - Moving targets, i.e. moving when fired at -> F41J9/00 - Target ranges -> F41J11/00
[F41J 1/01] Target discs characterised by their material, structure or surface, -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Targets having two or more electrically-conductive layers for short- circuiting by penetrating projectiles -> F41J5/044
[F41J 1/08] for ordnance, e.g. cannons -- F41J 1/08 classifies targets intended for use with ordnance such as cannons, covering devices and systems designed to be struck, penetrated or otherwise engaged by artillery fire for testing, training or performance evaluation. It includes both stationary and movable targets specifically adapted for cannon fire.
[F41J 1/10] Target stands -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes:
[F41J 11/00] Target ranges -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The set-up or configuration of a target range. It covers firearms and archery ranges. Also covers paint-ball or laser tag training facilities. Ranges for dynamic shooting with realistic scenery and urban combat triaining environments are also inlcuded.
[F41J 11/02] Safety means therefor -- **Definition:** This place covers:  All safety aspects in target ranges except for the bullet catcher.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Bullet catchers -> F41J13/00
[F41J 13/00] Bullet catchers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The means for decelerating and retain the bullets after their passage through the target.  Includes device for catching bullets intact for forensic examination, devices for assuring gun safety and systems for target ranges to avoid ricochets or as back stop.
[F41J 13/02] combined with targets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices for holding a target and a bullet trap.
[F41J 2/00] Reflecting targets, e.g. radar-reflector targets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Targets reflecting simulation beams or tracking signals and target actively transmitting signals for locating or decoy purposes. Emitted signals can have acoustic, radar, radio, visible/invisible light or heat signature.
[F41J 2/02] Active targets transmitting infrared radiation -- F41J 2/02 pertains to active targets that emit infrared radiation for use in weapons testing or training. These devices generate their own IR signature rather than merely reflecting external signals, providing realistic simulation of heat-emitting objects such as aircraft or missiles.
[F41J 3/00] Targets for arrows or darts, e.g. for sporting or amusement purposes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Targets specially adapted for archery arrows and darts, including targets for arrows/darts with safety tips, e.g. rounded soft-tips (target with corresponding protrusions), hook and loop tips or suction cup tips (smooth surface target). Includes systems for mounting such targets.
[F41J 3/0004] Archery targets -- F41J 3/0004 pertains to archery targets, the stationary devices used for shooting arrows or darts in sport, recreation, or training. These targets may be constructed from a range of materials and feature scoring zones to assess accuracy.
[F41J 3/0009] Dartboards -- F41J 3/0009 covers dartboards, the target surfaces used for throwing darts in sporting or amusement activities. The classification addresses the design, materials, mounting and related accessories of these weapon target devices.
[F41J 3/0014] Dartboard holders -- Dartboard holders are devices that support and secure a dartboard, allowing it to be mounted on walls, stands or other surfaces for recreational or competitive play. They may be adjustable for height or angle and are designed to withstand impact from darts.
[F41J 3/0019] Stands or wall mountings especially adapted for dartboards -- F41J 3/0019 refers to stands or wall mountings specially designed for dartboards, including portable floor stands and fixed wall brackets used in recreational or sporting contexts. These devices support dartboards securely for target shooting with arrows or darts.
[F41J 3/0023] Holders especially adapted for rotating the dartboard during use -- F41J 3/0023 pertains to holders specifically designed to rotate a dartboard during use, allowing the playing surface to be turned for training, entertainment or to present fresh target areas. The devices typically incorporate mechanisms that secure the board while enabling smooth, controlled rotation.
[F41J 3/0028] Dart cabinets, i.e. cabinets adapted for the dartboard or dartboard accessories -- The code F41J 3/0028 identifies dart cabinets, which are specially designed enclosures that hold a dartboard and associated accessories such as scoring devices or dart storage for sporting or amusement use. This falls under the mechanical engineering weapons targets hierarchy for arrow-type targets.
[F41J 3/0033] Dartboards for use with safety darts -- This subclass covers dartboards designed specifically for safety darts, typically made of softer materials to reduce injury and used in recreational or training contexts. It is classified under mechanical engineering, weapons, targets in the CPC system.
[F41J 3/0038] having a smooth surface especially for suction tips darts -- F41J 3/0038 designates targets for arrows or darts that have a smooth surface, especially intended for use with suction-tip darts in sporting or amusement applications. The subclass falls under mechanical engineering → weapons → targets and concerns surface treatments that improve dart adhesion.
[F41J 3/0042] having perforations for receiving blunt tip darts -- A target designed with a series of holes that accommodate blunt-tip darts, allowing the projectiles to be inserted and held securely during play. The perforations are sized to match the darts' shafts, ensuring consistent placement and easy removal. This design is used for sporting or amusement dart-shooting activities.
[F41J 3/0047] having protrusions for receiving blunt tip darts in between -- This subclass covers target devices that incorporate raised features or protrusions designed to catch or hold blunt-tip darts, ensuring the darts lodge between the protrusions during play or testing. It is used for sporting or amusement dart targets.
[F41J 3/0052] having a hook and loop surface for hook and loop tip darts -- This subclass defines targets for arrows or darts that incorporate a hook-and-loop surface to retain darts equipped with a matching hook-and-loop tip, typically used in sporting or amusement settings. It falls under mechanical engineering weapons, specifically targets for arrows or darts.
[F41J 3/0057] having a magnetic surface for receiving magnetic tip darts -- A target designed for arrows or darts that incorporates a magnetic surface to capture darts equipped with magnetic tips, enabling reliable retrieval and scoring in sporting or amusement applications. This feature facilitates easy collection of darts and reduces damage to both darts and target.
[F41J 3/0061] Target faces -- Target faces are the impact surfaces of arrow or dart targets used in sporting, recreational or training contexts. They are designed to receive projectiles and often feature scoring zones, and can be made from paper, synthetic materials, metal or composite constructions. This entry classifies the specific characteristics of those facing surfaces within the weapons-targets hierarchy.
[F41J 3/0066] Segmentation of conventional target faces -- The CPC entry F41J 3/0066 deals with the subdivision of conventional target faces used for arrows or darts, detailing ways the surface is divided into zones or sections for scoring, training or recreational purposes, and falls under mechanical engineering weapons targets.
[F41J 3/0071] Non-conventional target faces
[F41J 3/0076] Target faces simulating a different sport or game, e.g. football, billiard or rugby -- The code F41J 3/0076 covers target faces that are shaped or printed to resemble the layout of other sports or games such as football, billiards or rugby, used in archery or dart shooting. These simulated surfaces give shooters a different visual challenge while still functioning as a conventional target.
[F41J 3/008] characterised by the material -- This subgroup covers targets intended for use with arrows or darts where the defining feature is the material from which the target is made, such as foam, rubber, straw, or metal. It includes sporting and amusement applications.
[F41J 3/0085] made of natural fibres -- This subclass deals with targets for arrows or darts that are fabricated from natural fibers such as wood, cotton, hemp or other plant-based materials. It pertains to sporting or amusement applications where the impact surface is composed primarily of biodegradable or renewable fiber structures.
[F41J 3/009] made of plastic or foam -- The subclass F41J 3/009 covers targets designed for use with arrows or darts that are made of plastic or foam, typically employed in sport or amusement contexts. It lies within the mechanical-engineering weapons hierarchy under weapons-targets.
[F41J 3/0095] Manufacture of dartboards -- F41J 3/0095 relates to processes and methods for producing dartboards, the targets used in archery-type games and amusement. It covers materials, shaping, surface treatment, segmentation and assembly techniques specific to dartboard manufacturing.
[F41J 3/02] Indicators or score boards for arrow or dart games -- F41J 3/02 covers devices that display scores or give visual feedback in arrow or dart games, including electronic or mechanical scoreboards, indicator panels, and related accessories used in sporting or amusement target-shooting activities.
[F41J 5/00] Target indicating systems -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Systems for giving real time feedback to the shooter regarding his performance.  Also includes systems recording the performance of the shooter for later evaluation of performance.  The systems may be weapon mounted.
[F41J 5/02] Photo-electric hit-detector systems -- F41J 5/02 covers photo-electric hit-detector systems used in target indicating devices, where light-sensitive sensors detect the passage or impact of a projectile and generate an electronic signal to register a hit. These systems are employed in weapon training and testing to provide instantaneous, automated hit registration.
[F41J 5/04] Electric hit-indicating systems -- Electric hit-indicating systems are devices that detect a projectile's impact on a target and convey the event electrically, typically by generating a visual, auditory or data signal. They are used in shooting ranges, training simulators and scoring equipment to record and display hits.
[F41J 5/041] Targets comprising two sets of electric contacts forming a coordinate system grid -- This subclass covers weapon targets that use two orthogonal sets of electric contacts arranged as a grid, creating a coordinate system to locate impact points. The intersecting contacts generate signals when struck, allowing precise measurement of a projectile's point of impact.
[F41J 5/042] Targets comprising a system of electric contacts lying in the same plane for bridging by hitting projectiles -- Targets that consist of a planar array of electrical contacts designed to be bridged by striking projectiles, enabling detection or scoring of hits through an electric signal. This system is used in weapon training or testing devices where impact closes the circuit.
[F41J 5/044] Targets having two or more electrically-conductive layers for short- circuiting by penetrating projectiles -- The code F41J 5/044 designates targets composed of two or more electrically conductive layers that short-circuit when struck by a penetrating projectile, providing an electrical indication of impact. It falls under target indicating systems within the weapons subclass of mechanical engineering.
[F41J 5/048] one of the layers being in the form of discrete target sections -- F41J 5/048 falls under weapon target-indicating systems and concerns targets built with a layered structure in which at least one layer consists of separate, discrete target sections. This arrangement is used to create defined impact zones or to facilitate measurement and analysis of projectile effects across distinct target segments.
[F41J 5/052] Targets comprising a plurality of electric contacts, each corresponding to a discrete target section and being actuated by the movement thereof -- This classification covers target devices that contain several separate electric contacts, each assigned to an individual target section, where the contacts are triggered by the movement of the respective section.
[F41J 5/056] Switch actuation by hit-generated mechanical vibration of the target body, e.g. using shock or vibration transducers -- The subclass F41J 5/056 covers weapon target-indicating systems that initiate a switch by mechanical vibration generated when the target body is struck. The actuation is produced through shock or vibration transducers that convert the impact into a signal to activate the switching mechanism. This approach enables rapid, contact-free activation within targeting hardware.
[F41J 5/06] Acoustic hit-indicating systems, i.e. detecting of shock waves -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Switch actuation by hit-generated mechanical vibration of the target body, e.g. using shock or vibration transducers -> F41J5/056
[F41J 5/08] Infrared hit-indicating systems -- Infrared hit-indicating systems are devices that detect a projectile's impact on a target and produce a visual or electronic signal using infrared radiation. They are used in weapon training and testing to give immediate feedback on hits without needing direct line-of-sight observation.
[F41J 5/10] Cinematographic hit-indicating systems -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes cinematographic targets with several parallel layers of paper, the hit indicating being based on aligning the impact holes in the front and rear layer(s) of the multitude of paper layers. Includes camera guns & guns with camera's
[F41J 5/12] for indicating the distance by which a bullet misses the target -- The code F41J 5/12 covers systems that display the miss distance of a bullet relative to the intended point on a target, such as visual markers, electronic readouts or mechanical gauges that indicate how far the projectile fell short or beyond the aim point during shooting.
[F41J 5/14] Apparatus for signalling hits or scores to the shooter, e.g. manually operated, or for communication between target and shooter -- F41J 5/14 covers devices that indicate when a target has been hit or display the score to the shooter, such as manually activated signals or electronic communication systems linking the target and the shooter. These apparatus are used in shooting sports and weapon testing to provide immediate feedback.
[F41J 5/16] Manually evaluating scores, e.g. using scoring plugs or gauges -- F41J 5/16 covers manual methods for evaluating target scores within weapon target-indicating systems, such as the use of scoring plugs, gauges or similar devices to determine hit quality or impact location. It is a subcategory of mechanical-engineering weapons targeting, focusing on hands-on assessment techniques rather than automated measurement.
[F41J 5/18] Targets having hit-indicating means actuated or moved mechanically when the target has been hit, e.g. discs or flags -- F41J 5/18 covers targets that include mechanical hit-indicating means which move or are actuated when struck, such as rotating discs, flying flags or other parts that provide a visual cue of impact.
[F41J 5/20] indicating which part of the target has been hit, i.e. the score -- F41J 5/20 relates to devices that identify the precise part of a target that has been struck, providing a hit-location indication or score. It sits within mechanical engineering, weapons, targets and specifically target-indicating systems.
[F41J 5/205] having target sections displaced or broken when hit, e.g. for visual inspection -- This CPC subclass covers target-indicating systems where the target sections are displaced or broken when struck, allowing a visual inspection of the hit. It is applied in weapons training and testing to provide immediate visual confirmation of impact.
[F41J 5/22] the indicating means being a dispensing device -- A target-indicating system where the means of indication is a dispensing device that releases marking material-such as paint, smoke, tracer fluid or similar substances-to identify or track a target. It covers mechanisms that store, control and emit the marking agent during weapon operation.
[F41J 5/24] Targets producing a particular effect when hit, e.g. detonation of pyrotechnic charge, bell ring, photograph -- This subclass concerns targets that create a defined response when struck, such as igniting a pyrotechnic charge, ringing a bell, or activating a camera. It applies to weapon systems where the target itself serves as a trigger for a particular effect upon impact.
[F41J 5/26] exploding or disintegrating when hit -- F41J 5/26 designates target indicating systems that explode or break apart on impact. These devices are used in weapon training or testing to provide immediate visual or auditory feedback when struck.
[F41J 7/00] Movable targets which are stationary when fired at -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Static targets that can be moved after a shooting exercise in order to inspect the target from close by.  Static targets which react to a hit by disappearing out the field of view of the shooter.  Targets appearing unexpectedly for training shooters reflexes, e.g. bobbing targets.
[F41J 7/02] movable for checking -- F41J 7/02 covers movable targets that remain stationary when fired at and are used for checking weapon performance. These targets can be repositioned between shots but do not move during impact, facilitating calibration and testing of firearms. The class falls under mechanical engineering, weapons, targets.
[F41J 7/04] disappearing when hit -- F41J 7/04 refers to movable targets that disappear when struck, describing devices designed to become invisible or otherwise vanish upon impact, used for testing or training in weapon systems.
[F41J 7/06] Bobbing targets, i.e. targets intermittently or unexpectedly appearing -- F41J 7/06 is a CPC subclass for mechanical-engineering weapons covering movable targets that stay stationary when shot but appear intermittently or unexpectedly, known as bobbing targets. It includes designs and mechanisms that cause the target to move up-and-down or pop into view during shooting.
[F41J 9/00] Moving targets, i.e. moving when fired at -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Targets with propulsion means or transport mechanisms for the training of the shooting at mobile targets.  Towed targets, either at land, sea or air.  Includes moving physical depictions or mock-up targets as well as virtual targets displayed on a video viewing screen.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Reflecting targets, e.g. radar-reflector targets; Active targets transmitting electromagnetic or acoustic waves -> F41J2/00
[F41J 9/02] Land-based targets -- F41J 9/02 designates land-based moving targets-objects that move while being engaged by weapons. It falls under mechanical engineering and weapons categories, covering targets that travel or change position during firing, used for testing and training of fire-arms and missile systems.
[F41J 9/04] Seagoing targets -- F41J 9/04 - Seagoing targets are moving target devices designed to float or navigate on water for testing naval guns, missiles and other weapons, simulating targets that are in motion when engaged.
[F41J 9/06] towed -- This CPC class F41J 9/06 covers towed moving targets, meaning targets that are moved while being engaged by fire. It includes systems where a target is attached to a tow vehicle or cable to simulate a moving object for weapon testing.
[F41J 9/08] Airborne targets, e.g. drones, kites, balloons -- F41J 9/08 designates airborne targets such as drones, kites or balloons that are considered moving targets for weapon systems, relating to mechanisms for engaging targets that are in motion at the time of firing. This subclass falls under the broader categories of mechanical engineering, weapons and targets.
[F41J 9/10] towed -- F41J 9/10 covers towed moving targets that are pulled behind a vehicle or platform for use in weapons testing and training. These targets simulate moving objects that a projectile must engage while in motion.
[F41J 9/14] Cinematographic targets, e.g. moving-picture targets -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes targets for both, physical firearm projectiles and simulated (laser/light/IR) projectiles.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Teaching or practice apparatus for gun-aiming or gun-laying -> F41G3/26
[F41J 9/16] Clay-pigeon targets -- F41J 9/16 covers clay-pigeon targets, which are disposable, aerodynamically shaped projectiles launched to simulate moving game for shooting practice. The classification includes mechanisms for propelling, recovering and configuring such targets to present a moving target when fired at, typical of skeet and trap shooting.
[F41J 9/165] with hit-marking or tracer means -- F41J 9/165 covers weapons intended for moving targets that incorporate hit-marking or tracer features, allowing the projectile's trajectory or impact point to be visually tracked. Such systems are used to provide immediate feedback on accuracy, often in training or combat situations where the target is in motion.
