It falls under mechanical engineering, specifically the sub-category of explosive charges.
[F42B 3/22] Elements for controlling or guiding the detonation wave, e.g. tubes -- F42B 3/22 covers components that shape, direct or regulate the detonation wave in explosive charges, such as tubing or other guiding elements incorporated in blasting cartridges. These devices are used to control the timing and propagation of the explosion, improving safety and performance in applications ranging from blasting to fireworks.
[F42B 3/24] Cartridge closures or seals -- F42B 3/24 classifies the closure or sealing components of blasting cartridges, including end caps, plugs, gaskets and other devices that secure the explosive charge within the cartridge case and prevent premature discharge.
[F42B 3/26] Arrangements for mounting initiators -- F42B 3/26 covers the specific ways in which initiators-such as detonators, primers or igniters-are positioned and secured within blasting cartridges for ammunition or explosive charges. The classification addresses the mechanical arrangement of the initiator relative to the cartridge case to ensure reliable initiation.
[F42B 3/28] Cartridge cases characterised by the material used, e.g. coatings -- The subclass F42B 3/28 pertains to blasting cartridge cases whose classification depends on the material of the case or any applied surface treatment, including specific metal alloys, polymer liners, protective coatings or other material-based characteristics.
[F42B 33/00] Manufacture of ammunition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes and devices for initial manufacturing of an ammunition as well as processes and devices for reconditioning/reusing ammunition or parts of ammunitions.  Also includes processes and devices for dismantling or controlled destruction of unused ammunition.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Manufacturing processes for hollow charges -> F42B1/036 - Manufacture of blasting cartridge initiators -> F42B3/195 - Manufacturing processes for caseless ammunition -> F42B5/188
[F42B 33/001] Devices or processes for assembling ammunition, cartridges or cartridge elements from parts -- CPC F42B 33/001 classifies inventions that provide devices or processes for putting together ammunition, cartridges or their individual elements from separate parts. It includes tooling, machinery, feed systems and methods used in the assembly of primers, propellants, projectiles and cases into complete rounds, whether manually or automatically.
[F42B 33/002] Orienting or guiding means for cartridges or cartridge parts during the manufacturing or packaging process; Feeding cartridge elements to automatic machines -- F42B 33/002 relates to devices that orient, guide or position cartridges or cartridge components while they are being manufactured, packaged or fed into automatic equipment. It includes mechanisms that direct individual cartridge elements into machines for assembly, loading or packaging, supporting the production of ammunition.
[F42B 33/004] Cartridge loaders of the rotatable-turret type -- The F42B 33/004 subclass covers cartridge-loading machines that employ a rotatable-turret mechanism to position and insert ammunition rounds during production. These loaders automate the feeding of cartridges into chambers, improving speed and consistency for manufacturing explosive charges and other ammunition types.
[F42B 33/005] Crimping cartridge cases on projectiles -- The entry concerns methods and apparatus for deforming the end of a cartridge case to grip a projectile securely during ammunition manufacture. It includes mechanical or hydraulic crimping techniques that shape the case mouth to ensure proper sealing, alignment and resistance to displacement when the round is fired.
[F42B 33/007] Making cavities in an explosive or propulsive charge -- The entry F42B 33/007 covers methods for forming cavities or channels within explosive or propellant charges, such as creating voids for inserts, primers, or shaping the charge to control burn characteristics. It pertains to the manufacturing processes used in ammunition production.
[F42B 33/008] Cutting explosive or propulsive charges -- F42B 33/008 covers cutting explosives or propulsive charges used in the manufacture of ammunition, such as shaped charges that cut or fragment material during loading or assembly. The class applies to explosives designed to produce a cutting action rather than a primary blast effect and includes their formulation, preparation and handling for ammunition production.
[F42B 33/02] Filling cartridges, missiles, or fuzes -- F42B 33/02 relates to the manufacturing step of loading or filling ammunition components such as cartridges, missiles, or fuze devices with propellant, explosive or other functional materials. The classification covers equipment, processes and techniques used to accurately introduce the charge into the shell or warhead during production.
[F42B 33/0207] Processes for loading or filling propulsive or explosive charges in containers -- F42B 33/0207 covers methods for loading or filling propellant or explosive charges into containers such as shells, cartridges or rockets. The processes include techniques for measuring, inserting, sealing and handling the charges to ensure safety and performance. It falls under manufacturing of ammunition within mechanical engineering of explosive charges.
[F42B 33/0214] by casting  F42B33/004  takes precedence
[F42B 33/0221] by centrifugal casting -- The entry F42B 33/0221 describes the manufacture of ammunition by centrifugal casting, a process where molten metal is poured into a rapidly rotating mould to form shells or casings. This method is classified under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Explosive charges → Manufacture of ammunition. It pertains to producing components for blasting, fireworks or other munitions using centrifugal forces.
[F42B 33/0228] Funnel arrangements therefor -- The classification covers designs of funnel systems used in the production of ammunition, such as devices that guide powder, propellant or other charge components into casings. It relates to manufacturing processes for explosive charges within mechanical engineering.
[F42B 33/0235] Heating of casting equipment or explosive charge containers during the loading process -- F42B 33/0235 covers methods for heating casting equipment or containers that hold explosive charges while they are being loaded, to keep the material fluid or properly packed. It is applied in the manufacture of ammunition and explosive charges such as those used for blasting, fireworks, or other ordnance.
[F42B 33/0242] by pressure casting -- This subclass covers the manufacturing of ammunition in which the explosive charge is formed by pressure casting. The process involves forcing molten or pliable energetic material into a mold under pressure to achieve the desired shape and density. It is a technique used in the production of blasting caps, fireworks or small arms ammunition.
[F42B 33/025] by compacting  F42B33/004  takes precedence
[F42B 33/0257] by vibration compacting -- The subclass F42B 33/0257 covers manufacturing processes for ammunition in which the explosive charge is formed by compacting the material using vibration. It is a subcategory of mechanical engineering-ammunition-explosive charges, specifying vibration-based densification as the method of charge formation.
[F42B 33/0264] by using screw-type feeders  F42B33/004  takes precedence
[F42B 33/0271] for extruding blasting cartridges -- The CPC subclass F42B 33/0271 covers the manufacturing step of forming blasting cartridges by extrusion, detailing methods and apparatus for shaping the propellant and casing in a continuous or semi-continuous process. It falls under the broader category of ammunition production within mechanical engineering.
[F42B 33/0278] Safety arrangements therefor  F42B33/004  takes precedence -- F42B 33/0278 covers safety arrangements in the manufacture of ammunition and other explosive charges such as blasting agents and fireworks. It is nested under mechanical engineering → ammunition → explosive charges, with the broader safety provisions class F42B33/004 taking precedence.
[F42B 33/0285] Measuring explosive-charge levels in containers or cartridge cases; Methods or devices for controlling the quantity of material fed or filled  F42B33/004  takes precedence; controlling the quantity of material fed in packaging  B65B3/26 -- This subclass concerns techniques for determining how much explosive material is present in a container or cartridge case and the devices or methods used to control the amount that is fed or filled during ammunition manufacture. It falls under the broader group dealing with controlling material quantity in packaging.
[F42B 33/0292] by volumetric measurement, i.e. the volume of the material being determined before filling -- The entry F42B 33/0292 covers methods for determining the volume of an explosive or propellant charge prior to filling it into ammunition. It specifies volumetric measurement techniques used during the manufacture of ammunition to ensure correct charge size and performance. This falls under the mechanical-engineering subclass for explosive charges.
[F42B 33/04] Fitting or extracting primers in or from fuzes or charges -- F42B 33/04 covers processes for installing or removing primers in fuze or explosive charges during ammunition manufacturing. It includes methods and equipment used to fit primers into fuze assemblies or extract them for maintenance or reloading.
[F42B 33/06] Dismantling fuzes, cartridges, projectiles, missiles, rockets or bombs -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group includes the dismantling of ammunition with the aim of avoiding the triggering of a catastrophic detonation, e.g. by chemical bath, deep freezing, incinerator, laser cutting of the mantle.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridge loaders of the rotatable-turret type -> F42B33/004 - Fitting or extracting primers in or from fuzes or charges -> F42B33/04 - Rendering explosive charges harmless, destroying ammunition (by exploding within a safety container) -> F42D5/04
[F42B 33/062] by high-pressure water jet means -- F42B 33/062 designates manufacturing methods for ammunition that use high-pressure water-jet techniques to cut, shape, or finish explosive charges, typically as part of the production or processing of blast-type ammunition.
[F42B 33/065] by laser means -- A process for manufacturing ammunition in which lasers are employed to cut, shape, weld or otherwise treat explosive-charge components, such as casings, projectiles or warheads. This includes any laser-based material removal, joining or surface modification used during the production of ammunition.
[F42B 33/067] by combustion  incineration apparatuses or processes for used articles  F23G7/003 -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This class includes destruction of ammunition by combustion in the sense of incineration, i.e. no pressure confinement chambers or detonators are used. The aim is the deflagration at low pressure of the explosive to be destroyed.  Incineration in fluidised bed reactors.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Rendering explosive charges harmless, destroying ammunition (by exploding within a safety container) -> F42D5/04
[F42B 33/10] Reconditioning used cartridge cases -- F42B 33/10 covers the process of reconditioning used cartridge cases, which involves cleaning, reshaping, and refurbishing spent brass or steel casings for reuse in ammunition production. This activity falls within the manufacture of ammunition under the broader class of explosive charges in mechanical engineering.
[F42B 33/12] Crimping shotgun cartridges -- F42B 33/12 relates to methods and devices for crimping shotgun cartridges during ammunition manufacture, specifically shaping the case mouth to secure the projectile and ensure proper sealing. It falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and explosive-charge manufacturing.
[F42B 33/14] Surface treatment of cartridges or cartridge cases -- The class F42B 33/14 covers methods for treating the surface of cartridges or cartridge cases, including cleaning, coating, polishing, or chemical conversion applied during or after manufacture. It is part of the mechanical-engineering hierarchy under ammunition and explosive-charge production.
[F42B 35/00] Testing or checking of ammunition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  It includes the testing and checking of ammunition before the use, i.e during manufacturing, during storage or just prior to launch/deployment.  It further inlcudes processes and devices for the forensic testing of smallarms ammunition after an incident or crime.  Also includes firing test batches in specialised testing devices equipped with measuring instruments and/or high speed cameras; specialised testing devices therefore.
[F42B 35/02] Gauging, sorting, trimming or shortening cartridges or missiles -- The entry covers procedures for measuring, sorting and trimming or shortening cartridges or missiles during ammunition testing or inspection. It relates to mechanical engineering of explosive charges and includes methods to gauge dimensions and adjust length for performance or safety.
[F42B 39/00] Packaging or storage of ammunition or explosive charges -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Packaging of ammunition, e.g. cartridges, projectiles, warheads, rocket engines, fuzes, primers, self-contained propellants, detonators or explosives for safe storage and transport (in vehicle or worn on body).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Holder for fireworks -> F42B4/20
[F42B 39/002] Cartridge containers provided with cartridge-dispensing means -- The code refers to containers for ammunition that incorporate a mechanism to dispense individual cartridges, such as magazines, handheld dispensers or built-in release devices. It covers packaging or storage solutions that enable controlled delivery of explosive charges like bullets or shells.
[F42B 39/005] Protection for driving bands -- The classification F42B 39/005 relates to protective measures for driving bands of ammunition, covering liners, coatings, casings or other treatments that shield the bands from wear, corrosion or deformation during handling, storage, or firing.
[F42B 39/007] Packaging or storage of arrows or darts  quivers for arrows  F41B5/06
[F42B 39/02] Cartridge bags -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Belt or webbing worn ammunition pouches or magazine pouches or speedloader holsters.  Holders for extra ammunition mounted on the outside of a gun or gunstock.
[F42B 39/08] Cartridge belts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Means facilitating the feeding of ammunition to automatic firearms, i.e. cartridges carried by a textile band or by carrier units each holding one cartridge, the carrier units being sequentially connected to each other by connecting elements or connected to each other by belt links, each belt link holding one cartridge and embracing the previous or subsequent cartridge.  Includes solid inflexible metal strips or racks acting similar to belts (Hotchkiss type or Japanese Model 01 (1941)or japanese Type 92 HMG).
[F42B 39/082] for caseless ammunition -- F42B 39/082 covers methods and devices for packaging or storing caseless ammunition, a type of ammunition that lacks a separate cartridge case. It falls under the mechanical engineering section for explosive charges and addresses handling, containment, and protection of these self-contained rounds.
[F42B 39/085] for blank cartridges -- This CPC entry covers devices or methods for packaging or storing blank cartridges, a type of ammunition without a projectile used for training, ceremonial or other non-firearm purposes.
[F42B 39/087] Feed belts manufactured from fabric or plastics material -- This subclass addresses feed belts employed in the packaging or storage of ammunition or explosive charges that are made from fabric or plastic materials, focusing on the mechanical engineering aspects of ammunition handling systems.
[F42B 39/10] Machines for charging or for extracting cartridges from feed belts -- F42B 39/10 covers machines that load or unload cartridges from feed belts, used in the packaging or storage of ammunition and explosive charges. These devices are mechanical-engineering solutions for handling ammunition in blasting, fireworks, or military applications.
[F42B 39/14] Explosion or fire protection arrangements on packages or ammunition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Arrangements for reducing damage effects from the outside environment, e.g. fire, on the ammunition.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Packages or ammunition having valves for pressure-equalising; Packages or ammunition having plugs for pressure release, e.g. meltable; Blow-out panels; Venting arrangements -> F42B39/20 - Shock-absorbing arrangements in packages -> F42B39/24
[F42B 39/16] Fire-extinguishing -- F42B 39/16 concerns fire-extinguishing systems or methods used in the packaging, storage or transport of ammunition and explosive charges. It includes devices, chemicals or procedures designed to suppress or control fires that may arise from such materials. The entry is part of the mechanical-engineering group for ammunition safety.
[F42B 39/18] Heat shields -- F42B 39/18 covers heat shields used in the packaging or storage of ammunition and other explosive charges, protecting surrounding components and personnel from thermal effects during handling, transport or detonation. It belongs to the mechanical-engineering branch dealing with ammunition storage.
[F42B 39/20] Packages or ammunition having valves for pressure-equalising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Venting arrangements including pyrotechnic cutting arrangements  Arrangements for reducing damage to the outside environment caused by unintended activation of the ammunition itself, e.g. pressure or heat build up.
[F42B 39/22] Locking of ammunition in transport containers -- F42B 39/22 covers methods and devices for securing ammunition inside transport containers, including locks, latches, or other retaining mechanisms that keep explosive charges stable during handling and shipment. It falls under mechanical engineering, specifically the packaging and storage of ammunition and explosive charges.
[F42B 39/24] Shock-absorbing arrangements in packages -- This subclass covers devices or methods that cushion or dampen impacts on containers holding ammunition or explosive charges, ensuring safety during handling, transport, or storage. It includes shock-absorbing liners, cushions, padding, and structural features integrated into the package to mitigate mechanical stresses.
[F42B 39/26] Packages or containers for a plurality of ammunition, e.g. cartridges -- F42B 39/26 pertains to packaging or containers designed to hold multiple ammunition units such as cartridges, shells or rounds. It includes boxes, tins, belts and other storage solutions that protect the charges from moisture, impact and accidental ignition while facilitating handling and transport.
[F42B 39/28] Ammunition racks, e.g. in vehicles -- This classification covers designs for racks that hold ammunition within vehicles, including mounting, securing, and organizing devices to safely store and transport rounds. It addresses structural features, material choices, and integration with vehicle components to facilitate rapid access while protecting against shock and accidental discharge.
[F42B 39/30] Containers for detonators or fuzes -- This CPC entry covers containers designed to hold detonators or fuzes used in ammunition and explosive charges. It falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, explosive charges, focusing on the packaging or storage - specifically for these devices.
[F42B 4/00] Fireworks, i.e. pyrotechnic devices for amusement, display, illumination or signal purposes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes all mechanical aspects of fireworks for amusement purposes.
[F42B 4/02] in cartridge form, i.e. shell, propellant and primer -- F42B 4/02 pertains to fireworks that are supplied in cartridge form, meaning the shell, propellant and primer are combined in a single pre-assembled unit. This subclass addresses pyrotechnic devices used for amusement, display, illumination or signaling where the charge is integrated into a cartridge.
[F42B 4/04] Firecrackers -- F42B 4/04 is a CPC subclass under mechanical engineering → ammunition → explosive charges that classifies firecrackers, small pyrotechnic devices intended to produce a loud bang and flash for amusement, display, illumination or signaling purposes.
[F42B 4/06] Aerial display rockets -- F42B 4/06 covers aerial display rockets, which are pyrotechnic devices launched into the air to create visual effects for entertainment, illumination or signaling. These rockets are a type of fireworks used in public displays.
[F42B 4/08] characterised by having vanes, wings, parachutes or balloons -- F42B 4/08 covers pyrotechnic devices such as fireworks that incorporate aerodynamic features-vanes, wings, parachutes or balloons-to stabilize, guide or slow their flight or descent, thereby influencing trajectory, timing of burst or visual effect. This subclass groups designs where such elements are integral to the device's operation.
[F42B 4/10] characterised by having means to separate article or charge from casing without destroying the casing -- F42B 4/10 refers to fireworks that incorporate a mechanism allowing the pyrotechnic charge to be removed from its outer casing without breaking the casing, enabling separation of the article or charge while keeping the shell intact. Such designs are used for reusable or safety-oriented devices.
[F42B 4/12] Parachute or flare separation -- F42B 4/12 concerns the devices and methods used to detach a parachute or a flare from a firework or other pyrotechnic charge during its operation. It includes mechanisms for timing, release, and separation that enable safe deployment of illumination, signal or display elements after the explosive event. This subclass falls under the broader category of explosive charges for fireworks.
[F42B 4/14] characterised by having plural successively-ignited charges -- F42B 4/14 pertains to fireworks that incorporate several separate charges which are ignited in succession, producing a series of effects rather than a single simultaneous burst. This subclass defines pyrotechnic devices where the multiple charges are arranged to fire one after another for a staged display.
[F42B 4/16] Hand-thrown impact-exploded noise makers; -- Hand-thrown noise makers that explode on impact are classified under CPC F42B 4/16, a subgroup of fireworks within mechanical engineering. These devices are designed to be tossed by hand, where the sudden impact initiates an explosive charge that generates a loud sound for amusement, signaling or visual display purposes.
[F42B 4/18] Simulations, e.g. pine cone, house that is destroyed, warship, volcano
[F42B 4/20] characterised by having holder or support other than casing, e.g. whirler or spike support -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes containers for fireworks that serve as packaging for storage and transport and also serve as launch units.
[F42B 4/22] characterised by having means to separate article or charge from casing without destroying the casing -- This subclass covers fireworks that incorporate a mechanism allowing the explosive article or charge to be removed from its outer casing without breaking the casing, such as removable shells or detachable compartments. It is used for devices where the charge can be reloaded or inspected while preserving the outer shell.
[F42B 4/24] characterised by having plural successively-ignited charges -- This subclass covers fireworks that contain two or more charges designed to ignite one after another, producing a series of successive effects such as multiple bursts, sparks or flames. Typical examples include Roman candles, multi-shot aerial shells and similar pyrotechnic devices used for amusement, display or signaling.
[F42B 4/26] Flares -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Flares for signalling, illuminating and as leurres/decoys.  Flares consisting of stacked platelets or disc shaped pellets use "platelets".  Flares consisting of elongated packages filled with slow burning chemical compositions with high electromagnetic spectrum output that burn down from one end as torches.
[F42B 4/28] Parachute flares -- Parachute flares are pyrotechnic illumination or signaling devices mounted on a parachute that deploys to provide a slow-descending, burning source of light. They are used for nighttime signaling, search-and-rescue, or visual displays and fall under the fireworks subgroup of explosive charges.
[F42B 4/30] Manufacture -- The F42B 4/30 subclass covers methods, apparatus and processes used to manufacture fireworks, including the preparation of pyrotechnic compositions, shaping, loading, and finishing steps that produce devices for amusement, display, illumination or signalling. It addresses the practical production techniques for assembling and packaging explosive charges intended for non-military, celebratory purposes.
[F42B 5/00] Cartridge ammunition, e.g. separately-loaded propellant charges -- **Definition:** This place covers:  A cartridge is traditionally considered to be the combination of projectile, propellant, primer and cartridge case into a single unit. This subclass further includes caseless ammunitions, i.e. a unit comprising a formed propellant, primer and projectile without a case. This main group covers all the cartridged ammunitions except for the shotgun ammunitions, which are covered in F42B7/00 .  Also comprises separately packaged propellant charges for artillery gun.  **Glossary:** - Case: container for housing propellant charge, primer and missile - Cartridge: case containing propellant charge(s), primer(s) and missile(s); formed propellant with missile and primer
[F42B 5/02] Cartridges, i.e. cases with charge and missile -- F42B 5/02 pertains to cartridges, the containers that combine a propellant charge with a missile or projectile in ammunition. It falls under mechanical engineering, within the ammunition subclass for explosive charges and separately-loaded cartridge ammunition.
[F42B 5/025] characterised by the dimension of the case or the missile -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes identification markings on case or projectile.

[F42B 5/045] of telescopic type -- The F42B 5/045 subclass covers cartridge ammunition in which the propellant charge is formed by telescopic components, such as an inner case that slides within an outer case to create a compact, separable-loaded round. [F42B 5/05] for recoilless guns -- F42B 5/05 covers cartridge ammunition that is specially adapted for use in recoilless guns, a type of lightweight weapon that vents propellant gases to reduce recoil. [F42B 5/067] Mounting or locking missiles in cartridge cases -- The F42B 5/067 subclass concerns arrangements for mounting or locking missiles within cartridge cases, typically used in separately-loaded propellant charges for ammunition. [F42B 5/073] using an auxiliary locking element -- F42B 5/073 pertains to cartridge ammunition where an auxiliary locking element is employed to secure the propellant charge or other components within the cartridge case, preventing premature movement or separation during handling and firing. The auxiliary element may be a separate lock, latch, or clamp that engages the charge, case or primer to enhance safety and reliability.
[F42B 5/08] modified for electric ignition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes optical ignition.
[F42B 5/10] with self-propelled bullet -- F42B 5/10 designates cartridge ammunition that incorporates a self-propelled bullet, meaning the projectile contains its own propulsion mechanism rather than relying solely on the propellant charge in the case. [F42B 5/105] propelled by two propulsive charges, the rearwardly situated one being separated from the rest of the projectile during flight or in the barrel; Projectiles with self-ejecting cartridge cases -- The class covers cartridge ammunition that uses two propulsive charges, with the rearward charge separating from the projectile either while in the barrel or during flight, and includes projectiles that have self-ejecting cartridge cases.

[F42B 5/155] Smoke-pot projectors, e.g. arranged on vehicles -- F42B 5/155 relates to smoke-pot projectors designed to be mounted on vehicles and to discharge smoke for concealment, signaling or screening purposes. [F42B 5/16] characterised by composition or physical dimensions or form of propellant charge, or powder -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridges for cleaning; for cooling; for lubricating; for wear reducing -> F42B5/24
[F42B 5/18] Caseless ammunition -- F42B 5/18 covers caseless ammunition, which integrates the propellant and projectile in a single unit without a separate cartridge case, used in firearms and weapons where a traditional shell is omitted. [F42B 5/181] consisting of a combustible casing wall and a metal base; Connectors therefor -- The entry relates to cartridge ammunition whose case wall is made of a combustible material while a metal base holds the propellant and projectile, and it includes the connectors that join the two parts. This design reduces the weight of spent cases and the amount of debris left after firing.
[F42B 5/182] Caseless cartridges characterised by their shape -- F42B 5/182 covers caseless ammunition where the propellant charge and projectile are formed as a single unit and the design is distinguished primarily by the external shape of the cartridge. [F42B 5/184] telescopic -- F42B 5/184 covers cartridge ammunition in which the propellant charges are arranged telescopically, meaning one charge is nested within another to reduce overall length or adjust burn characteristics. [F42B 5/196] Coatings -- F42B 5/196 pertains to the application of protective, functional or decorative coatings on cartridge ammunition or separately loaded propellant charges. [F42B 5/24] for cleaning -- This CPC subclass deals with cleaning of cartridge ammunition and separately-loaded propellant charges. [F42B 5/285] formed by assembling several elements -- F42B 5/285 covers cartridge ammunition where the propellant charge is formed by assembling multiple separate elements, such as individual powder bags or segments, into a complete charge for use in firearms or blasting. [F42B 5/29] wound from sheets or strips -- F42B 5/29 pertains to ammunition in which the propellant charge is made from sheet or strip material that is wound into a compact form.
