[F42B 5/295] coated -- F42B 5/295 covers cartridge ammunition in which the propellant charges or other elements are provided with a coating, such as a protective, insulating, or burn-rate-modifying layer. The coating may be applied to control moisture, improve handling, or adjust performance of the explosive charge.
[F42B 5/297] with plastics -- The subclass F42B 5/297 relates to cartridge ammunition whose propellant charge or associated parts are made from or incorporate plastic materials, such as polymeric casings, liners or binders, replacing traditional metal components in separately-loaded explosive charges.
[F42B 5/30] of plastics -- This subclass covers cartridge ammunition where the case or other components are made of plastic material. It includes the design, production and use of plastic-based shells or propellant charges for firearms and blasting applications.
[F42B 5/307] formed by assembling several elements -- F42B 5/307 covers cartridge ammunition whose explosive charge is created by assembling several separate elements, such as individual propellant grains, primers and projectiles, rather than being formed as a single unit. It applies to separately-loaded ammunition used in blasting, fireworks and other mechanical-engineering contexts.
[F42B 5/313] all elements made of plastics -- This subclass groups cartridge ammunition in which every part - the casing, primer, propellant charge and projectile - is made from plastic materials, emphasizing lightweight, corrosion-resistant and potentially lower-cost designs often used for non-lethal or specialized munitions.
[F42B 5/32] for rim fire -- This subclass covers cartridge ammunition in which the propellant charge is loaded separately and ignited by a rim-fire system, where the primer is located in the rim of the cartridge base. It falls under the mechanical-engineering group for explosive charges in the CPC shared by the EPO and USPTO.
[F42B 5/34] with provision for varying the length -- F42B 5/34 covers cartridge ammunition in which separately loaded propellant charges are designed with a mechanism that allows the overall length of the charge to be varied, enabling adjustment of ballistic performance or compatibility with different weapon systems.
[F42B 5/36] modified for housing an integral firing-cap -- F42B 5/36 covers cartridge ammunition that is adapted to contain an integral firing-cap built into the housing. The modification integrates the primer or igniter within the case, eliminating separate caps and improving reliability for blasting, fireworks or military rounds. It falls under the mechanical engineering branch for explosive charges and specifically addresses designs of separately-loaded propellant charges.
[F42B 5/38] Separately-loaded propellant charges, e.g. cartridge bags -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridges characterised by composition or physical dimensions or form of propellant charge, with or without projectile, or powder -> F42B5/16 - Cartridge cases characterised by the material of the casing wall -> F42B5/192
[F42B 6/00] Projectiles or missiles specially adapted for projection without use of explosive or combustible propellant charge, e.g. for blow guns, bows or crossbows, hand-held spring or air guns -- **Definition:** This place covers:  All projectiles or missiles which are not propelled from a firearm, i.e. not propelled by the combustion of a propellant in the cartridge chamber of a firearm's barrel, including darts, arrows, crossbow bolts, harpoons, fish spears, airgun pellets, paint balls, throwing stars or other non-standard-dart sharp throwing objects excluding knives and axes.
[F42B 6/003] Darts -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Includes throwing stars or other non-standard-dart sharp throwing objects excluding knives and axes.
[F42B 6/006] Projectiles for electromagnetic or plasma guns -- F42B 6/006 covers projectiles designed specifically for use in electromagnetic or plasma launchers such as railguns or plasma cannons. The entry includes bodies, sabot or payload configurations that are accelerated by magnetic fields or ionized plasma rather than chemical propellants. These projectiles may be solid, composite or contain electronics for guidance.
[F42B 6/02] Arrows -- F42B 6/02 pertains to arrows, which are non-explosive projectiles specifically designed for launch by bows, crossbows, blow-guns, hand-held spring or air-gun mechanisms, and similar devices that propel missiles without using combustible propellant charges.
[F42B 6/04] Archery arrows -- F42B 6/04 relates to archery arrows, the non-explosive projectiles designed for use with bows, blow guns, spring- or air-powered devices. The subclass falls under mechanical engineering of ammunition, specifically explosive-charge-free missiles used for hunting, sport or signaling.
[F42B 6/06] Tail ends, e.g. nocks, fletching -- The F42B 6/06 class covers tail-end components for non-explosive projectiles such as those launched from blow guns, bows, crossbows, spring or air guns. Items include nocks, fletching and similar devices that stabilize or attach the projectile's rear.
[F42B 6/08] Arrow heads -- F42B 6/08 covers arrow heads, the terminal devices of projectiles propelled by bows, crossbows, blow guns or spring-air guns. The classification includes designs that improve penetration, flight stability and aerodynamic performance of non-explosive projectiles.
[F42B 6/10] Air gun pellets -- This CPC entry covers non-explosive projectiles such as air-gun pellets, which are used in blow-guns, bows, crossbows, or hand-held spring and air guns that launch a projectile without an explosive or combustible propellant. It falls under the mechanical-engineering hierarchy for ammunition and explosive-charge classifications, specifically for projectile designs adapted for non-propellant propulsion.
[F42B 7/00] Shotgun ammunition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  All projectiles or missiles specially adapted to be fired from a smooth bore shotgun barrel for shot pellets or from a rifled shotgun barrel for slugs. In literature a difference between birdshot and buckshot is made, however in the classification scheme these difference in shot dimension is not taken into account, i.e. bird- and buckshot will be both classified under F42B7/04 .
[F42B 7/02] Cartridges, i.e. cases with propellant charge and missile -- This CPC class covers shotgun cartridges, which are complete ammunition units consisting of a case, a propellant charge and a projectile. It is situated under mechanical engineering, ammunition and explosive charges and addresses the design and construction of shotgun shells.
[F42B 7/04] of pellet type -- F42B 7/04 covers shotgun ammunition where the projectile is a group of small pellets rather than a single slug. It classifies pellets-type loads designed for spread patterns used in hunting and sport shooting within the broader category of explosive charges for firearms.
[F42B 7/043] with shot-scattering means -- F42B 7/043 classifies shotgun cartridges that incorporate shot-scattering means, such as wads, crimped pellets or devices that disperse the shot upon firing. It applies to ammunition designed to spread the shot pattern for a wider impact area.
[F42B 7/046] Pellets or shot therefor -- F42B 7/046 classifies the design, manufacture and material aspects of pellets or shot intended for use in shotgun ammunition. It includes individual projectiles, their bonding, coating or packaging, and related manufacturing processes for all types of shotgun shot.
[F42B 7/06] with cartridge case of plastics -- F42B 7/06 designates shotgun ammunition in which the cartridge case is made of plastic rather than metal, covering the structure and related features of such plastic shells used for firing.
[F42B 7/08] Wads, therefor -- F42B 7/08 relates to wads used in shotgun ammunition, covering the material that separates the propellant charge from the shot and the muzzle, and any modifications or structures of the wad that affect loading, sealing, or shot pattern. The class falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition and explosive charges for shotgun shells.
[F42B 7/10] Ball or slug shotgun cartridges -- F42B 7/10 covers shotgun cartridges that contain a single solid projectile such as a ball or slug, intended for use in standard-gauge shotguns. It includes designs where the projectile is the sole payload, distinguishing them from shot shells that contain multiple pellets.
[F42B 7/12] Cartridge top closures, i.e. for the missile side -- F42B 7/12 pertains to the design of cartridge top closures that seal the missile side of shotgun shells, addressing how the closure secures the projectile within the casing. It falls under the mechanical engineering hierarchy for ammunition, specifically explosive charges and shotgun ammunition.
[F42B 8/00] Practice or training ammunition -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Ammunition either devoid of - or with strongly reduced - propellant energy or warhead energy, in order to enable safe and cost-efficient weapon's training, i.e. including inert or dummy ammunition and reduced energy ammunition.
[F42B 8/02] Cartridges -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cartridge top closures, i.e. for the missile side -> F42B7/12 - Light- or radiation-emitting guns; Light- or radiation-sensitive guns; Cartridges carrying light emitting sources, e.g. laser -> F41A33/02
[F42B 8/04] Blank cartridges, i.e. primed cartridges without projectile but containing an explosive or combustible powder charge -- F42B 8/04 covers blank cartridges, which are primed ammunition units lacking a projectile but containing an explosive or combustible powder charge. These cartridges are used for practice, training or ceremonial firing where the generation of a muzzle blast is required without launching a projectile.
[F42B 8/06] for cap-firing pistols -- F42B 8/06 designates practice or training ammunition intended for use in cap-firing pistols, a type of non-lethal projectile employed in training and demonstrations. It resides in the CPC hierarchy under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Explosive Charges, specifically for blasting, fireworks and related ammunition.
[F42B 8/08] Dummy cartridges, i.e. inert cartridges containing neither primer nor explosive or combustible powder charge -- F42B 8/08 covers inert or dummy cartridges that contain no primer, propellant or explosive charge and are used for training, testing or handling practice. These cartridges simulate real ammunition while providing a safe, non-explosive alternative for drills and equipment verification.
[F42B 8/10] with sub-calibre adaptor -- F42B 8/10 classifies practice or training ammunition that incorporates a sub-calibre adaptor, allowing the firing of reduced-size projectiles for training while using a standard-calibre weapon. This falls under the Mechanical Engineering - Ammunition - Explosive Charges hierarchy.
[F42B 8/12] Projectiles or missiles -- F42B 8/12 covers practice or training ammunition in the form of projectiles or missiles. It includes non-lethal or reduced-power devices used for training, drills, and testing of firing systems. The classification falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and explosive charges.
[F42B 8/14] disintegrating in flight or upon impact -- F42B 8/14 refers to practice or training ammunition that is engineered to break apart either during its flight or on impact. The subclass captures designs where the projectile disintegrates to limit lethality, typically used for safety in training exercises involving explosive charges.
[F42B 8/16] containing an inert filler in powder or granular form -- F42B 8/16 covers practice or training ammunition in which the explosive charge incorporates an inert filler in powder or granular form, providing a simulated load that mimics real ammunition without containing active explosive material.
[F42B 8/18] Rifle grenades -- F42B 8/18 covers rifle-launched grenades intended for practice or training, featuring reduced-charge or non-lethal explosive elements that mimic the ballistic performance of combat grenades. These items are classified under mechanical engineering and ammunition as part of explosive charge technologies used for training purposes.
[F42B 8/20] Mortar grenades -- The CPC code F42B 8/20 designates mortar grenades, a type of practice or training ammunition used in mortar weapons. It falls under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Explosive charges, covering devices that simulate live rounds for safe training and testing.
[F42B 8/22] Fall bombs -- Fall bombs are practice or training ammunition classified under CPC F42B 8/22, a subset of explosive charges used for blasting, fireworks and ammunition. They are designed to be dropped from aircraft and detonate on impact, providing realistic training without the destructive power of live ordnance.
[F42B 8/24] Rockets -- F42B 8/24 covers rockets employed as practice or training ammunition, including their design, construction, propulsion, launch mechanisms, and safety aspects. The classification applies to non-combat rockets used for training drills, testing, and instructional purposes, encompassing both the explosive charge and the supporting hardware.
[F42B 8/26] Hand grenades -- F42B 8/26 relates to hand grenades, encompassing the design, manufacture and use of portable explosive devices intended as practice or training ammunition. The entry falls within mechanical engineering and the broader category of explosive charges, focusing on non-combat training applications.
[F42B 8/28] Land or marine mines -- The F42B 8/28 subclass pertains to land or marine mines, including both operational and training types. It covers the design, construction, deployment mechanisms, safety devices and performance testing of mines intended for use on land or in water, as well as non-lethal training versions used for practice.
[F42B 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups of this subclass -- F42B 99/00 is the residual bucket for explosive-charge technologies within the mechanical-engineering section on ammunition. It captures any patent subject matter concerning blasting, fireworks or ammunition that does not fall into the specific groups defined elsewhere in the subclass, providing a catch-all category for miscellaneous or novel explosive inventions.
[F42C] AMMUNITION FUZES -- **Definition:** This place covers:  An assembly or mechanism which incorporates safety and arming means in order that the explosion can only take place under certain conditions; this assembly or mechanism determines also the moment (instantaneous or delayed) or the manner, e.g. impact, proximity, hydrostatic pressure, of the firing.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Chemical aspects of detonating or priming devices -> C06C - Fuses or fuse cords, i. e. a continuous train of explosive enclosed in a usually flexible cord or cable for setting-off an explosive charge in the art of blasting -> C06C5/00 - Blasting cartridge initiators -> F42B3/10 - Filling fuzes -> F42B33/02 - Fitting or extracting primers in or from fuzes -> F42B33/04 - Containers for fuzes -> F42B39/30
[F42C 1/00] Impact fuzes, i.e. fuzes actuated only by ammunition impact -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fuzes wherein the impact of the fuze onto the target activates a firing pin which then triggers immediate or delayed detonation of the warhead.  Fuzes without a firing pin wherein the impact of the fuze onto the target is detected by a sensor which in turn generates an output triggering immediate or delayed detonation of the warhead.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Double action percussion fuze -> F42C7/12 - Protruding stand-off member for hollow charges -> F42B12/105
[F42C 1/02] with firing-pin structurally combined with fuze -- Impact fuze subcategory that covers designs where the firing pin is an integral part of the fuze mechanism, so the pin and fuze are structurally combined rather than separate components. This arrangement is used for ammunition that detonates only upon impact.
[F42C 1/04] operating by inertia of members on impact -- F42C 1/04 relates to impact fuzes that are triggered by the inertia of internal members when the projectile strikes a target. The fuze operates solely on the sudden deceleration caused by impact, requiring no external power or timed initiation.
[F42C 1/06] for any direction of impact -- F42C 1/06 classifies impact fuzes designed to activate when the ammunition contacts a target from any direction, without requiring a specific orientation for activation.
[F42C 1/08] with delayed action after ignition of fuze -- This classification covers impact-activated ammunition fuzes that incorporate a delay mechanism so the explosive effect occurs a short time after the fuze is ignited by impact. It is used to allow the projectile to penetrate or pass a target before the warhead detonates.
[F42C 1/09] the fuze activating a propulsive charge for propelling the ammunition or the warhead into the air, e.g. in rebounding projectiles -- F42C 1/09 covers impact-activated fuzes that, upon striking a target, ignite a propulsive charge to launch the projectile or warhead back into the air, such as in rebounding or bouncing ammunition. The fuze's purpose is to provide a secondary lift after impact.
[F42C 1/10] without firing-pin -- Impact fuzes that function without a firing pin rely solely on the projectile's collision to initiate detonation, eliminating the separate pin mechanism. This simplifies the fuze design, often reducing size, weight and cost for ammunition.
[F42C 11/00] Electric fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fuzes characterised by the electric or electronic circuitry, which is usually triggered or controlled by one of the fuze sensor mechanisms covered in F42C1/00 - F42C9/18 or F42C13/00 . Generation of electricity therefore.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Proximity fuzes -> F42C13/00 - Safety or arming effected by electric means -> F42C15/40 - Electric contact parts for fuzes -> F42C19/06 - Electric primers, the initial explosive component in the pyrotechnic or explosive train is electrically initiated -> F42C19/12 - Bridge initiators -> F42B3/12 - Spark initiators -> F42B3/14 - Pyrotechnic delay initiators -> F42B3/16 - Safety initiators resistant to premature firing by static electricity or stray currents -> F42B3/18
[F42C 11/001] Electric circuits for fuzes characterised by the ammunition class or type  F42C11/02  -  F42C11/06  take precedence; mechanical fuzes having electric igniters for hand grenades or marine warheads  F42C14/025 ,  F42C14/045 -- F42C 11/001 covers electric circuit designs for ammunition fuzes that are defined principally by the class or type of ammunition they serve, taking precedence over the broader groups F42C 11/02-F42C 11/06. It includes circuits used in mechanical fuzes equipped with electric igniters for hand grenades or marine warheads, such as those classified under F42C 14/025 and F42C 14/045.
[F42C 11/002] Smart ammunition fuzes, i.e. having an integrated scanning, guiding and firing system -- F42C 11/002 refers to smart ammunition fuzes that embed electronic scanning, guidance and firing mechanisms, allowing the fuze to detect, track and adjust to a target autonomously before detonation. The code falls under the electric fuze subgroup of ammunition fuzes within the mechanical engineering hierarchy.
[F42C 11/003] for hand grenades -- F42C 11/003 covers electric fuze systems specifically designed for hand grenades, detailing the electrical initiation circuitry, safety arming mechanisms and timing functions that trigger the explosive charge.
[F42C 11/005] for marine warheads, e.g. torpedoes, mines, depth charges -- F42C 11/005 covers electric fuzes designed for marine warheads such as torpedoes, naval mines and depth charges. The classification falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes and electric fuzes, and is used by the EPO and USPTO to index inventions related to underwater explosive devices.
[F42C 11/006] for fall bombs -- F42C 11/006 relates to electric fuzes designed for fall bombs, i.e., bombs released from aircraft that descend by gravity. The subclass includes circuitry and activation methods that initiate detonation on impact or at a predetermined point during the bomb's free-fall trajectory.
[F42C 11/007] for land mines -- F42C 11/007 designates electric fuzes intended for use in land mines, falling under the hierarchy of Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Ammunition Fuzes → Electric fuzes. This subclass addresses the specific technical features and activation mechanisms of electrically powered detonators for ground-based explosive devices.
[F42C 11/008] Power generation in electric fuzes  F42C11/02 ,  F42C11/04  and  F42C15/295  take precedence -- This classification covers the generation of electrical power within electric fuzes used for ammunition. It includes methods and devices that produce energy for the fuze circuit, such as batteries, generators, or capacitive storage, and supersedes related sub-classes F42C11/02, F42C11/04 and F42C15/295.
[F42C 11/02] with piezo-crystal -- F42C 11/02 covers electric ammunition fuzes that use a piezo-crystal as the primary sensing element. The piezo-crystal generates an electric signal when mechanical stress from impact or pressure occurs, initiating the fuze's firing circuit. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes, electric fuzes.
[F42C 11/04] with current induction -- F42C 11/04 covers electric fuzes for ammunition that are powered by current induction, where a magnetic field induces the necessary electrical charge to trigger the fuze. This subclass falls under ammunition fuzes within mechanical engineering, specifying induction-based initiation rather than direct battery or external power sources.
[F42C 11/06] with time delay by electric circuitry -- F42C 11/06 classifies electric ammunition fuzes that create a delayed detonation through electronic circuitry, integrating a timer or logic circuit to postpone activation after a preset interval. The delay can be set mechanically, digitally, or by programmable components, allowing controlled timing for ignition, safety, or sequencing in munitions. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and electric fuzes.
[F42C 11/065] Programmable electronic delay initiators in projectiles -- F42C 11/065 pertains to programmable electronic delay initiators incorporated into projectile fuzes, where a micro-processor or similar circuitry sets a selectable time interval after activation before the fuze detonates. The electronic delay can be adjusted to suit various mission requirements, improving safety and flexibility in ammunition deployment.
[F42C 1/12] with delayed action after ignition of fuze -- F42C 1/12 covers impact fuzes that incorporate a timed delay after the initial ignition caused by ammunition impact, so the warhead detonates a preset interval later instead of instantly. The delay may be used to allow penetration or to synchronize explosion with a target.
[F42C 1/14] operating at a predetermined distance from ground or target by means of a protruding member -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Protruding stand-off member for hollow charges -> F42B12/105
[F42C 13/00] Proximity fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fuzes wherein detonation is initiated after an electronic circuitry including a non-contact (e.g. electrostatic, electrodynamic, optical, field sensitive, accoustic or magnetic) proximity sensor has determined that the proximity of the target is sufficient for optimised effect of the warhead.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Proximity sensor by contacting of a protruding memeber -> F42C1/14 - Proximity fuzes in combination with other fuzes -> F42C9/148
[F42C 13/003] operated by variations in electrostatic field -- F42C 13/003 covers proximity fuzes that are triggered by changes in an electrostatic field. These devices detect variations in the surrounding electrostatic environment to initiate detonation, fitting within the hierarchy of mechanical engineering, ammunition, and ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 13/006] for non-guided, spinning, braked or gravity-driven weapons, e.g. parachute-braked sub-munitions -- F42C 13/006 concerns proximity fuze designs used in non-guided munitions that travel by spin, aerodynamic braking or gravity, such as sub-munitions slowed by parachutes. The classification covers mechanisms that detect a target's approach and trigger detonation without active guidance. It falls under the broader categories of mechanical engineering, ammunition, and ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 13/02] operated by intensity of light or similar radiation -- F42C 13/02 covers proximity fuzes for ammunition that activate when they detect a certain level of light or other electromagnetic radiation. These devices use optical or radiative sensors to determine distance to a target and initiate detonation. The classification is used for designs employing photodetectors, infrared, or similar radiation-sensing elements.
[F42C 13/023] using active distance measurement -- The subclass F42C 13/023 covers proximity fuzes that determine the optimal detonation point by actively measuring the distance to a target, using technologies such as radar, laser, ultrasonic or other sensor-based ranging methods. It pertains to ammunition fuzes that trigger when a preset distance is reached, improving accuracy and allowing safe standoff engagement. This falls within the broader categories of mechanical engineering, ammunition, and ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 13/026] Remotely actuated projectile fuzes operated by optical transmission links -- F42C 13/026 pertains to projectile fuzes that are remotely actuated via optical transmission links, enabling command-initiated arming or detonation from a distance. The classification covers designs in which light-based signals control proximity fuzes used in ammunition, providing precise, non-electrical activation.
[F42C 13/04] operated by radio waves -- F42C 13/04 designates proximity fuzes that are activated or controlled by radio-wave signals, using electromagnetic radiation to detect the approach of a target and trigger detonation. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and ammunition fuzes, specifying radio-wave-operated devices for explosive projectiles.
[F42C 13/042] based on distance determination by coded radar techniques -- F42C 13/042 refers to proximity fuzes that determine distance by employing coded radar techniques, where the fuze emits a radar signal with a specific code and measures the returned echoes to calculate the separation from the target. This method enables precise detonation timing for ammunition and falls under the mechanical-engineering hierarchy of ammunition → ammunition fuzes → proximity fuzes.
[F42C 13/045] using transmission of F.M. waves -- F42C 13/045 pertains to proximity fuze designs that employ transmission of frequency-modulated (FM) waves for target detection. The method involves emitting an FM signal, monitoring its reflected or doppler-shifted return, and using the received data to initiate fuze activation when a predetermined proximity is reached. This subclass falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition and ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 13/047] Remotely actuated projectile fuzes operated by radio transmission links -- The code F42C 13/047 classifies proximity fuzes that are remotely actuated by radio-transmission links. It covers projectile fuzes that receive command signals to trigger detonation at a distance rather than by mechanical impact or time delay, falling under ammunition fuzes in mechanical engineering.
[F42C 13/06] operated by sound waves -- F42C 13/06 addresses proximity fuzes that are triggered by sound waves. These fuzes use acoustic sensors to detect the pressure or vibrations generated by an approaching target and initiate detonation without direct contact. The design belongs to mechanical engineering and ammunition fuze technology.
[F42C 13/08] operated by variations in magnetic field -- F42C 13/08 covers proximity fuzes that are triggered by variations in magnetic field, using magnetic sensors to detect a target's approach and initiate detonation. The subclass is situated under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes and proximity fuzes.
[F42C 14/00] fuzes characterised by the ammunition class or type -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This main group is organised as an application group, i.e. non electric fuzes characterised by the ammunition they are designed for.  If a fuze is characterised by a features relating to a special adaptation for the use with a particular ammunition not listed in the sub-groups, classify in main group.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Impact fuzes, i.e. fuzes actuated only by ammunition impact -> F42C1/00 - Fuzes actuated by application of a predetermined mechanical force, e.g. tension, torsion, pressure -> F42C7/00 - Time fuzes; Combined time and percussion or pressure-actuated fuzes; Fuzes for timed self-destruction of ammunition -> F42C9/00 - Electric circuits for fuzes characterised by the ammunition class or type -> F42C11/001 - Proximity fuzes; Fuzes for remote detonation -> F42C13/00 - Arming-means in fuzes; Safety means for preventing premature detonation of fuzes or charges -> F42C15/00
[F42C 14/02] for hand grenades -- F42C 14/02 covers fuzes designed specifically for hand-grenades, falling under the ammunition fuzes subclass of mechanical engineering. These fuzes are intended for use with hand-grenade types and are classified within the Cooperative Patent Classification system used by the EPO and USPTO.
[F42C 14/025] having electric igniters -- F42C 14/025 covers ammunition fuzes that incorporate electric igniters. These fuzes are designed to be triggered electrically and are classified according to the ammunition class or type they serve. The code falls under the mechanical engineering section for ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 14/04] for torpedoes, marine mines or depth charges -- F42C 14/04 designates fuzes that are expressly intended for use in underwater weapons such as torpedoes, naval mines and depth charges. The subclass groups fuze mechanisms whose operation is defined by the type of ammunition rather than by a particular triggering principle. It is part of the mechanical engineering section dealing with ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 14/045] having electric igniters -- F42C 14/045 is a CPC subclass within mechanical engineering for ammunition fuzes that are characterised by the ammunition type, specifically covering fuzes incorporating electric igniters to initiate the charge.
[F42C 14/06] for fall bombs -- This subcategory covers fuze designs specifically intended for use in free-fall bombs, detailing activation mechanisms triggered by impact, retardation or other conditions after release. It includes safety, arming and timing features tailored to fall-bomb applications.
[F42C 14/08] for land mines -- F42C 14/08 covers fuze mechanisms specifically designed for land mines. It is placed in the CPC hierarchy under Mechanical Engineering, Ammunition, Ammunition Fuzes, focusing on fuzes characterised by the class or type of ammunition they serve.
[F42C 15/00] Arming-means in fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Mechanisms or electric circuits keeping a fuze in a safe state until certain predefined conditions, usually launch and/or flight conditions, are met and causing automatic transition the fuze into the armed state as soon as all conditions are met.
[F42C 15/005] Combination-type safety mechanisms, i.e. two or more safeties are moved in a predetermined sequence to each other -- The F42C 15/005 subclass covers combination-type safety mechanisms in ammunition fuzes, where two or more safeties are moved in a predetermined sequence relative to each other. It pertains to arming-means that require a specific order of safety-device actions before the fuze can be armed, providing enhanced protection against accidental initiation.
[F42C 15/16] wherein the firing pin is displaced out of the action line for safety -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/16 covers safety mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that displace the firing pin out of the line of action to prevent unintended ignition. It is a specific arming-means feature within the broader category of ammunition fuzes in mechanical engineering.
[F42C 15/18] wherein a carrier for an element of the pyrotechnic or explosive train is moved -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Movable blocking member in the pyrotechnic or explosive train -> F42C15/34 - Safety or arming means wherein the safety or arming action is effected electrically -> F42C15/40
[F42C 15/184] using a slidable carrier -- F42C 15/184 pertains to ammunition fuzes that incorporate a slidable carrier as part of the arming mechanism. The carrier moves relative to the fuze body to position or release a detonator or other initiating component, enabling controlled activation of the warhead.
[F42C 15/188] using a rotatable carrier -- F42C 15/188 concerns arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that employ a rotatable carrier to position or index components for safe and reliable initiation. The rotating carrier may be driven by spin, propulsion gases, or mechanical movement to control the arming sequence.
[F42C 15/192] rotatable in a plane which is parallel to the longitudinal axis of the projectile -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/192 covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that rotate within a plane parallel to the projectile's longitudinal axis. It relates to designs where the arming means are mounted to turn around an axis aligned with the projectile's flight direction, allowing controlled activation.
[F42C 15/196] by the action of centrifugal or inertia forces on the carrier body, e.g. the carrier having eccentrically mounted weights or eccentric centre of gravity -- F42C 15/196 classifies arming mechanisms for ammunition fuzes that rely on centrifugal or inertia forces generated by the carrier body, for example designs that employ eccentrically mounted weights or shift the centre of gravity to activate the fuze during projectile motion.
[F42C 15/20] wherein a securing-pin or latch is removed to arm the fuze, e.g. removed from the firing-pin -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/20 covers fuze arming mechanisms that require the removal of a securing pin or latch before the fuze becomes live, such as taking a pin out of the firing-pin assembly. This action physically releases the firing mechanism, completing the arming sequence of the ammunition.
[F42C 15/21] using spring action -- This CPC subclass concerns ammunition fuzes that use spring action to provide the mechanical energy needed for arming or activation. It includes designs where a compressed spring releases stored energy to move arming pins, sear mechanisms or other components into the armed position, enabling reliable initiation of the explosive charge.
[F42C 15/22] using centrifugal force -- F42C 15/22 covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that employ centrifugal force generated by the projectile's spin to move or release safety components, ensuring the fuze remains inert until sufficient rotational speed is achieved after launch. This method provides a reliable, spin-dependent means of initiating the fuze only under the intended firing conditions.
[F42C 15/23] by unwinding a flexible ribbon or tape -- F42C 15/23 covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that operate by unwinding a flexible ribbon or tape to transfer energy or position the detonator. The method is used to ensure safe handling until the ribbon is released during launch or trajectory.
[F42C 15/24] wherein the safety or arming action is effected by inertia means -- This CPC sub-group covers ammunition fuze designs where the safety or arming function is performed by inertial mechanisms such as weighted masses, springs or centrifugal forces that respond to motion. It is classified under mechanical engineering, ammunition fuzes, arming-means in fuzes.
[F42C 15/26] using centrifugal force -- The subclass F42C 15/26 covers fuze arming mechanisms that employ centrifugal force generated by the projectile's rotation to move or release arming components. It includes designs where spinning mass, rotors or weighted elements activate the fuze once a preset rotational speed is reached, ensuring safe handling until launch.
[F42C 15/28] operated by flow of fluent material, e.g. shot, fluids -- F42C 15/28 covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that are activated by the passage of a fluent material such as liquid, gas, or shot. The design uses the flow of the material to move a component that releases the fuze's safety features, allowing the detonation sequence to proceed once the projectile is in flight. This subcategory falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and arming-means in fuzes.
[F42C 15/285] stored within the fuze housing -- This CPC subclass concerns the location of arming means that are stored inside the fuze housing of ammunition. It covers designs where the arming devices, such as springs or detonators, are retained within the fuze body until activation. It falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 15/29] operated by fluidic oscillators -- This CPC subclass F42C 15/29 falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes and arming-means in fuzes and covers fuzes whose arming mechanism is driven by fluidic oscillators, i.e., devices that use self-sustaining fluid flow oscillations to activate the detonator.
[F42C 15/295] operated by a turbine or a propeller -- The CPC code F42C 15/295 covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that are driven by a turbine or a propeller. These devices use the rotational energy generated by fluid flow or a small propeller to move safety components into the armed position, ensuring the fuze activates only after the projectile has traveled a predetermined distance or time. This sub-class falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, and ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 15/30] of propellant gases, i.e. derived from propulsive charge or rocket motor -- F42C 15/30 designates fuze arming means that are activated by gases generated from the propellant charge or rocket motor. The subclass covers devices that use pressure, flow or chemical energy of these gases to trigger the fuze's internal mechanisms, ensuring safe ignition only after launch.
[F42C 15/31] generated by the combustion of a pyrotechnic or explosive charge within the fuze -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/31 covers arming means in ammunition fuzes that are activated by the combustion of a pyrotechnic or explosive charge located within the fuze. The generated energy is used to move, position or release a component of the fuze, such as a striker, detonator or safety mechanism, thereby preparing the munition for initiation.
[F42C 15/32] operated by change of fluid pressure -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/32 pertains to arming-means in ammunition fuzes that are triggered by a change in fluid pressure, such as hydraulic or pneumatic pressure variations caused by launch, impact, or environmental conditions. It classifies fuze mechanisms that use pressure differentials to transition from a safe to an armed state. This entry falls under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Ammunition Fuzes → Arming-means in fuzes.
[F42C 15/33] by breaking a vacuum or pressure container -- The CPC subclass F42C 15/33 covers arming-means in ammunition fuzes that are triggered by breaking a sealed vacuum or pressure container. When the container ruptures the stored pressure or vacuum is released, providing the energy or movement needed to arm the fuze for initiation.
[F42C 15/34] wherein the safety or arming action is effected by a blocking-member in the pyrotechnic or explosive train between primer and main charge -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Safety or arming means wherein a carrier for an element of the pyrotechnic or explosive train is moved -> F42C15/18 - Safety or arming means wherein the safety or arming action is effected electrically -> F42C15/40
[F42C 15/36] wherein arming is effected by combustion or fusion of an element; -- A sub-class of ammunition fuzes covering devices where the arming mechanism is triggered by the combustion or fusion of a material element, such as a pyrotechnic charge or a metallic fuse element, producing the energy needed to ready the fuze for operation.
[F42C 15/38] wherein arming is effected by chemical action -- This subclass covers ammunition fuze designs where the arming function is achieved through a chemical reaction, such as the release of a catalyst or the consumption of a reactive material that activates the detonator after a set condition. It is part of the broader arming-means group within the mechanical engineering section for ammunition.
[F42C 15/40] wherein the safety or arming action is effected electrically -- This CPC subclass defines ammunition fuzes whose safety or arming function is achieved by an electrical mechanism. It includes any design where electrical signals, circuits or components initiate the transition from a safe to an armed state, ensuring activation only when intended.
[F42C 15/42] from a remote location, e.g. for controlled mines or mine fields -- This subclass covers arming mechanisms in ammunition fuzes that are triggered from a remote location, such as those used to activate controlled mines or mine fields. The technology enables a fuze to be armed or detonated by a signal or command transmitted at a distance.
[F42C 15/44] Arrangements for disarming, or for rendering harmless, fuzes after arming, e.g. after launch -- This CPC subclass (F42C 15/44) covers mechanisms and methods that deactivate or neutralise a fuze after it has been armed, such as systems that safely render the fuze harmless following launch. It includes designs for automatic disarming, self-destruct, or safety-delay devices within ammunition.
[F42C 17/00] Fuze-setting apparatus -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Apparatus for setting the fuzes of a projectile or missile. The apparatus can either be a robotic device or classical manual device for manipulating a mechanically settable fuze, or a data interface for setting electric/electronic fuzes.
[F42C 17/02] Fuze-setting keys -- The CPC entry F42C 17/02, titled fuze-setting keys, falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes, fuze-setting apparatus. It covers devices used to adjust or program the timing or activation settings of explosive fuzes, typically handheld keys or tools that interface with the fuze mechanism to set delay, impact, or other triggering parameters.
[F42C 17/04] for electric fuzes -- The F42C 17/04 subclass-under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Ammunition Fuzes → Fuze-setting apparatus-covers devices that set or adjust fuzes by means of electrical power, including circuits, connectors and control units designed for electric-actuated fuzes.
[F42C 19/00] Details of fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Structural details possibly pertinent to all types of fuzes, such as the body and the caps. Further includes details of electrical components pertinent to electric fuzes only.  Includes the primers, i.e. the initial explosive component in the pyrotechnic or explosive train.
[F42C 19/02] Fuze bodies -- F42C 19/02 relates to the bodies of ammunition fuzes, covering their structural design, material selection and manufacturing methods. It addresses the core casing that houses the triggering mechanisms and ensures proper fit, strength and protection within the overall fuze assembly.
[F42C 19/04] Protective caps -- Protective caps are components fitted over ammunition fuzes to shield the fuze mechanism from mechanical damage, moisture and premature activation during handling, storage and firing. They are typically removable or frangible pieces designed to be discarded or destroyed upon chambering, ensuring the fuze remains functional until the intended moment of detonation.
[F42C 19/06] Electric contact parts specially adapted for use with electric fuzes -- This subclass covers electric contact components that are specifically designed for integration with electric fuzes in ammunition. It includes switches, connectors, and other conductive parts that transmit electrical signals to initiate the fuze. The classification falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes, details of fuzes.
[F42C 19/07] Nose-contacts for projectiles or missiles -- F42C 19/07 covers nose-contact elements that are mounted on the front of projectiles or missiles and form part of a fuze system. These components detect impact or proximity and trigger the fuze's initiation sequence. The classification is used for designs that integrate the contact device with the projectile's nose geometry.
[F42C 19/08] Primers -- It pertains to primers, which are small explosive charges used to initiate larger ammunition fuzes. The classification covers the design, composition and function of these initiating devices for small-arms and artillery ammunition.
[F42C 19/0803] characterised by the combination of  per se  known chemical composition in the priming substance -- F42C 19/0803 covers ammunition fuzes that are defined by a priming substance formed from a combination of already known chemical components. The classification applies when the fuze's operation depends on a specific formulation of established compounds in the primer, and it falls within the details of fuzes in mechanical engineering.
[F42C 19/0807] characterised by the particular configuration of the transmission channels from the priming energy source to the charge to be ignited, e.g. multiple channels, nozzles, diaphragms or filters -- F42C 19/0807 classifies ammunition fuzes whose distinguishing feature is the specific arrangement of transmission channels that convey energy from the primer to the main charge, including designs with multiple channels, nozzles, diaphragms or filters. This falls under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Ammunition fuzes.
[F42C 19/0811] characterised by the generation of a plasma for initiating the charge to be ignited -- F42C 19/0811 covers ammunition fuze designs in which the initiation of the main charge is achieved by creating a plasma discharge. The plasma acts as the energy source that ignites the propellant, providing rapid and reliable activation for the munition.
[F42C 19/0815] Intermediate ignition capsules, i.e. self-contained primary pyrotechnic module transmitting the initial firing signal to the secondary explosive, e.g. using electric, radio frequency, optical or percussion signals to the secondary explosive  initiators for blasting cartridges or air bags  F42B3/10 -- Intermediate ignition capsules are self-contained primary pyrotechnic modules that receive an electric, radio-frequency, optical or percussion signal and transmit it to a secondary explosive initiator, commonly used in blasting cartridges or air-bag inflators. They fall under the mechanical engineering hierarchy for ammunition fuzes, specifically the F42C 19/0815 subclass.
[F42C 19/0819] Primers or igniters for the initiation of rocket motors, i.e. pyrotechnical aspects thereof -- This CPC subclass relates to the design and composition of primers or igniters that start rocket motors, emphasizing their pyrotechnic characteristics. It is situated in the hierarchy Mechanical Engineering - Ammunition - Ammunition Fuzes and deals with detailed aspects of fuze technology for rocket propulsion.
[F42C 19/0823] Primers or igniters for the initiation or the propellant charge in a cartridged ammunition  primers for caseless ammunition  F42C19/085 -- This CPC subclass F42C 19/0823 covers primers or igniters specifically designed to start the propellant charge in both cartridge-based and caseless ammunition. It includes chemical or mechanical devices that provide the initial ignition for the projectile's firing sequence.
[F42C 19/0826] comprising an elongated perforated tube, i.e. flame tube, for the transmission of the initial energy to the propellant charge, e.g. used for artillery shells and kinetic energy penetrators -- F42C 19/0826 covers fuzes that incorporate an elongated perforated, or flame, tube to convey the initiating energy to the propellant charge, a feature applied in artillery shells and kinetic-energy penetrators. The tube directs the flash or hot gases from the primer into the main charge, improving ignition reliability and timing.
[F42C 19/083] characterised by the shape and configuration of the base element embedded in the cartridge bottom, e.g. the housing for the squib or percussion cap -- F42C 19/083 classifies ammunition fuzes based on the shape and configuration of the base element that is integrated into the cartridge bottom, including designs of the housing for the squib or percussion cap that initiates the charge.
[F42C 19/0834] Arrangements of a multiplicity of primers or detonators dispersed within a propellant charge for increased efficiency -- This classification covers designs where many primers or detonators are distributed throughout the propellant to improve the burn rate and overall performance of the charge. It includes configurations that use multiple-initiation points to achieve more uniform or faster ignition, enhancing ammunition efficiency.
[F42C 19/0838] Primers or igniters for the initiation or the explosive charge in a warhead  F42C19/095  takes precedence -- F42C 19/0838 concerns primers or igniters that initiate the explosive charge in a warhead, forming part of the detailed design of ammunition fuzes. It sits within the hierarchy mechanical engineering → ammunition → ammunition fuzes and is superseded by the more specific code F42C 19/095.
[F42C 19/0842] Arrangements of a multiplicity of primers or detonators, dispersed within a warhead, for multiple mode selection -- The code F42C 19/0842 covers warhead designs in which several primers or detonators are distributed throughout the explosive charge and can be selected to initiate different firing modes. It addresses the configuration and control of multiple initiation points to achieve varied detonation effects.
[F42C 19/0846] Arrangements of a multiplicity of primers or detonators, dispersed within a warhead, for increased efficiency -- The CPC subclass F42C 19/0846 covers designs that distribute multiple primers or detonators throughout a warhead to achieve a more uniform or rapid initiation and greater overall efficiency. It is placed under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes, and the details of fuzes category.
[F42C 19/085] Primers for caseless ammunition -- This subclass covers primers specifically designed for caseless ammunition, including the composition, placement and activation mechanisms that initiate the propellant without a separate cartridge case. It addresses chemical formulations, ignition timing and integration methods that ensure reliable firing of self-contained rounds.
[F42C 19/09] Primers or detonators containing a hollow charge -- This subclass deals with primers or detonators that integrate a hollow (shaped) charge as part of the initiating device. The hollow charge focuses explosive energy to defeat barriers or to initiate the main charge, and the classification covers the design and arrangement of such combined fuzes within ammunition.
[F42C 19/095] Arrangements of a multiplicity of primers or detonators, dispersed around a warhead, one of the primers or detonators being selected for directional detonation effects -- This CPC subclass covers warhead designs that employ multiple primers or detonators arranged around the explosive charge, with only one selected for activation to produce a directional detonation effect, enabling controlled blast shaping for improved target engagement or reduced collateral damage.
[F42C 19/10] Percussion caps -- F42C 19/10 covers percussion caps, the small explosive devices that ignite the main propellant charge when struck and are used in small arms, artillery and other ammunition. The classification includes the design, composition and mounting of caps that form part of a fuze system to initiate detonation.
[F42C 19/12] electric -- F42C 19/12 pertains to electric fuzes for ammunition, covering designs that use electrical energy to initiate a projectile, including circuit configurations, power sources, safety and arming mechanisms, and the integration of electronic components that control timing or detonation.
[F42C 19/14] operable also in the percussion mode -- F42C 19/14 covers ammunition fuzes that are capable of being triggered in percussion mode, meaning they can function when struck by impact as well as by other initiation methods. The entry is part of the mechanical-engineering branch for ammunition fuze details, describing designs that combine percussion activation with alternative firing mechanisms.
[F42C 21/00] Checking fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices and methods for checking and testing fuzes during manufacturing or just prior to launch or deployment.
[F42C 3/00] Fuzes actuated by exposure to a liquid, e.g. seawater -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fuzes activated by sensors detecting liquid exposure to liquid, e.g. components swelling or disintegrating when contacted by a liquid, in practice sea, lake or river water.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Protruding stand-off member for hollow charges -> F42C5/00
[F42C 5/00] Fuzes actuated by exposure to a predetermined ambient fluid pressure -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fuzes that initiate if the water pressure rises above a certain level which is applicable in depth charges.  Also includes fuzes triggered when a threshold of gas pressure is reached, e.g. though a gas generating capsule or by sympathetic detonation of a nearby explosive charge.  Also includes fuzes actuated when the pressure value goes below a predefined theshold, e.g. detonation only possible at a certain altitude.
[F42C 5/02] barometric pressure -- The CPC subclass F42C 5/02 covers ammunition fuzes that trigger by sensing ambient barometric pressure. These devices rely on changes in atmospheric pressure to initiate detonation, allowing activation at specific altitudes or pressure conditions. It falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition fuzes actuated by fluid pressure.
[F42C 7/00] Fuzes actuated by application of a predetermined mechanical force, e.g. tension, torsion, pressure -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The fuse is actuated by application of a mechanical force, i.e. the forceful relative displacement of two components of the fuze relative to each other. Basically a mechanical switch triggering a detonation.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Impact fuzes, i.e. fuzes actuated only by ammunition impact -> F42C1/00 - Fuzes actuated by exposure to a predetermined ambient fluid pressure -> F42C5/00
[F42C 7/02] Contact fuzes, i.e. fuzes actuated by mechanical contact between a stationary ammunition, e.g. a land mine, and a moving target, e.g. a person -- A contact fuze is a mechanical detonator that activates when a stationary munition such as a land mine is struck by a moving target, applying a predetermined force like tension or pressure. The impact causes a mechanical linkage to close an electrical or pyrotechnic circuit, triggering the explosive charge. This type belongs to the CPC subclass F42C 7/02 for fuzes actuated by direct mechanical contact.
[F42C 7/04] actuated by applying pressure on the ammunition head -- F42C 7/04 covers ammunition fuzes that are triggered by pressure applied directly to the head of the round, using a mechanical force to initiate detonation. The subclass groups designs where head-impact or compression deforms a component, activating the fuze.
[F42C 7/06] and comprising pneumatic or hydraulic retarding means -- The subclass F42C 7/06 covers ammunition fuzes that are triggered by a predetermined mechanical force such as tension, torsion or pressure and that incorporate pneumatic or hydraulic retarding means to delay or control the fuze action. It is a narrow category within mechanical-actuated fuzes for ammunition, specifying the use of gas- or fluid-based devices to modulate the timing or force of activation.
[F42C 7/08] of release type, i.e. actuated by releasing pressure from the ammunition head -- This subclass (F42C 7/08) covers release-type ammunition fuzes that are triggered by the sudden drop of pressure when the pressure chamber of the cartridge head is opened, rather than by direct tension, torsion or compression. The fuze activates as the stored pressure is released, initiating the ignition or detonation sequence.
[F42C 7/10] of antenna type -- This subclass covers ammunition fuzes that are triggered by a predetermined mechanical force such as tension, torsion or pressure and employ an antenna-type sensing element. The antenna element detects the applied force to initiate the fuze activation.
[F42C 7/12] Percussion fuzes of the double-action type, i.e. fuzes cocked and fired in a single movement, e.g. by pulling an incorporated percussion pin or hammer -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The percussion is initiated by a spring loaded percussion pin after the relative displacement of the two components of the fuze.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Impact fuzes -> F42C1/00 - Percussion caps -> F42C19/10
[F42C 9/00] Time fuzes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Non-electronic fuzes causing detonation of the ammunition after a predetermined time from the initiation of the fuze itself, i.e. the timing is not caused by an electric or electronic circuitry.  Timing can be caused by clockwork or a burning pyrotechnic unit.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Electric time fuzes, the time dely being caused by electric circuitry -> F42C11/06
[F42C 9/02] the timing being caused by mechanical means -- F42C 9/02 covers time fuzes in ammunition where the delay is generated by purely mechanical mechanisms such as springs, gears or clockwork devices. These devices control when a projectile initiates its payload without electronic or chemical timing.
[F42C 9/04] by spring motor -- F42C 9/04 covers time fuzes that are actuated by a spring motor, where stored mechanical energy from a wound spring drives the timing mechanism after ignition. The spring releases at a preset interval to trigger the fuze, providing a reliable, self-contained delay without external power.
[F42C 9/041] the clockwork activating a security device, e.g. for unlocking the firing-pin -- The code F42C 9/041 refers to clockwork mechanisms that release a security device, such as unlocking a firing-pin, in time-fuzed ammunition. It covers the mechanical timing components that trigger the activation of the fuze after a preset interval.
[F42C 9/043] and the firing-pin being activated by impact -- The CPC subclass F42C 9/043 covers time fuzes in which the firing-pin is set off by the impact of a moving part, such as a projectile or internal component, rather than by a separate mechanical trigger. This mechanism links the timing element directly to the physical shock that initiates the fuze's detonation sequence.
[F42C 9/045] and the firing-pin being activated by a spring -- F42C 9/045 covers time-based ammunition fuzes in which the firing-pin is released by a spring mechanism after a set interval. The subclass addresses designs where spring tension is stored and then used to drive the pin into the detonator, providing reliable ignition timing for projectiles.
[F42C 9/046] and the activating spring being the spring of the clock-work mechanism -- The CPC entry F42C 9/046 covers time fuzes that use the spring of a clock-work mechanism as the activating spring, providing the energy to trigger the fuze after a set interval. This design integrates the timing spring directly into the fuze's activation system, linking the clockwork's stored energy to the detonation sequence.
[F42C 9/048] Unlocking of clockwork mechanisms, e.g. by inertia or centrifugal forces; Means for disconnecting the clockwork mechanism from the setting mechanism -- In CPC class F42C 9/048, the subject is mechanisms that release or disengage a clockwork fuze by inertial or centrifugal action, separating the winding gear from the setting gear. The entry covers unlocking devices used in time fuzes for ammunition.
[F42C 9/06] by flow of fluent material, e.g. shot, fluids -- F42C 9/06 covers time-fuzing mechanisms in ammunition that generate a delay by the flow of a fluent material such as shot or liquids, using the movement of the material to trigger ignition after a prescribed interval. This sub-class falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition, ammunition fuzes and time fuzes.
[F42C 9/08] the timing being caused by chemical action, e.g. of acids -- F42C 9/08 covers chemical-driven time fuzes for ammunition, where the delay before detonation is produced by a chemical reaction such as acid corrosion of a restraining element. It pertains to fuzes that rely on controlled chemical action to achieve a preset timing interval.
[F42C 9/10] the timing being caused by combustion -- F42C 9/10 covers time fuzes in which the delay interval is produced by a combustion process, such as the controlled burn of a pyrotechnic composition or propellant that determines when the fuze triggers the explosive charge.
[F42C 9/12] with ring combustion elements -- F42C 9/12 defines time fuzes that employ ring-shaped combustion elements, such as pyrotechnic or explosive rings, to generate the delay before initiation. These ring components burn or react in a controlled manner, providing a predictable timing interval for the detonation of ammunition. This subclass falls under Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Ammunition fuzes → Time fuzes.
[F42C 9/14] Double fuzes -- F42C 9/14 covers ammunition that incorporates two time fuzes in a single projectile. A double-fuze arrangement provides simultaneous or sequential initiation of the charge, enhancing reliability, safety, or allowing multiple detonation times. It is employed in artillery shells and similar munitions where precise timing is critical.
[F42C 9/141] Impact fuze in combination with a clockwork time fuze -- The CPC subclass F42C 9/141 pertains to impact fuzes that are integrated with a clockwork time fuze, combining mechanical activation on impact with a timed delay. It falls within mechanical engineering, specifically the ammunition fuzes and time-fuze categories.
[F42C 9/142] combined time and percussion fuzes in which the timing is caused by combustion -- F42C 9/142 designates combined time-and-percussion ammunition fuzes in which the delay period is produced by a controlled combustion reaction. These devices integrate a chemical timing element with a percussion initiation mechanism for synchronized detonation.
[F42C 9/144] with ring or spiral combustion elements -- The CPC subclass F42C 9/144 defines time fuzes for ammunition that use a ring- or spiral-shaped combustion element to control the delay before detonation, allowing the burn rate to be set by the geometry of the element. This design is employed in mechanical engineering of ammunition fuzes to achieve precise timing of the explosive charge.
[F42C 9/145] combined time and percussion fuzes in which the timing is caused by chemical reaction -- F42C 9/145 covers ammunition fuzes that combine a time delay with a percussion initiation, where the timing interval is generated by a chemical reaction, integrating both delayed and impact activation in a single device.
[F42C 9/147] Impact fuze in combination with electric time fuze -- A hybrid fuze that combines a mechanical impact initiation with an electric time-delay circuit, allowing a projectile to detonate on impact or after a preset interval. It is used in artillery and small-arms ammunition to provide flexible timing for target engagement.
[F42C 9/148] Proximity fuzes in combination with other fuzes -- Proximity fuzes that are integrated with one or more additional fuze types, such as time, impact or magnetic fuzes, to provide layered or redundant triggering of ammunition. The combination allows a projectile to detonate when it approaches a target while also meeting auxiliary conditions, enhancing reliability and effectiveness.
[F42C 9/16] for self-destruction of ammunition -- F42C 9/16 refers to ammunition fuzes that incorporate a self-destruction function, causing the round to neutralize itself after a set time delay. The feature is typically achieved by triggering an internal charge that renders the projectile harmless, and it falls under the broader category of time fuzes for ammunition.
[F42C 9/18] when the spin rate falls below a predetermined limit, e.g. a spring force being stronger than the locking action of a centrifugally-operated lock -- F42C 9/18 pertains to time-fuzed ammunition that is released when the projectile's spin rate falls below a predetermined limit, for example when a spring force exceeds the holding action of a centrifugally operated lock. The subclass addresses designs that use loss of rotational speed as a trigger for fuze activation.
[F42C 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups of this subclass -- F42C 99/00 is a CPC subclass for ammunition fuze technology that captures any subject matter not specifically covered by the other groups within the subclass. It serves as a catch-all for novel or unconventional fuze designs, materials, or functions that fall outside existing classifications.
[F42D] BLASTING -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This subclass covers devices and methods for blasting for both civilian and military applications. The documentation is also organised according to the particular blasting operations. Further it includes particular safety arrangements for blasting or detonations.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Fuses, e.g. fuse cords -> C06C5/00 - Blasting cartridges -> F42B3/00
[F42D 1/00] Blasting methods or apparatus, e.g. loading or tamping -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Devices and methods for blasting, including the arrangement of blasting cartridges as the smallest explosive unit into assemblies, pyrotechnic, electric and electronic ignition arrangements, in particular for the timed ignition of a multitude of single blasting units, and methods and apparatus for the tamping or loading of explosives. Further includes set-ups for breaching of doors or walls.
[F42D 1/02] Arranging blasting cartridges to form an assembly -- F42D 1/02 relates to methods and devices for arranging several blasting cartridges together to form a single assembly, such as linking, bundling or nesting them so they can be loaded, tamped or detonated as one unit, improving control over the timing and distribution of the explosion.
[F42D 1/04] Arrangements for ignition -- F42D 1/04 pertains to the arrangements for ignition used in blasting methods or apparatus, describing devices or systems that initiate explosive charges, including electrical, mechanical, or chemical ignition setups employed in ammunition, mining and related fields.
[F42D 1/041] Tools for adapting cartridges for the mounting of detonators  cartridges specially adapted for the mounting of detonators  F42B3/26
[F42D 1/042] Logic explosive circuits, e.g. with explosive diodes -- F42D 1/042 is a subclass of the Mechanical Engineering → Ammunition → Blasting group and relates to blasting methods or apparatus that use logic explosive circuits, such as explosive diodes, to control the initiation and sequencing of charges. This classification covers devices that integrate electronic-style logic functions directly into the explosive material.
[F42D 1/043] Connectors for detonating cords and ignition tubes, e.g. Nonel tubes  mounting of detonators in blasting cartridges  F42B3/26 -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Mounting of detonators in blasting cartridges -> F42B3/26
[F42D 1/045] Arrangements for electric ignition -- The subclass F42D 1/045 covers configurations and devices that provide electric initiation of explosive charges, including wiring, switches, and control circuitry used to ignite blasting materials in ammunition and mining applications.
[F42D 1/05] Electric circuits for blasting -- Electric circuit arrangements used to initiate blasting charges, including wiring, power sources, firing devices, control panels and safety interlocks. The entry covers designs that supply, regulate or distribute electric energy to detonators or blasting caps for controlled explosive discharge.
[F42D 1/055] specially adapted for firing multiple charges with a time delay -- This subclass covers devices or systems designed to fire several explosive charges sequentially with a programmed time interval, allowing controlled, delayed detonation of multiple loads. It includes apparatus that loads, tampes and times the charges for coordinated blasting operations.
[F42D 1/06] Relative timing of multiple charges -- The entry covers methods for controlling the relative timing of two or more explosive charges in a blast, including sequential, simultaneous or delayed detonation using devices such as delay pins, electronic timers or firing circuits to achieve desired fragmentation, vibration control or safety outcomes.
[F42D 1/08] Tamping methods -- The CPC subclass F42D 1/08 covers methods and devices for tamping, the process of compacting or compressing explosive charges in blasting operations. It includes mechanical, hydraulic or pneumatic systems that apply pressure to loaded boreholes to improve charge density and control detonation. The subclass falls under mechanical engineering - ammunition - blasting.
[F42D 1/10] Feeding explosives in granular or slurry form -- F42D 1/10 classifies methods and apparatus for supplying explosives that are in granular or slurry form to a blast site, covering loading, conveying, or feeding equipment designed to handle such material during blasting operations. It pertains to the preparation stage of ammunition in mechanical engineering.
[F42D 1/12] Feeding tamping material by pneumatic or hydraulic pressure -- The code F42D 1/12 covers systems that deliver tamping material into a borehole using air or fluid pressure, typically to compact explosives during blasting operations. It includes pneumatic or hydraulic feeding devices that automate loading and tamping, improving safety and efficiency in mining or demolition.
[F42D 1/14] Hand-operated tamping or loading -- The class F42D 1/14 covers hand-operated tools for tamping or loading explosive charges in blasting operations. It includes manually powered devices that compact material in boreholes or insert charge carriers, intended for use where powered equipment is unavailable or impractical.
[F42D 1/16] Tamping tools -- F42D 1/16 covers tools and devices used to compact or press explosive charges in boreholes during blasting operations. These tamping tools, such as rods, pistons or mechanical tampers, ensure proper charge placement, improve energy transfer and enhance safety and efficiency of the blasting process.
[F42D 1/18] Plugs for boreholes -- F42D 1/18 covers devices used to seal boreholes in blasting operations. The plugs prevent premature gas escape, protect the charge, and can be made of various materials such as wood, metal, or plastic, sometimes oriented for controlled detonation.
[F42D 1/20] Tamping cartridges, i.e. cartridges containing tamping material -- Tamping cartridges are containers filled with material such as sand, gravel or polymer beads that are placed in a borehole after loading explosive charges to improve the packing and density of the charge. By providing consistent tamping pressure, they help ensure reliable detonation, reduce misfires and control the energy release during blasting operations.
[F42D 1/22] Methods for holding or positioning for blasting cartridges or tamping cartridges -- It covers techniques and devices that secure or align blasting or tamping cartridges during loading, ensuring correct orientation and stability before ignition. These methods are employed in artillery, demolition and mining operations to improve safety and effectiveness.
[F42D 1/24] characterised by the tamping material -- F42D 1/24 is a CPC subclass for blasting methods or apparatus where the tamping material used to compact the explosive charge is a defining characteristic, focusing on the type, composition, or behavior of the material employed to fill the space around the charge.
[F42D 1/26] Tamping with foaming agents -- F42D 1/26 covers techniques for compacting or tamping explosive loads by applying a foaming agent that expands to fill voids and provide a seal, enhancing blast efficiency and safety. The method may involve mixing foam-forming chemicals with water or other liquids and introducing the mixture into the borehole before detonation.
[F42D 1/28] Tamping with gelling agents -- The subclass F42D 1/28 covers blasting tamping techniques that employ gelling agents to bind or thicken the tamping material. It includes methods and apparatus where gels improve compaction, reduce dust and enhance the stability of the charge during loading.
[F42D 3/00] Particular applications of blasting techniques -- The code F42D 3/00 addresses particular applications of blasting techniques, including shaping, cutting, or cleaning metal parts, detonating charges in ammunition production, and using explosive energy for construction or demolition. It is situated within the mechanical-engineering branch of the ammunition-blasting hierarchy.
[F42D 3/02] for demolition of tall structures, e.g. chimney stacks -- A subclass of the CPC covering blasting techniques applied to the demolition of tall structures such as chimney stacks, detailing specific methods, charge configurations and safety measures for dismantling high-rise masonry or steel components. It falls under mechanical engineering, ammunition and blasting categories, focusing on practical demolition applications.
[F42D 3/04] for rock blasting -- The CPC entry F42D 3/04 falls under section F (Mechanical engineering), class 42 (Ammunition; blasting), subclass D (Particular applications of blasting techniques) and designates inventions relating to rock blasting. It covers methods, apparatuses and procedures for fragmenting or excavating rock, such as drilling, charge placement, initiation and control of explosive charges in mining, quarrying, tunnel construction and other civil-engineering contexts.
[F42D 3/06] for seismic purposes -- F42D 3/06 pertains to the use of controlled explosions to produce seismic waves for exploration, monitoring or geophysical surveying. It includes methods and devices that generate, modulate or detect such waves, typically for locating subsurface structures, assessing geological formations or evaluating underground resources. This subclass falls under particular applications of blasting techniques in mechanical engineering.
[F42D 5/00] Safety arrangements -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods and devices for increasing the safety of blasting operation, e.g. during blasting operation by providing a physical detonation wave absorbing shield, or the identification, neutralisation and removal of explosives in cases where the explosive did not detonate (abort of operation, malfunction/dud or decommissioning).
[F42D 5/02] Locating undetonated charges -- The F42D 5/02 class covers methods, devices and systems for detecting and locating undetonated explosive charges, including sensors, remote-inspection techniques and probing tools used to identify buried or concealed ordnance. It addresses safety arrangements for handling, mapping and clearance of unexploded munitions in military and civilian contexts.
[F42D 5/04] Rendering explosive charges harmless, e.g. destroying ammunition -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Fitting or extracting primers in or from fuzes or charges -> F42B33/04 - Dismantling fuzes, cartridges, projectiles, missiles, rockets or bombs -> F42B33/06 - Explosion or fire protection arrangements on packages or ammunition -> F42B39/14 - Packages or ammunition having valves for pressure-equalising; Packages or ammunition having plugs for pressure release, e.g. meltable -> F42B39/20
[F42D 5/045] Detonation-wave absorbing or damping means -- **Definition:** This place covers:  This group includes all means to avoid the propagation of the detonation or blast wave during the destruction of ammunition by controlled detonation in a pressure chamber which is able to withstand a detonation inside. Also includes detonation wave guiding means.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Dismantling fuzes, cartridges, projectiles, missiles, rockets or bombs by combustion -> F42B33/067
[F42D 5/05] Blasting mats -- F42D 5/05 covers blasting mats, protective barriers placed around or over a blast site to contain fragments, reduce over-pressure, and safeguard personnel and equipment. These mats are usually made of woven fabric, rubber or other shock-absorbing materials and are employed in mining, demolition and construction blasting operations. The entry falls under safety arrangements within the ammunition and blasting sections of mechanical engineering.
[F42D 5/055] Silencing means for blasting operations -- This subclass covers devices or methods that reduce the noise produced during blasting, such as sound-absorbing liners, mufflers, or barrier systems incorporated into explosive charges or equipment. It includes designs intended to protect personnel and the environment from the acoustic impact of blasting operations.
[F42D 5/06] Unloading boreholes -- The F42D 5/06 entry covers safety arrangements for unloading boreholes after a blasting operation. It includes methods and devices that safely remove explosive residues, gases or pressure from drilled holes to prevent accidental ignition and protect personnel and equipment.
[F42D 99/00] Subject matter not provided for in other groups in this subclass -- F42D 99/00 is a residual category within the blasting subclass of the ammunition group of mechanical engineering. It covers any blasting-related inventions that are not specifically covered by the other defined groups in the subclass.
